{{short description|Impact of coronavirus}}
{{Use dmy dates|date=December 2020}}
{{COVID-19 pandemic sidebar|expanded=issues}}
The [[COVID-19 pandemic]] has caused the most significant disruption<ref name="auto2">{{Cite journal|last1=Ying-Ying Wong|first1=Ashley|last2=Ka-Kin Ling|first2=Samuel|last3=Louie|first3=Lobo|last4=Ying-Kan Law|first4=George|last5=Chi-Hung So|first5=Raymond|last6=Chi-Wo Lee|first6=Daniel|last7=Chung-Fai Yau|first7=Forrest|last8=Shu-Hang Yung|first8=Patrick|date=28 July 2020|title=Impact of the COVID-19 pandemic on sports and exercise|url=http://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S2214687320300674|journal=Asia-Pacific Journal of Sports Medicine, Arthroscopy, Rehabilitation and Technology|volume=22|pages=39–44|language=en|doi=10.1016/j.asmart.2020.07.006|pmid=32821648|issn=2214-6873|pmc=7386263}}</ref> to the [[2020 in sports|worldwide sporting calendar]] since [[World War II]]. Across the world and to varying degrees, sports events have been cancelled or postponed.<ref name="BBC overview">{{cite web |title=Coronavirus: How the virus has impacted sporting events around the world |url=https://www.bbc.com/sport/51605235 |website=BBC |date=12 March 2020 |accessdate=12 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |last1= |first1= |title=How the coronavirus is affecting sports leagues and events |url=https://www.latimes.com/sports/story/2020-03-09/coronavirus-latest-news-sports-world |website=Los Angeles Times |date=12 March 2020 |accessdate=12 March 2020}}</ref><ref name=":13">{{Cite journal|last1=Cooper|first1=J. A.|last2=Alderman|first2=Derek H.|date=26 May 2020|title=Cancelling March Madness exposes opportunities for a more sustainable sports tourism economy|journal=Tourism Geographies|volume=22|issue=3|pages=525–535|doi=10.1080/14616688.2020.1759135|s2cid=219462858|issn=1461-6688}}</ref> The [[2020 Summer Olympics]] in Tokyo were rescheduled to 2021.<ref name="auto2"/> Spectators have no games to watch and players no games to play.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Fitzsimmons |first=Caitlin |url=https://www.smh.com.au/lifestyle/health-and-wellness/craig-foster-rallying-sport-to-play-for-lives-in-volunteer-response-20200404-p54h0t.html |title=Craig Foster rallying sport to 'play for lives' in volunteer response |date=5 April 2020 |work=The Sydney Morning Herald|access-date=5 April 2020}}</ref> Only a few countries and territories, such as [[Hong Kong]],<ref name="auto2"/> [[Turkmenistan]],<ref>{{Cite web |url=https://turkmenportal.com/blog/27032/binagar-lidiruet-v-chempionate-turkmenistana-po-basketbolu |title="Бинагар" лидирует в чемпионате Туркменистана по баскетболу |access-date=23 April 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200502164823/https://turkmenportal.com/blog/27032/binagar-lidiruet-v-chempionate-turkmenistana-po-basketbolu |archive-date=2 May 2020 |url-status=dead }}</ref> [[Belarus]], and [[Nicaragua]], have continued professional sporting matches as planned.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Wagner |first1=James |title=Looking for a Full Sports Calendar? Try Nicaragua |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2020/04/14/sports/coronavirus-nicaragua-sports-events.html |accessdate=16 April 2020 |work=The New York Times |date=14 April 2020}}</ref>

==International multi-sport events==
===Summer Olympics===
The [[2020 Summer Olympics]] and [[2020 Summer Paralympics|Paralympics]] were scheduled to take place in [[Tokyo]] starting 24 July. Although the Japanese government had taken extra precautions to help minimize the [[COVID-19 pandemic in Japan|outbreak's impact in the country]],<ref name="auto1">{{cite web |url=https://abcnews.go.com/Sports/wireStory/abe-brushes-worries-virus-impact-tokyo-olympics-68719487 |title=Abe brushes aside worries of virus impact on Tokyo Olympics |publisher=ABC News}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/feb/01/tokyo-2020-organisers-fight-false-rumours-olympics-cancelled-over-coronavirus-crisis |title=Tokyo 2020 organisers fight false rumours Olympics cancelled over coronavirus crisis |first=Justin |last=McCurry |date=1 February 2020 |work=The Guardian}}</ref> qualifying events were being canceled or postponed almost daily. "And the Games themselves are expected to draw 600,000 foreign visitors from nearly every country. According to Japanese public broadcaster [[NHK]], Tokyo 2020 organizing-committee chief executive Toshiro Muto voiced concerns on 5 February, that COVID-19 might "throw cold water on the momentum toward the Games."<ref>Campbell, C., Gregory, S., & Shibata, M. (2020). The Olympics-Size Risk of COVID-19. TIME Magazine, 195(7/8), 15–16.</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.sltrib.com/sports/2020/03/10/coronavirus-already/ |title=Coronavirus already causing Olympic chaos at qualifying events |first=Ellingworth |last=Ellingworth |accessdate=13 March 2020 |work=The Salt Lake Tribune}}</ref>

The traditional [[Olympic flame]] lighting ceremony in [[Olympia, Greece]], to mark the start of the [[2020 Summer Olympics torch relay]] was held on 12 March without spectators.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-olympics-2020-flame/tokyo-2020-torch-lit-behind-closed-doors-in-ancient-olympia-idUSKBN20Z1EO |title=Tokyo 2020 torch lit behind closed doors in ancient Olympia |website=Reuters |accessdate=15 March 2020 |date=12 March 2020}}</ref> On 23 March, Canada, Australia, and Great Britain announced that they would withdraw from the Games unless they are postponed for one year.<ref>{{Cite web|title=Canada, Australia withdraw from Tokyo 2020 as organizers ponder postponement|url=https://www.cnbc.com/2020/03/23/olympics-canada-australia-withdraw-from-tokyo-2020.html|date=23 March 2020|website=CNBC|language=en|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200323112916/https://www.cnbc.com/2020/03/23/olympics-canada-australia-withdraw-from-tokyo-2020.html|archive-date=23 March 2020|access-date=23 March 2020}}</ref> On 24 March 2020, the IOC and Tokyo Organizing Committee announced that the 2020 Summer Olympics and Paralympics would be "rescheduled to a date beyond 2020 but not later than summer 2021", marking the first time in the history of the modern Olympics that an Olympiad has been postponed.<ref>{{cite web|title=Tokyo 2020: Olympic Games organisers 'agree postponement'|url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/sport/olympics/52020134|date=24 March 2020|work=[[BBC Sport]]|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200324124243/https://www.bbc.co.uk/sport/olympics/52020134|archive-date=24 March 2020|accessdate=24 March 2020}}</ref><ref name="Postponement">{{Cite web|title=Tokyo Olympics postponed to 2021 due to coronavirus pandemic|url=https://www.theguardian.com/sport/2020/mar/24/tokyo-olympics-to-be-postponed-to-2021-due-to-coronavirus-pandemic|last1=McCurry|first1=Justin|last2=Ingle|first2=Sean|date=24 March 2020|work=[[The Guardian]]|language=en-GB|issn=0261-3077|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200324123239/https://www.theguardian.com/sport/2020/mar/24/tokyo-olympics-to-be-postponed-to-2021-due-to-coronavirus-pandemic|archive-date=24 March 2020|access-date=24 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|title=Olympics history: Have the Games been postponed before?|url=https://www.latimes.com/sports/olympics/story/2020-03-24/olympics-history-tokyo-games-postponed|date=24 March 2020|website=Los Angeles Times|language=en-US|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200324211447/https://www.latimes.com/sports/olympics/story/2020-03-24/olympics-history-tokyo-games-postponed|archive-date=24 March 2020|access-date=25 March 2020}}</ref> The opening ceremonies of the Games were officially rescheduled to 23 July 2021.<ref>{{cite web|title=Rescheduled Tokyo 2020 Olympics to open on July 23 in 2021|url=https://www.insidethegames.biz/articles/1092594/postponed-tokyo-olympics-july-23-opening|last=Pavitt|first=Michael|date=20 March 2020|website=insidethegames.biz|access-date=20 March 2020}}</ref>

On 29 April 2020, Prime Minister [[Shinzo Abe]] warned that the Games "must be held in a way that shows the world has won its battle against the coronavirus pandemic".<ref>{{Cite news|last=Ingle|first=Sean|date=29 April 2020|title=Tokyo Olympics in 2021 at risk of cancellation admits Japan's PM|language=en-GB|work=The Guardian|url=https://www.theguardian.com/sport/2020/apr/29/tokyo-olympics-not-reliant-on-covid-19-vaccine-senior-ioc-member|access-date=4 May 2020|issn=0261-3077}}</ref> He also says that if a vaccine is not found, the Olympics will be canceled completely.

=== Winter Olympics ===
Although the next Winter Olympics are not until [[2022 Winter Olympics|2023]] (hosted by Beijing, China), the pandemic has already impacted qualifying in specific sports such as [[Curling at the 2022 Winter Olympics|curling]]—where the [[World Curling Federation]] announced a proposal to have qualification be dependent on performance in the 2021 world championships (whose top teams will automatically qualify) and a final qualification tournament, as opposed to the previous plan of having qualification determined by both the 2020 and 2021 world championships.<ref>{{Cite web|title=Curling wants 2021 world championships to determine qualifying for Beijing Olympics|url=https://www.cbc.ca/sports/olympics/winter/curling/world-curling-olympic-qualification-1.5527737|last=|first=|date=9 April 2020|website=CBC Sports|access-date=4 May 2020}}</ref> Qualification for the [[Ice hockey at the 2022 Winter Olympics|women's hockey tournament]] was to be determined by [[IIHF World Ranking]]s after the [[2020 IIHF Women's World Championship|2020 Women's World Championship]]. As the tournament was cancelled, the existing rankings going into the tournament were used instead.<ref>{{Cite web|title=U.S., Canada in same 2022 Olympic hockey group|url=https://nhl.nbcsports.com/2020/04/24/u-s-canada-men-women-in-same-groups-for-2022-olympics/|last=|first=|date=24 April 2020|website=NBC Sports|language=en-US|access-date=4 May 2020}}</ref> The opening ceremonies of the Games were officially rescheduled to 3 February 2023.

===World Games===
The [[World Games]] in [[Birmingham, Alabama|Birmingham]], [[Alabama]], were scheduled for July 2021, but because of the rescheduling of the [[2020 Summer Olympics]], the [[2022 World Games|eleventh World Games]] will be held in July 2022 instead.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://swimswam.com/2021-world-games-postponed-to-2022-to-accommodate-olympic-move/|title=2021 WORLD GAMES POSTPONED TO 2022 TO ACCOMMODATE OLYMPIC MOVE|website=SwimSwam|access-date=2 April 2020}}</ref>

===Arctic Winter Games===
The [[2020 Arctic Winter Games]] were canceled.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.cbc.ca/news/canada/north/arctic-winter-games-cancelled-coronavirus-1.5490055 |title='Shocked and disappointed': Arctic Winter Games cancelled due to coronavirus concerns &#124; CBC News}}</ref>

===ASEAN Para Games===
The [[2020 ASEAN Para Games]] were cancelled.<ref>{{cite news |title=2020 ASEAN Para Games officially canceled |url=https://www.thejakartapost.com/news/2020/05/09/2020-asean-para-games-officially-canceled.html |accessdate=10 May 2020 |work=The Jakarta Post |date=9 May 2020}}</ref>

===Summer World University Games===
The [[2021 Summer World University Games]] were postponed for ten days by the rescheduling of the Summer Olympics.
===World Masters Games===
* The [[World Masters Games|2021 World Masters Games]], original schedule held in [[Osaka Prefecture]], [[Nara Prefecture]], [[Kyoto Prefecture]], [[Hyogo Prefecture]], [[Shiga Prefecture]] and [[Wakayama Prefecture]] on 14 to 30 May, that indefinite postponed after 2022, the organisation announced on 28 October.{{citation needed|date=November 2020}}

==National amateur multi-sport governing-body competitions==
=== Canada ===
[[U Sports]] curtailed its men's and women's ice hockey championships on 12 March 2020. On 8 June, U Sports announced that it had cancelled all national championships for the fall semester of the 2020–21 academic year, including [[Canadian football|football]]{{efn|name=Football_definition|In [[North American English]], the word "football" almost always refers to [[American football]] and [[Canadian football]] (known as [[gridiron football]]); [[association football]] is called "[[Names for association football|soccer]]".}} (the first time the [[Vanier Cup]] will not be contested since its inception), [[Cross country running|cross-country]], field hockey, women's rugby, and soccer.<ref name=":17">{{Cite web|last=|first=|date=8 June 2020|title=Vanier Cup among national U Sports championships cancelled because of COVID-19 pandemic|url=https://www.cbc.ca/sports/usports-cancel-fall-season-1.5602556|access-date=8 June 2020|website=CBC Sports}}</ref>  On 15 October 2020, U Sports announced it would do the same thing for the winter 2021 portion of the 2020-21, once again cancelling all winter national championships as well.  [[Atlantic University Sport]], [[Canada West Universities Athletic Association|Canada West]], and [[Ontario University Athletics]] followed suit, suspending all university athletics programs initially through to 31 December 2020, but was later extended through to 31 March 2021, as announced on 15 October 2020.<ref>{{Cite web|last=Ethier|first=Matt|date=9 June 2020|title=How the OUA's decision to cancel the 2020 season will impact athletic scholarships|url=https://kitchener.ctvnews.ca/how-the-oua-s-decision-to-cancel-the-2020-season-will-impact-athletic-scholarships-1.4977342|access-date=10 June 2020|website=CTV News Kitchener|language=en}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|date=8 June 2020|title=Canada West cancels fall sports due to COVID-19|url=https://www.nelsonstar.com/sports/canada-west-cancels-fall-sports-due-to-covid-19/|access-date=8 June 2020|website=Nelson Star|language=en-US}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|last=Sawatzky|first=Mike|date=11 May 2020|title=U Sports revamps schedules|language=en-CA|work=Winnipeg Free Press|url=https://www.winnipegfreepress.com/sports/amateur/u-sports-revamps-schedules-570390642.html|access-date=8 June 2020}}</ref><ref name=":18">{{Cite web|title=Atlantic University Sport suspends all competition until January 2021|url=https://globalnews.ca/news/7038366/atlantic-university-sport-suspended/|access-date=8 June 2020|website=Global News|language=en}}</ref> <ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.sportsnet.ca/usports/article/u-sports-cancels-2021-winter-national-championships/|title=U Sports cancels 2021 winter national championships - Sportsnet.ca|website=www.sportsnet.ca}}</ref>

===Ireland===
{{Main|Impact of the COVID-19 pandemic on sports in the Republic of Ireland}}
The [[COVID-19 pandemic in the Republic of Ireland]] has had a significant impact on the conduct of sports affecting both competitive sports leagues and tournaments and recreational sports. The [[Gaelic games]] of [[Gaelic football|football]], [[hurling]], [[camogie]], and [[ladies' Gaelic football|ladies' football]]—mostly played in [[Ireland]]—saw all competitions suspended from 12 March 2020. The [[2020 National Hurling League|National Hurling League]], [[2020 National Football League (Ireland)|National Football League]], [[2020 National Camogie League|National Camogie League]] and [[2020 Ladies' National Football League|Ladies' National Football League]] were suspended, with competitions not intended to resume until 29 March at the earliest.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.gaa.ie/news-archive/news/gaa-camogie-association-and-the-lgfa-suspend-all-activity/ |title=GAA, Camogie Association, and the LGFA suspend all activity |website=www.gaa.ie}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.balls.ie/gaa/gaa-camogie-association-gaa-suspend-activities-march-29th-427885 |title=GAA, Camogie Association And LGFA Suspend All Activity Until March 29th |first=P. J. |last=Browne |website=Balls.ie}}</ref> On 17 March, the [[Gaelic Athletic Association]] (GAA) confirmed that [[2020 Connacht Senior Football Championship|the opening fixture]] of the [[2020 All-Ireland Senior Football Championship]]—due to have taken place at [[Gaelic Park]] in [[Riverdale, Bronx|The Bronx]] on 3 May—had been postponed.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.irishexaminer.com/breakingnews/sport/gaa/galway-and-new-york-clash-first-major-casualty-of-pandemic-988773.html |title=Galway and New York clash first major casualty of pandemic |work=[[Irish Examiner]] |first=Eoghan |last=Cormican |date=18 March 2020 |accessdate=22 March 2020}}</ref>

On 26 June, the [[Gaelic Athletic Association]] (GAA) announced that all GAA competitions would commence in October 2020, with the hurling and football competitions to be an all-knockout competition. As from 12 September, [[London]] withdrew from the championship and from 3 November, [[Sligo]] withdrew from the [[Connacht]] football championship.

=== Philippines ===
In the Philippines, [[NCAA Season 95]] and [[UAAP Season 82]] were both indefinitely suspended.<ref name=philippinencaa>{{cite news |last1=Villar |first1=Joey |title=NCAA succumbs to coronavirus scare, postpones all high school games |url=https://www.philstar.com/sports/2020/02/07/1991189/ncaa-succumbs-coronavirus-scare-postpones-all-high-school-games |accessdate=7 February 2020 |work=The Philippine Star |date=7 February 2020}}</ref><ref name="pba" /> NCAA Season 95 was terminated on 19 March after the [[2020 Luzon enhanced community quarantine|then community quarantine in Luzon]] was upgraded to an "enhanced community quarantine", in effect a lockdown.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.rappler.com/sports/university/ncaa/255125-season-95-terminated-coronavirus-luzon-lockdown|title=NCAA Season 95 terminated|last=Go|first=Beatrice|website=Rappler|language=en|access-date=24 March 2020}}</ref> UAAP Season 82 was canceled on 7 April, after the enhanced community quarantine was extended to 30 April.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.cnnphilippines.com/sports/2020/4/7/uaap-cancels-season-82-covid-pandemic.html|title=UAAP board cancels Season 82 due to COVID-19 pandemic|website=cnn|language=en|access-date=7 April 2020}}</ref>

On 1 May, the [[Cebu Schools Athletic Foundation, Inc.]] (CESAFI) have decided to cancel their 2020 season.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://cebudailynews.inquirer.net/306772/cesafi-cancels-2020-season-due-to-covid-19-threat|title=Cesafi cancels 2020 season due to COVID-19 threat|website=cebudailynews.inquirer.net|language=en|access-date=3 May 2020}}</ref>

===United Kingdom===
On 16 March 2020, [[British Universities and Colleges Sport]], the UK organisation for university sport, announced that all fixtures from 17 March to 1 April would not take place. Some individual events, like the [[orienteering]] and [[windsurfing]] championships were canceled entirely, while others were postponed indefinitely.<ref name="BUCS Cancellations">{{cite web |url=https://www.bucs.org.uk/update-covid-19-coronavirus.html |title=BUCS Statement regarding CoVid-19 |publisher=BUCS |date=16 March 2020 |accessdate=17 March 2020}}</ref>

===United States===
On 11 March 2020, the [[National Collegiate Athletic Association]] (NCAA) — the main U.S.A sanctioning body for [[College athletics in the United States|college athletics]] — initially announced that its winter-semester championships and tournaments, including its popular [[2020 NCAA Division I Men's Basketball Tournament|"March Madness" men's basketball tournament]], would be conducted behind closed doors with "only essential staff and limited family attendance".<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.usatoday.com/story/sports/ncaab/2020/03/11/ncaa-tournament-fans-banned-due-to-coronavirus-concerns/5024027002/ |title=NCAA men's and women's basketball tournaments will not include fans due to coronavirus concerns |first=Tom |last=Schad |newspaper=USA Today |date=11 March 2020|access-date=11 March 2020}}</ref>

The following day, in respect of the suspension of the [[NBA]] season and other professional sports leagues, the NCAA announced that all remaining championship events for the 2019–20 academic year would be canceled entirely, resulting in the first cancellation in the 81-year history of the [[NCAA basketball]] tournament.<ref name="NCAA cancellations">{{cite press release |url=https://www.ncaa.org/about/resources/media-center/news/ncaa-cancels-remaining-winter-and-spring-championships |title=NCAA cancels remaining winter and spring championships |publisher=NCAA |date=12 March 2020 |accessdate=12 March 2020}}</ref> This created a ''de facto'' [[mythical national championship]] situation.<ref>{{cite web|title=Kansas has best claim to the national championship after NCAA tournament cancellation|url=https://ftw.usatoday.com/2020/03/kansas-coronavirus-march-madness-ncaa-tournament-champion-claim-canceled|last1=Joseph|first1=Andrew|website=USA Today|publisher=Gannett|accessdate=22 April 2020|ref=USATS}}</ref> Other American multi-sports organizations—the [[National Association of Intercollegiate Athletics]] (NAIA),<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.naia.org/general/2019-20/releases/spring-sports-cancelled|title=NAIA Cancels Spring 2020 Sports Season|date=16 March 2020|website=NAIA}}</ref> [[National Junior College Athletic Association]] (NJCAA),<ref>{{cite web|url=https://njcaa.org/general/2019-20/releases/20200316k2au00|title=NJCAA COVID-19 update - spring sports season cancelled|date=16 March 2020|website=NJCAA}}</ref> and [[California Community College Athletic Association]] (CCCAA)<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.cccaasports.org/coronavirus/spring_sports_cancellation|title=CCCAA cancels spring sports, restores seasons of competition for student-athletes and announces recruiting ban|date=19 March 2020|website=CCCAA}}</ref>—also canceled their seasons. Additionally the Community College level sports governing bodies restored the season of eligibility to athletes who had already participated in the 2020 spring season.

On 12 May 2020, because the [[California State University]] system announced that in-person classes would remain suspended through the fall 2020 semester, the [[California Collegiate Athletic Association]] (CCAA)—a 12-member [[NCAA Division II]] conference consisting entirely of CSU campuses{{efn|At the time of announcement, 13 schools were CCAA members, but the only  one of these schools that was not a CSU campus, [[UC San Diego Tritons|UC San Diego]], joined the [[NCAA Division I|Division I]] [[Big West Conference]] on 1 July 2020.<ref>{{cite press release|url=http://www.bigwest.org//story.asp?story_id=20127 |title=CSU Bakersfield, UC San Diego to Join Big West Conference |publisher=Big West Conference |date=27 November 2017 |accessdate=11 December 2017}}</ref>}}—announced that it would also suspend its fall athletics season.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.espn.com/college-sports/story/_/id/29168107/california-state-university-stay-online-leaving-fall-sports-air |title=California State University system to stay online, leaving fall sports up in air |first=Kyle |last=Bonagura |website=ESPN.com |date=12 May 2020 |accessdate=18 May 2020}}</ref>

The [[Patriot League]], an [[NCAA Division I]] conference that competes in the second level of D1 Football,{{efn|name=Football_definition}} the [[NCAA Division I#Football Championship Subdivision|Football Championship Subdivision]] (FCS), initially announced on 22 June that while it would hold its fall sports seasons, its teams would not fly to any competitions, and overnight travel would only be allowed on a case-by-case basis.<ref>{{cite press release|url=https://patriotleague.org/news/2020/6/22/general-patriot-league-council-of-presidents-announces-guidance-regarding-2020-fall-competition.aspx |title=Patriot League Council of Presidents Announces Guidance Regarding 2020 Fall Competition |publisher=Patriot League |date=22 June 2020 |accessdate=23 June 2020}}</ref> Another FCS conference, the [[Ivy League]], announced on 8 July that it was canceling all fall sports, and that winter sports (whose seasons normally begin during the fall academic term) would not begin play until after the end of the fall term. It left open the possibility of shifting its fall sports, including football, to the spring.<ref>{{cite press release|url=https://ivyleague.com/news/2020/7/8/general-ivy-league-outlines-intercollegiate-athletics-plans-no-competition-in-fall-semester.aspx |title=Ivy League Outlines Intercollegiate Athletics Plans; No Competition in Fall Semester |publisher=Ivy League |date=8 July 2020 |accessdate=8 July 2020}}</ref> The Patriot League would later cancel its fall sports season entirely on 13 July, but gave the two federally operated [[United States service academies|service academies]] among its membership, [[Army Black Knights|Army]] and [[Navy Midshipmen|Navy]], the option to play fall sports as they saw fit. While the academies are full members of the Patriot League, their football teams play outside the conference in the top-level [[NCAA Division I Football Bowl Subdivision|Football Bowl Subdivision]] (FBS).<ref>{{cite press release|url=https://patriotleague.org/news/2020/7/13/general-patriot-league-announces-decisions-surrounding-fall-sport-season.aspx |title=Patriot League Announces Decisions Surrounding Fall Sport Season |publisher=Patriot League |date=13 July 2020 |accessdate=13 July 2020}}</ref>

The days following the Ivy League's cancellation of fall sports saw two of the major [[Power Five conferences|"Power Five" conferences]] of FBS announce that if fall sports were played, only in-conference matchups would take place. The [[Big Ten Conference]] made this announcement on 9 July,<ref>{{cite press release|url=https://bigten.org/news/2020/7/9/big-ten-statement-on-2020-21-fall-season.aspx |title=Big Ten Statement on 2020–21 Fall Season |publisher=Big Ten Conference |date=9 July 2020 |accessdate=9 July 2020}}</ref> with the [[Pac-12 Conference]] doing the same the next day.<ref>{{cite press release|url=https://pac-12.com/article/2020/07/10/pac-12-ceo-group-announces-decision-schedule-conference-only-play-several-fall |title=Pac-12 CEO Group announces decision to schedule conference-only play for several Fall sports & to delay move toward mandatory athletics activities |publisher=Pac-12 Conference |date=10 July 2020 |accessdate=13 July 2020}}</ref> Both conferences later chose to hold abbreviated conference-only football seasons, with the Big Ten starting play on the weekend of 24 October<ref>{{cite press release|url=https://bigten.org/news/2020/9/16/the-big-ten-conference-adopts-stringent-medical-protocols-football-season-to-resume-october-23-24-2020.aspx |title=The Big Ten Conference Adopts Stringent Medical Protocols; Football Season to Resume October 23-24, 2020 |publisher=Big Ten Conference |date=16 September 2020 |accessdate=21 October 2020}}</ref> and the Pac-12 on the weekend of 7 November.<ref>{{cite press release|url=https://pac-12.com/article/2020/10/03/pac-12-announces-2020-football-schedule |title=Pac-12 announces 2020 football schedule |publisher=Pac-12 Conference |date=3 October 2020 |accessdate=21 October 2020}}</ref>

In August, the NCAA announced that the Division II and Division III Presidents Councils decided to cancel national championships in all fall sports.<ref>{{cite press release|url=http://www.ncaa.org/about/resources/media-center/news/dii-presidents-council-cancels-fall-2020-championships|title=DII Presidents Council cancels fall 2020 championships |publisher=NCAA |date=5 August 2020 |accessdate=14 December 2020}}</ref> <ref>{{cite press release|url=hhttp://www.ncaa.org/about/resources/media-center/news/division-iii-presidents-council-cancels-fall-championships|title=Division III Presidents Council cancels fall championships |publisher=NCAA |date=22 September 2020 |accessdate=14 December 2020}}</ref>

In September, it was announced that 2020 Division I championships administered by NCAA in fall sports (cross country, field hockey, football soccer, women’s volleyball and men’s water polo) would be rescheduled to spring 2021, and conducted with a 25% reduction in championship participants. Matches played in fall or spring would count toward qualification. The Football Bowl Subdivision was not included as it is not an NCAA-administered championship. <ref>{{cite press release|url=https://www.ncaa.com/news/ncaa/article/2020-09-16/ncaa-di-council-approves-moving-fall-championships-spring|title=DI Board of Directors approves plan for holding fall championships in spring |publisher=NCAA |date=22 September 2020 |accessdate=14 December 2020}}</ref>

In December, the NCAA announced that 2021 Division II championship events in winter and spring sports would also have a 25% overall reduction in participants (individual sports varied from 17-34% based on logistics) to mitigate costs of testing and health protocols, as well as lost income. <ref>{{cite press release|url=http://www.ncaa.org/about/resources/media-center/news/division-ii-reduces-bracket-field-sizes-2021-winter-and-spring-championships|title=Division II reduces bracket, field sizes for 2021 winter and spring championships |publisher=NCAA |date=22 September 2020 |accessdate=14 December 2020}}</ref>

====Long-term effects====

The financial fallout from the pandemic was specifically cited by the following schools in their decisions to drop certain sports programs:

*[[Alabama–Huntsville Chargers|University of Alabama in Huntsville]] (UAH) – Men's and women's tennis <ref>{{cite press release|url=https://uahchargers.com/news/2020/5/22/general-covid-19-forcing-uah-to-take-steps-for-more-budget-reductions.aspx | title= COVID-19 Forcing UAH to Take Steps for More Budget Reductions| publisher= UAH Athletics | date=22 May 2020| accessdate= 23 May 2020}}</ref>
* [[Appalachian State Mountaineers|Appalachian State University]] – Men's indoor track & field, [[Appalachian State Mountaineers men's soccer|men's soccer]], men's tennis<ref>{{cite press release|url=https://appstatesports.com/news/2020/5/26/app-state-athletics-announces-program-changes.aspx |title=App State Athletics Announces Program Changes |publisher=Appalachian State Mountaineers |date=26 May 2020 |accessdate=2 June 2020}}</ref>

Additionally, the [[Arkansas–Pine Bluff Golden Lions and Golden Lady Lions|University of Arkansas at Pine Bluff]] announced that it was "suspending" its men's and women's tennis teams for the 2020–21 school year, citing the pandemic, but did not officially eliminate the tennis program.<ref>{{cite press release|url=https://uapblionsroar.com/news/2020/6/11/mens-tennis-uapb-to-suspend-tennis-programs.aspx |title=UAPB to Suspend Tennis Programs |publisher=UAPB Golden Lions |date=11 June 2020 |accessdate=13 June 2020}}</ref>

UAH initially dropped [[Alabama–Huntsville Chargers men's ice hockey|men's ice hockey]] alongside both of its tennis teams, but a successful fundraising drive by alumni and team supporters led the school to reinstate hockey a week later.<ref>{{Cite web|date=29 May 2020|title=UAH announces hockey will return after private donations|url=https://www.al.com/news/2020/05/uah-announces-hockey-will-return-after-private-funds-raised-to-support-program.html|access-date=5 June 2020|website=[[Advance Publications|AL.com]] |language=en}}</ref> Similarly, [[Bowling Green Falcons|Bowling Green State University]] announced that it would drop its [[Bowling Green Falcons baseball|baseball team]],<ref>{{cite press release|url=https://bgsufalcons.com/news/2020/5/15/general-bgsu-announces-athletics-restructuring.aspx |title=BGSU Announces Athletics Restructuring |publisher=Bowling Green Falcons |date=15 May 2020 |accessdate=21 May 2020}}</ref> but also had a successful fundraising effort that led to the team being reinstated.<ref>{{Cite web|title=Bowling Green reinstates baseball program|url=https://www.toledoblade.com/sports/bgsu/2020/06/02/BGSU-reinstates-baseball-program/stories/20200602125|access-date=3 June 2020|website=Toledo Blade|language=en}}</ref> The University of Minnesota, which had announced plans to drop four men's sports effective in 2021–22, announced that one of these sports, namely outdoor track & field, would be spared discontinuation, pending a further review of the school's sports offerings in spring 2021.<ref name=MinnesotaSports/> The most extensive rollback of plans to drop sports came at the [[William & Mary Tribe|College of William & Mary]]. In early September 2020, W&M announced it would drop seven sports effective in 2021–22—men's and women's gymnastics, men's and women's swimming & diving, men's indoor and outdoor track & field, and women's volleyball.<ref>{{cite press release|url=https://tribeathletics.com/news/2020/9/3/general-open-letter-to-the-william-mary-community-and-to-all-who-support-william-mary-athletics.aspx |title=Open Letter to the William & Mary Community and to All Who Support William & Mary Athletics |publisher=William & Mary Tribe|date=3 September 2020 |accessdate=7 September 2020}}</ref> The fallout from this move led the school's athletic director to resign a month after this announcement.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.espn.com/college-sports/story/_/id/30263862/william-mary-changes-course-reinstates-3-men-sports |title=William & Mary changes course, reinstates 3 men's sports |agency=Associated Press |website=ESPN.com |date=5 November 2020 |accessdate=6 November 2020}}</ref> W&M eventually reversed course completely, restoring the three women's sports on 19 October<ref>{{cite press release|url=https://tribeathletics.com/news/2020/10/19/general-william-mary-athletics-the-path-forward.aspx |title=William & Mary Athletics: The Path Forward |publisher=William & Mary Tribe |date=19 October 2020 |accessdate=6 November 2020}}</ref> and announcing on 5 November that the four men's sports would continue to be sponsored through at least 2021–22.<ref>{{cite press release|url=https://tribeathletics.com/news/2020/11/5/general-university-resets-process-to-determine-long-term-sustainability-for-w-m-athletics.aspx |title=University resets process to determine long-term sustainability for W&M Athletics |publisher=William & Mary Tribe |date=5 November 2020 |accessdate=6 November 2020}}</ref>

[[MacMurray College]], [[Notre Dame de Namur University]], and [[Urbana University]] announced that they would wind down operations and close due to economic issues brought upon or exacerbated by the pandemic—effectively ending the entirety of their athletics programs.<ref>{{Cite web|title=Horgan: Notre Dame de Namur appears to be in a grim death spiral|url=https://www.mercurynews.com/horgan-notre-dame-de-namur-appears-to-be-in-a-grim-death-spiral|date=17 May 2020|website=The Mercury News|language=en-US|access-date=22 May 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|title=Coronavirus pandemic closes Urbana University campus permanently|url=https://www.cleveland.com/news/2020/04/coronavirus-pandemic-closes-urbana-university-campus-permanently.html|last=Bamforth|first=Emily|date=21 April 2020|newspaper=The Plain Dealer|location=Cleveland|language=en|access-date=22 May 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|title=END OF AN ERA: MacMurray closure means end of rivalry with Blackburn|url=https://www.thetelegraph.com/sports/article/END-OF-AN-ERA-MacMurray-closure-means-end-of-15192837.php|last=Emery|first=Tom|date=10 April 2020|website=Alton Telegraph|access-date=22 May 2020}}</ref>

In August 2020, officials at the [[University of California, Riverside]], a Division I member, publicly announced that shutting down the school's [[UC Riverside Highlanders|entire athletic program]] was one possible option to address pandemic-related financial challenges. As of mid-October, no decision on the program's future had yet been reached.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.espn.com/mens-college-basketball/story/_/id/30153974/uc-riverside-terms-division-survival-season-covid-19 |title=UC Riverside and the terms of Division I survival in the season of COVID-19 |first=Myron |last=Medcalf |website=ESPN.com |date=21 October 2020 |accessdate=21 October 2020}}</ref>

==Alpine skiing==
The [[2019–20 FIS Alpine Ski World Cup]] ended two weeks earlier after World Cup races in [[Sweden]], [[Slovenia]], and [[Italy]] scheduled for March were canceled.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.fis-ski.com/en/international-ski-federation/news-multimedia/news/fis-alpine-ski-world-cup-finals-cortina-ita-cancelled |title=FIS Alpine Ski World Cup Finals in Cortina Cancelled |date=6 March 2020 |publisher=[[International Ski Federation]] |access-date=29 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.fis-ski.com/en/alpine-skiing/alpine-news-multimedia/news-multimedia/news/test2/audi-fis-women-s-world-cup-races-in-are-swe-cancelled |title=Audi FIS Women's World Cup races in Are (SWE) Cancelled |date=11 March 2020 |publisher=[[International Ski Federation]] |access-date=29 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.fis-ski.com/en/alpine-skiing/alpine-news-multimedia/news-multimedia/news/test2/audi-fis-men-s-world-cup-races-in-kranjska-gora-slo-cancelled |title=Audi FIS Men's World Cup races in Kranjska Gora (SLO) Cancelled |date=12 March 2020 |publisher=[[International Ski Federation]] |access-date=29 March 2020}}</ref> An earlier February World Cup race was moved from China to [[Austria]].<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.espn.com/olympics/skiing/story/_/id/28600579/world-cup-ski-races-canceled-china-move-austria |title=World Cup ski races canceled in China move to Austria |date=30 January 2020 |website=[[ESPN]] |agency=Associated Press |access-date=29 March 2020 |quote=}}</ref>

==Archery==
The opening three stages of the [[2020 Archery World Cup]] were postponed. Other events postponed include the [[Pan American Archery Championships]], which were scheduled to be held in [[Monterrey]], [[Mexico]], from 23 to 29 March, and the [[European Para-Archery Championships]], which were scheduled to be held in [[Olbia]], [[Italy]], from 18 to 26 April.<ref>{{cite web |title=International Archery Suspended Until 30 April due to COVID-19 Outbreak |url=https://worldarchery.org/news/178285/international-archery-suspended-until-30-april-due-covid-19-outbreak-1 |website=World Archery |date=16 March 2020 |accessdate=24 March 2020}}</ref>

On 15 July it was announced that the [[2020 Archery World Cup]] would be cancelled.

==Association football==
{{main|Impact of the COVID-19 pandemic on association football}}

==Athletics==
The [[2021 World Athletics Indoor Championships|2020 World Athletics Indoor Championships]] were scheduled to be held from 13 to 15 March in [[Nanjing]], [[China]], but were postponed until March 2021.<ref>{{cite web |title=World Athletics to postpone World Athletics Indoor Championships Nanjing 2020 |url=https://www.worldathletics.org/news/press-releases/indoor-championships-nanjing-2020-postponed |website=World Athletics |accessdate=16 March 2020}}</ref>

The [[2020 World Athletics Half Marathon Championships]] was scheduled to be held on 29 March in [[Gdynia]], [[Poland]], but was postponed until October 2020.<ref>{{cite web |title=World Half Marathon Championships in Gdynia to be postponed |url=https://www.worldathletics.org/competitions/world-athletics-half-marathon-championships/news/world-half-marathon-championships-gdynia-post |website=World Athletics |accessdate=16 March 2020}}</ref>

The first three events of the [[2020 Diamond League]], scheduled to be held in [[Qatar]] in April, followed by two events in [[China]] in May, were postponed until later in the year.<ref>{{cite web |title=Wanda Diamond League suspends early-season events |url=https://www.diamondleague.com/news/single-news/news/detail/News/wanda-diamond-league-suspends-early-season-events/ |website=Diamond League |accessdate=23 March 2020}}</ref> On 12 May, a revised schedule was issued, but no points will be awarded for the events.

The [[2020 Boston Marathon]], originally scheduled for 20 April, was postponed until 14 September before being canceled completely on 28 May.<ref>{{Cite web|date=28 May 2020|title=Boston Marathon canceled for first time|url=https://www.espn.com/olympics/trackandfield/story/_/id/29235688/boston-marathon-canceled-first-due-coronavirus|access-date=3 July 2020|website=ESPN.com|language=en}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.boston.com/sports/boston-marathon/2020/03/15/2020-boston-marathon-monday-september |title=Marathon Monday in September? Here's what we know so far about the 2020 Boston Marathon's new date |work=Boston.com |accessdate=16 March 2020}}</ref> The [[2020 London Marathon]], scheduled to take place on 26 April, was postponed until 4 October and was restricted to elites only.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/sport/athletics/51878234 |title=Coronavirus: London Marathon postponed until October |newspaper=BBC Sport |date=13 March 2020 |accessdate=13 March 2020}}</ref> The 2020 [[Rome Marathon]] was cancelled as is with the [[Berlin Marathon|Berlin]], [[New York City marathon|New York City]] and the [[Toronto Waterfront Marathon]]s.<ref name="cancellation.1">{{cite web |author=user |url=https://www.runromethemarathon.com/en/2020/03/05/acea-run-rome-the-marathon-of-29-march-2020-cancelled/ |title=Acea Run Rome The Marathon of 29 March 2020 cancelled – ACEA RUN ROME THE MARATHON |publisher=Runromethemarathon.com |date=5 March 2020 |accessdate=14 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|title=Event Update|url=http://www.scc-events.com/en/corporate/events/event-update.html|access-date=3 July 2020|website=www.scc-events.com}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |url=https://clicklancashire.com/2020/06/26/new-york-city-marathon-set-for-november-1-canceled-because.html |title=Archived copy |access-date=29 June 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200630172513/https://clicklancashire.com/2020/06/26/new-york-city-marathon-set-for-november-1-canceled-because.html |archive-date=30 June 2020 |url-status=dead }}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.cp24.com/news/toronto-cancels-city-permitted-events-until-october-will-stage-online-only-nuit-blanche-1.5022482|title=Toronto cancels city-permitted events until October, will stage online only Nuit Blanche|first=Chris|last=Fox|date=13 July 2020|website=CP24}}</ref>

The 2020 [[Two Oceans Marathon]], scheduled for 8–11 April, has been cancelled.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.twooceansmarathon.org.za/2020-two-oceans-marathon-cancelled-amid-covid-19-pandemic/ |title=2020 Two Oceans Marathon cancelled amid COVID-19 Pandemic |website=Two Oceans Marathon |language=en-US|access-date=16 March 2020}}</ref>

The 2020 [[Three Peaks Race]], originally scheduled for 25 April, has been postponed to 26 September.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.grough.co.uk/magazine/2020/03/12/coronavirus-claims-second-dales-event-as-three-peaks-race-put-back-to-September |title=Coronavirus claims second Dales event as Three Peaks Race put back to September |date=12 March 2020 |accessdate=18 March 2020 |publisher=Grough |first=Bob |last=Smith}}</ref>

The 2020 [[Grandma's Marathon]], scheduled for 20 June, was canceled by the organizers more than 50 days before it was to begin. They announced on 31 March that the marathon, the half-marathon, and the 5K would all be canceled.<ref>{{cite web |author1=Grandma's Marathon staff |title=COVID-19 Update/Cancellation |url=https://grandmasmarathon.com/covid19/ |website=grandmasmarathon.com |accessdate=31 March 2020 |location=Duluth, Minnesota |date=31 March 2020}}</ref>

Two of the [[Standard Chartered]] 2020 marathon series, [[Hong Kong Marathon]] and [[Kuala Lumpur Marathon]] was cancelled by the organizer over uncertainty of the COVID-19 outbreak.<ref>{{cite news
| author    = SCMP Sport
| date     = 25 January 2020
| title    = Hong Kong Marathon cancelled in wake of coronavirus outbreak – most social media users say it's a 'wise' and 'right' decision

 |first=

The 2020 [[Berlin Marathon]] was prohibited from being held on its originally scheduled dates.<ref name="2020.notice">{{cite web|url=https://www.scc-events.com/en/corporate/events/event-update.html |title=Event Update ::: SCC &#124; EVENTS |publisher=Scc-events.com |date= |accessdate=22 April 2020}}</ref> It would be cancelled on 24 June.

The [[Atlanta Track Club]] originally moved the [[Peachtree Road Race]] from 4 July to 26 November, but the race was cancelled on 19 August 2020.  Organisers then moved the PNC Atlanta 10 Miler from [[Atlantic Station]] to [[Road Atlanta|Michelin Raceway]] in Hall County and renamed it the ''PNC Atlanta 10 Miler:  Extreme Hills Edition''.  Furthremore, officials announced on 2 November the 2021 [[Publix]] [[Atlanta Marathon]] will not be held in [[Centennial Olympic Park]] but will move 50km south to [[Hampton, Georgia]], as a multiple-loop race on the premises of [[Atlanta Motor Speedway]] in Henry County.  Organisers noted a continuing ban on events in Fulton County forced the moves to closed-course motorsport venues that are not public roads.

The 2020 [[Comrades Marathon]] were cancelled.<ref>{{cite news |title=Comrades Marathon cancelled due to Covid-19 |url=https://www.sport24.co.za/OtherSport/Athletics/comrades-marathon-cancelled-due-to-covid-19-20200514 |accessdate=14 May 2020 |agency=Sport24 |publisher=News24}}</ref>

Both the 2020 and 2021 editions of the [[Big Sur International Marathon]] were cancelled.<ref name="2021.cancellation">{{Cite web|url=https://www.montereyherald.com/big-sur-running-races-canceled-for-2021|title=Big Sur running races canceled for 2021|date=20 August 2020}}</ref><ref name="2021.cancellation.faq">{{Cite web|url=https://www.bigsurmarathon.org/frequently-asked-questions-about-big-sur-marathon-foundation-2020-and-2021-events-status/|title=Frequently Asked Questions about Big Sur Marathon 2020 and 2021 Events Status}}</ref>

On 28 October, organisers announced that the [[Boston Marathon|2021 Boston Marathon]] would not be held on [[Patriots Day]] (19 April) as usual, to be rescheduled to sometime in the fall.  Organisers cited an ongoing ban on road races in Massachusetts. <ref>{{cite web |title=2021 Boston Marathon Will Not Take Place in April |url=https://www.baa.org/2021-boston-marathon-will-not-take-place-april/ |website=Boston Athletic Association |accessdate=30 October 2020}}</ref>

==Australian rules football==
At the conclusion of its first round of games (played from 19 to 22 March), the [[2020 AFL season]] was suspended until 11 June, while the finals series of the [[2020 AFL Women's season]] was cancelled after its semi-finals were played, with no premiership awarded.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.news.com.au/sport/afl/afl-round-one-live-updates-travel-warnings-threaten-2020-season/news-story/7d60daac2b783f10205d648b1f19fc33 |title=AFL 2020 premiership officially postponed |date=22 March 2020 |website=NewsComAu |language=en|access-date=2 April 2020}}</ref>  Both the AFL Women's semi-finals and the first round of the AFL season were played in empty stadiums.

The annual [[Australian Football Hall of Fame]] induction event was instead held over four nights as a series of television shows with pre-recorded vision and interviews with the inductees.<ref>{{cite web |title=Four-night extravaganza: Hall of Fame locked in |url=https://www.afl.com.au/news/434008/four-night-extravaganza-hall-of-fame-locked-in |website=afl.com.au |accessdate=3 June 2020 |language=en| first=Callum|last=Twomey|date=25 May 2020}}</ref> The [[AFL Women's best and fairest]] awards were also changed to be a television only event, with the players being live streamed from their homes.<ref>{{cite news |title=Teenager Madison Prespakis named AFLW best-and-fairest for 2020 |url=https://www.abc.net.au/news/2020-04-28/madison-presipakis-named-aflw-best-and-fairest-winner/12194720 |accessdate=3 June 2020 |work=www.abc.net.au |date=28 April 2020 |language=en-AU}}</ref>

At levels below the fully professional AFL, most leagues either cancelled their entire season<ref>{{cite news |last1=Ractliffe |first1=Damien |title=Big metropolitan footy leagues abandon 2020 seasons |url=https://www.theage.com.au/sport/afl/big-metropolitan-footy-leagues-abandon-2020-seasons-20200603-p54z3d.html |accessdate=3 June 2020 |work=The Age |date=3 June 2020 |language=en}}</ref> or significantly delayed their start.<ref>{{cite news |title=WAFC boss still aiming for WAFL crowds |url=https://www.perthnow.com.au/sport/wafl/west-australian-football-commission-boss-gavin-taylor-still-hopeful-of-1500-crowds-at-some-point-during-wafl-season-ng-b881563687z |accessdate=3 June 2020 |work=PerthNow |date=31 May 2020 |language=en}}</ref> Player payments were cut to zero in the [[South Australian National Football League]].<ref>{{cite news |title=AFL 2020: SANFL return, zero salary cap in 2020, return from coronavirus, South Australia footy, players won't be paid |url=https://www.foxsports.com.au/afl/afl-2020-sanfl-return-zero-salary-cap-in-2020-return-from-coronavirus-south-australia-footy-players-wont-be-paid/news-story/653e76861d8158cbf24a4d2acb393fab |accessdate=3 June 2020 |work=Fox Sports |date=10 May 2020 |language=en-AU|first=Mitchell |last=Woodcock}}</ref>

The 2020 AFL season later resumed, however many games, particularly in the early rounds, were played without crowds. The league also reduced playing time by 20%, to four 16-minute quarters instead of 20-minute quarters.  Other smaller changes have also been added due to the pandemic.

On 28 June, officials in the state of [[Queensland]] announced a travel ban to and from the state of [[Victoria (Australian state)|Victoria]].  The AFL then relocated all games scheduled for Victoria to other states for that week and the following week.<ref>{{cite news |title=Richmond's clash with West Coast in Queensland cancelled after Victoria's COVID spike |url=https://www.7news.com.au/sport/afl/richmond-clash-with-west-coast-in-queensland-under-threat-after-victorias-covid-spike-c-1131115.amp |accessdate=17 July 2020 |work=Seven Network |date=28 June 2020 |language=en-AU|first=Glenn |last=Valencich}}</ref>  Then, on 15 July, the AFL announced that all teams based in Victoria would relocate to either Queensland or [[Western Australia]] for the rest of the season. This came due to Victoria ordering a six-week lockdown to deal with a surge in cases.<ref>{{cite news |title=Fixture bonanza: Get set for 19 straight days of footy |url=https://www.afl.com.au/news/465498/fixture-bonanza-get-set-for-19-straight-days-of-footy |accessdate=17 July 2020 |work=Australian Football League |date=15 July 2020 |language=en-AU|first=Damian |last=Barrett}}</ref>

On 21 July, the AFL revealed that matches in rounds 9 through 12 would be played in a rapid-fire format, every day from 29 July to 17 August.  Two games were played on selected Mondays, Wednesdays, and Thursdays during this period.  In addition, matches were not played in [[New South Wales]] due to an increase in coronavirus cases in that state.<ref>{{cite news |title=Footy every day: Check out the next four rounds of the AFL's fixture |url=https://www.afl.com.au/news/468187/footy-every-day-check-out-the-next-four-rounds-of-the-afl-s-fixture |accessdate=22 July 2020 |work=Australian Football League |date=21 July 2020 |language=en-AU|first=Damian |last=Barrett}}</ref>

The remaining games of the 2020 season were played predominantly in Queensland and South Australia, as well as Western Australia and the Northern Territory. Crowd levels were capped, but by the conclusion of the season, crowds of over 20,000 were able to attend games. The [[2020 AFL Grand Final|Grand Final]] was held on 24 October, around a month later than usual, at the Gabba, in Brisbane, Queensland - the first time the Grand Final was played outside of Victoria.

==Badminton==
All scheduled [[Badminton World Federation]] tournaments were suspended until 12 April due to coronavirus concerns.<ref>{{cite news |title=BWF Suspends International Badminton |url=https://bwfbadminton.com/news-single/2020/03/14/bwf-suspends-international-badminton/ |publisher=Badminton World Federation |accessdate=14 March 2020 |date=14 March 2020 |work=bwfbadminton.com}}</ref> The affected tournaments are [[2020 Swiss Open (badminton)|Swiss Open]], [[2020 India Open|India Open]], [[2020 Orléans Masters|Orléans Masters]], [[2020 Malaysia Open|Malaysia Open]], and [[2020 Singapore Open|Singapore Open]]. Previously the body had suspended the [[2020 German Open (badminton)|German Open]]<ref>{{cite news |title=BWF Media Statement on Yonex German Open 2020 |url=https://bwfworldtour.bwfbadminton.com/news-single/2020/02/26/bwf-media-statement-on-yonex-german-open-2020-2/ |publisher=Badminton World Federation |accessdate=2 March 2020 |date=26 February 2020 |work=bwfbadminton.com}}</ref> and pushed the [[2020 Lingshui China Masters|Lingshui China Masters]] from February to May 2020.<ref>{{cite news |title=BWF Statement on Postponement of Lingshui China Masters |url=https://bwfbadminton.com/news-single/2020/02/01/bwf-statement-on-postponement-of-lingshui-china-masters/ |publisher=Badminton World Federation |accessdate=2 February 2020 |date=1 February 2020 |work=bwfbadminton.com}}</ref> The [[2020 Thomas & Uber Cup]] had also originally been postponed to 15–23 August, but on 29 April was postponed again to 3–11 October after Denmark extended a ban on "larger gatherings" to 31 August.<ref>{{Cite web|title=New Dates for TOTAL BWF Thomas and Uber Finals 2020|url=https://bwfthomasubercups.bwfbadminton.com/news-single/2020/04/29/new-dates-for-total-bwf-thomas-and-uber-finals-2020|access-date=3 July 2020|website=bwfthomasubercups.bwfbadminton.com|language=en-US}}</ref>

On 6 April all scheduled tournaments were suspended until 1 August, with World Rankings frozen as of 17 March.

==Baseball==

===International===
The [[2021 World Baseball Classic – Qualification|qualifying round]] of the [[World Baseball Softball Confederation]]-sanctioned [[2021 World Baseball Classic]], scheduled in [[Tucson, Arizona]], United States in March 2020 was postponed on 12 March 2020.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Harrigan |first1=Thomas |title=World Baseball Classic qualifier games postponed |url=https://www.mlb.com/news/world-baseball-classic-qualifier-games-postponed |accessdate=13 March 2020 |work=MLB.com |date=12 March 2020}}</ref>  The tournament itself has been rescheduled tentatively to 2023, depending on a new collective bargaining agreement between MLB and the [[Major League Baseball Players' Association|players' union]].

On 30 April 2020, [[Little League International]] announced that the [[2020 Little League World Series]] and its associated regional qualifiers would be cancelled due to the pandemic. This was the first cancellation of [[Little League World Series|the tournament]] since its [[1947 Little League World Series|first edition in 1947]].<ref>{{cite news |title=Little League World Series canceled for first time because of coronavirus |url=https://www.espn.com/espn/story/_/id/29118983/little-league-world-series-canceled-first-coronavirus |accessdate=30 April 2020 |work=ESPN.com |date=30 April 2020}}</ref>

===Asia===

====Japan====
On 26 February 2020, [[Nippon Professional Baseball]] announced that spring training would continue behind closed doors.<ref>{{cite news |title=Japanese baseball to play remainder of preseason without spectators due to virus fears |url=https://www.japantimes.co.jp/sports/2020/02/26/baseball/japanese-baseball/japanese-baseball-play-remainder-preseason-without-spectators-due-virus-fears/ |accessdate=12 March 2020 |work=Japan Times |agency=Kyodo News |date=26 February 2020}}</ref> On 9 March, the league announced that the start of its [[2020 Nippon Professional Baseball season|2020 season]], originally scheduled for 20 March, would be postponed until April.<ref>{{cite news |title=Japan's pro baseball league delays season start over coronavirus |url=https://english.kyodonews.net/news/2020/03/6cba442bcfa8-breaking-news-japan-pro-baseball-to-delay-start-of-season-over-virus-source.html |accessdate=12 March 2020 |agency=Kyodo News |date=9 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Coskrey |first1=Jason |title=BayStars, Tigers managers react to NPB's decision to push back start of season |url=https://www.japantimes.co.jp/?post_type=sports&p=2526679 |accessdate=12 March 2020 |work=Japan Times |date=10 March 2020}}</ref> Eventually, the heavily-modified season started on 19 June and was shortened from 143 games to 120 games. To maximize the number of intraleague games that could be played, [[interleague play (NPB)|interleague play]] and the [[Nippon Professional Baseball All-Star Series|All-Star Series]] were eliminated.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Nagatsuka|first1=Kaz |title=NPB can play ball in Japan from June 19, but minus fans |url=https://www.japantimes.co.jp/sports/2020/05/25/baseball/japanese-baseball/npb-can-play-ball-june-19-stadiums-will-empty/ |accessdate=13 October 2020 |work=The Japan Times |date=25 May 2020}}</ref>  Additionally, NPB's post-season, the [[Climax Series]], was affected as well. The [[Pacific League]] reduced [[2020 Pacific League Climax Series|their post-season]] from two playoff series to one, while the [[Central League]] cancelled their Climax Series altogether, instead opting to advance their regular-season champion directly to the [[Japan Series]]<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.japantimes.co.jp/sports/2020/06/15/baseball/japanese-baseball/central-pacific-leagues-announce-schedules-remainder-season/ |title=Central, Pacific Leagues announce schedules for remainder of season |date=15 June 2020 |accessdate=16 June 2020 |work=[[The Japan Times]] |author=Nagatsuka, Kaz}}</ref> [[NPB Commissioner]] Atsushi Saito announced on June, fan entry admit within 5000 audience in ballpark, that start from 10 July, set on hand spray and thermo-temperatures measuring device in stadium entrance.{{citation needed|date=July 2020}}
According to NPB commissioner Saito announced on 12 September, the maximum number of all home stadium onto admit allowance spectators will be raised range from 11,000 to 20,000 from 19 September.{{citation needed|date=September 2020}}

On 4 March, the [[Japan High School Baseball Federation]] announced that the [[National High School Baseball Invitational Tournament]], scheduled to begin on 19 March, would take place without fans in attendance.<ref>{{cite news |title=Japan's Senbatsu spring HS baseball tourney to be held with no spectators due to virus |url=https://mainichi.jp/english/articles/20200304/p2a/00m/0na/025000c |accessdate=13 March 2020 |work=The Mainichi |date=4 March 2020}}</ref> However, on 11 March, the governing body of [[high school baseball in Japan]] declared that the tournament had been cancelled.<ref name=koshiencancel >{{cite news |title=Organizers cancel Spring Koshien due to COVID-19 crisis |url=https://www.japantimes.co.jp/sports/2020/03/11/baseball/cancel-spring-koshien-coronavirus/ |accessdate=12 March 2020 |work=Japan Times |agency=Kyodo News |date=11 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=Japan's Senbatsu spring HS baseball tournament canceled over coronavirus fears |url=https://mainichi.jp/english/articles/20200311/p2a/00m/0sp/017000c |accessdate=12 March 2020 |work=The Manichi |date=12 March 2020}}</ref> The cancellation of the 2020 tournament marked the first time the contest had been cancelled since its establishment in 1924. The tournaments were not formally scheduled between 1942 and 1946, due to [[World War II]].<ref name=koshiencancel /><ref>{{cite news |title=Spring high school baseball tourney cancelled over coronavirus |url=https://english.kyodonews.net/news/2020/03/c9ea2971def3-breaking-news-national-invitational-hs-baseball-tournament-cancelled-due-to-virus.html |accessdate=12 March 2020 |agency=Kyodo News |date=11 March 2020}}</ref> 
According to JHSBF chairman Hideaki Hatta announced on 20 May, all games, including regional qualifying were cancelled on [[Japanese High School Baseball Championship|High School Baseball Tournament of Japan]], that one of the more popular sports event in the nation, since [[Second World War]] (1941 to 1945).{{citation needed|date=September 2020}}
According to Japan Students Baseball Association honour chairman Tatsuro Matsumae (松前達郎) announced on 9 October,
a Meiji Shrine Baseball Tournament (明治神宮野球大会), section of university and senior high-school section officially suspend by high level positive infection continue [[COVID-19]] around [[Tokyo Metropolitan Area]], this tournament suspend since 1988, when critical condition of [[Emperor Hirohito]], after September.{{citation needed|date=October 2020}}

====South Korea====
Opening Day of the [[2020 KBO League season]] was originally scheduled for 28 March 2020.<ref>{{cite news |title=Baseball league announces 2020 regular season schedule |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200114224208/https://en.yna.co.kr/view/AEN20191216007100315 |accessdate=12 March 2020 |work=The Korea Herald |agency=Yonhap News Agency |archivedate=14 January 2020 |date=16 December 2019 |url=https://en.yna.co.kr/view/AEN20191216007100315}} [http://www.koreaherald.com/view.php?ud=20191216000870 Alt URL]</ref> The [[Korea Baseball Organization]] announced in March that all ten exhibition games would be cancelled.<ref>{{cite news |title=(LEAD) Pro baseball league postpones start of regular season over coronavirus |url=https://en.yna.co.kr/view/AEN20200310005251315?input=tw |accessdate=12 March 2020 |agency=Yonhap News Agency |date=10 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=The Latest: South Korean baseball season postponed |url=https://wtmj.com/national/2020/03/12/the-latest-south-korean-baseball-season-postponed/ |accessdate=12 March 2020 |agency=Associated Press |publisher=WTMJ-TV |date=12 March 2020}}</ref> The league later decided that exhibition games would be played starting 21 April with no spectators. The start of the regular season would also take place with no spectators, on 5 May.<ref>{{cite news |title=Baseball quietly returns to South Korea as games begin without fans |url=https://www.espn.com/mlb/story/_/id/29074958/baseball-quietly-returns-south-korea-games-begin-fans |accessdate=22 April 2020 |agency=Associated Press |work=ESPN.com |date=20 April 2020}}</ref>

====Taiwan====
The Taiwan-based [[Chinese Professional Baseball League]] was scheduled to begin its [[2020 Chinese Professional Baseball League season|2020 season]] on 14 March.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Gleeson |first1=Scott |title=Chinese Professional Baseball League team will have robot mannequins fill in as fans at games |url=https://www.usatoday.com/story/sports/mlb/2020/04/07/coronavirus-taiwanese-team-use-robots-fans-games-chinese-professional-baseball/2960662001/ |accessdate=14 April 2020 |work=USA Today |date=7 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Bengel |first1=Chris |title=Rakuten Monkeys will have robot mannequins dressed as fans when 2020 season begins |url=https://www.cbssports.com/mlb/news/rakuten-monkeys-will-have-robot-mannequins-dressed-as-fans-when-2020-season-begins/ |accessdate=11 April 2020 |agency=[[CBS Sports]] |date=7 April 2020}}</ref> On 1 April, the league announced that opening day would take place on 11 April, without fans in attendance.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Armstrong |first1=Megan |title=CPBL's Rakuten Monkeys to Use Robot Mannequins as Fans Amid COVID-19 |url=https://bleacherreport.com/articles/2885524-cpbls-rakuten-monkeys-to-use-robot-mannequins-as-fans-amid-covid-19 |accessdate=11 April 2020 |agency=[[Bleacher 2020}}</ref>  On 9 May, the CPBL began admitting spectators.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.newsday.com/sports/baseball/mlb-coronavirus-taiwan-cpbl-baseball-fans-1.44476409|title=MLB left watching and waiting as Taiwan allows 1,000 fans at games|website=Newsday}}</ref>

===North America===
[[File:Nationals players during the National Anthem.jpg|thumb|Cut-outs of fans placed in seats at [[Nationals Park]] in August 2020]]
[[File:Luis Rojas (50381392121) (cropped).jpg|thumb|upright|[[Luis Rojas (baseball)|Luis Rojas]] of the [[New York Mets]] wears a face mask in September 2020]] 


On 12 March 2020, [[Major League Baseball]] suspended all [[spring training]] activities. [[Opening Day]] of the 2020 season, scheduled for 26 March, was postponed, as was the start of the regular season for [[Minor League Baseball]], which was to begin on 9 April.<ref>{{cite news |title=MLB suspends spring training, delays Opening Day at least two weeks |url=https://www.espn.com/mlb/story/_/id/28892315/sources-mlb-expected-suspend-spring-training |accessdate=12 March 2020 |website=[[ESPN.com]] |date=12 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.mlb.com/news/mlb-2020-season-delayed |title=Opening Day delayed at least 2 weeks; Spring Training games cancelled |website=[[MLB.com]] |date=12 March 2020 |accessdate=12 March 2020}}</ref> In addition, the [[MLB Mexico Series|Mexico Series]] and [[MLB Puerto Rico Series|Puerto Rico Series]] games were canceled; the former would have featured the [[San Diego Padres]] playing the [[Arizona Diamondbacks]] at Mexico City's [[Estadio Alfredo Harp Helú]], and the latter featuring the [[New York Mets]] playing the [[Miami Marlins]] at [[Hiram Bithorn Stadium]] in [[San Juan, Puerto Rico|San Juan]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.chicagotribune.com/sports/cubs/ct-chicago-cubs-london-coronavirus-20200319-mrawzroybfeddblje4ltkxvf7q-story.html|title=MLB just canceled 2 international series in April. What does it mean for the Cubs-Cardinals series in London in June?|last=Gonzales|first=Mark|website=chicagotribune.com|access-date=1 April 2020}}</ref> MLB also canceled the 2020 [[MLB London Series|London Series]] games, which would have featured the [[Chicago Cubs]] playing the [[St. Louis Cardinals]] at [[London Stadium]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.espn.com/mlb/story/_/id/28981187/mlb-cancels-cubs-cards-london-series-june|title=MLB cancels Cubs-Cards London series in June|date=1 April 2020|website=ESPN.com|language=en|access-date=1 April 2020}}</ref>

Also on 12 March, the [[National Collegiate Athletic Association]] (NCAA) announced the suspension of its baseball season and cancellation of the entire season, further adding an automatic [[redshirt (college sports)|redshirt]] year without officially using a redshirt year.  Seniors who would have exhausted their eligibility would not be charged a year, as most conferences had not begun their conference seasons.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.omaha.com/sports/cws/college-baseball-stunned-after-ncaa-decision-to-cancel-college-world/article_ba4b22b5-7cbd-52a7-b0a0-edb0eba8f079.html |title=College baseball stunned after NCAA decision to cancel College World Series, end season in March |newspaper=Omaha World-Herald |last=Bland |first=Evan |date=12 March 2020 |accessdate=12 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ncaa.org/about/resources/media-center/news/division-i-council-extends-eligibility-student-athletes-impacted-covid-19 |title=NCAA Division I Council Extends Eligibility of Student-Athletes Impacted by COVID-19 |website=NCAA.org|language=en|access-date=15 July 2020}}</ref>

On 30 April, the [[2020 Little League World Series]] and its other associated tournaments were canceled, and with it, the [[2020 MLB Little League Classic]] game between the [[Boston Red Sox]] and [[Baltimore Orioles]] scheduled for 23 August in [[Williamsport, Pennsylvania]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.espn.com/espn/story/_/id/29118983/little-league-world-series-canceled-first-coronavirus|title=Little League World Series canceled for first time because of coronavirus pandemic|publisher=[[ESPN]]|accessdate=30 April 2020|date=30 April 2020}}</ref>

Several [[summer collegiate baseball]] leagues were canceled entirely, while others postponed their starts from the beginning of June to the beginning of July. The [[Portland Pickles]] of the [[West Coast League]] announced that they would play without fans, while several other teams withdrew from their leagues entirely.<ref>{{Cite web|title=Pickles plan season slate sans fans|url=https://ballparkdigest.com/2020/05/07/pickles-plan-season-slate-sans-fans/|last=Reichard|first=Kevin|date=7 May 2020|website=Ballpark Digest|language=en-US|access-date=8 May 2020}}</ref>

On 30 June 2020 Minor League Baseball was cancelled outright.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.mlb.com/news/2020-minor-league-baseball-season-canceled |title=2020 Minor League Baseball season canceled |first=David |last=Adler |website=[[MLB.com]] |date=30 June 2020 |accessdate=30 June 2020}}</ref>

On 1 July, the 2020 [[Mexican Baseball League]] season was cancelled because of MiLB affiliations.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.espn.com/mlb/story/_/id/29394774/mexico-cancels-baseball-season-coronavirus-pandemic|title=Mexico cancels baseball season because of coronavirus pandemic|work=ESPN|date=1 July 2020}}</ref>

On 18 July, the [[Toronto Blue Jays]] were denied permission by the Canadian federal government to play their home games at the [[Rogers Centre]].<ref>{{cite web |last1=Harrington |first1=Mike |title=Buffalo bound? Canada denies Blue Jays permission to play in Toronto |url=https://buffalonews.com/sports/buffalo-bound-canada-denies-blue-jays-permission-to-play-in-toronto/article_2bd47384-c92a-11ea-b29e-b3ec114b6725.html |website=The Buffalo News |accessdate=19 July 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |last1=Armstrong |first1=Laura |title=The Blue Jays will call Buffalo or Dunedin home after Rogers Centre pitch strikes out |url=https://www.thestar.com/sports/bluejays/2020/07/18/the-blue-jays-will-call-buffalo-or-dunedin-home-after-rogers-centre-pitch-strikes-out.html |website=The Toronto Star |accessdate=19 July 2020}}</ref> On 24 July, the Blue Jays announced they would play their home games at [[Sahlen Field]] in [[Buffalo, New York|Buffalo]].<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.usatoday.com/story/sports/mlb/bluejays/2020/07/24/toronto-blue-jays-play-home-games-buffalo-2020/5502146002/|title=Toronto Blue Jays to play home games at Buffalo's Sahlen Field this season|first=Bob|last=Nightengale|website=USA TODAY}}</ref>

The 60-game [[2020 Major League Baseball season]] began on 23 July with the [[New York Yankees]] at [[Washington Nationals]] and [[San Francisco Giants]] at [[Los Angeles Dodgers]]. Subsequently, seven teams were forced to postpone games as a result of COVID-19 outbreaks.  The worst of these, and the first, involved 17 members of the [[Miami Marlins]].  Starting on 27 July 11 of their games were postponed.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.si.com/mlb/2020/07/28/washington-nationals-miami-marlins-coronavirus|title=Nationals Push Back Against Playing Marlins in Miami|publisher=Sports Illustrated}}</ref>  This was followed, in order, by the [[2020 Philadelphia Phillies season|Philadelphia Phillies]], [[2020 St. Louis Cardinals season|St. Louis Cardinals]], [[2020 Cincinnati Reds season|Cincinnati Reds]], [[2020 New York Mets season|New York Mets]], [[2020 Oakland Athletics season|Oakland Athletics]], and [[2020 San Francisco Giants season|San Francisco Giants]].

====Justin Turner controversy====
During the 2020 MLB season, teams endured multiple outbreaks. In their handling of positive tests, many teams complied with updated protocols, making sure that infected team members were not spreading the virus to other players, coaching staff, and members of the organization. Compliance lapsed when one of the players, [[2020 Los Angeles Dodgers season|Los Angeles Dodgers]] third baseman [[Justin Turner]], who had a positive COVID-19 case, stormed the field after the Dodgers won the [[2020 World Series]]. After being ordered into isolation and failing to comply with the rules - by running onto the field, taking photos, and hugging players - Turner, the Dodgers, and MLB received unwanted backlash from fans and the media around the world.<ref name=":110">{{Cite web|last=Williams Davis|first=Bradford|date=28 October 2020|title=Justin Turner and the Dodgers ruined their title celebration with reckless behavior|url=https://www.nydailynews.com/sports/baseball/ny-20201028-jlpdxlwoh5eytcr6avn6jgso2u-story.html|url-status=live|archive-url=|archive-date=|access-date=|website=New York Daily News}}</ref>

After an MLB investigation, no further action was taken against Turner or the Dodgers; however, there were reportedly five positive tests among other members of the organization.

Turner's diagnosis was announced late in the Dodgers' Game 6 eventual win.  It has been speculated that the World Series would have faced significant delays if the [[2020 Tampa Bay Rays season|Tampa Bay Rays]] had won and forced a Game 7.

==Basketball==

===Africa===
The launch of the [[2020 BAL season|inaugural season]] of the [[Basketball Africa League]] set for March 2020 was delayed due to the coronavirus pandemic. No new date has been announced.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Solomon |first1=Salem |title=Basketball Africa League Delays Inaugural Season Because of Coronavirus |url=https://www.voanews.com/science-health/coronavirus-outbreak/basketball-africa-league-delays-inaugural-season-because |accessdate=13 March 2020 |agency=Voice of America |date=6 March 2020}}</ref>

===Asia===
The [[2019–20 Chinese Basketball Association season]] was suspended on 1 February 2020.<ref>{{cite news |last=Prewitt |first=Alex |url=https://www.si.com/nba/2020/03/13/cba-coronavirus-nba-allerik-freeman |title=While the NBA Pauses, China Is Ready to Play Again. For Better or Worse |date=13 March 2020 |work=Sports Illustrated |accessdate=20 March 2020}}</ref> However, [[China Basketball Association|China Basketball Association (CBA)]] chairman [[Yao Ming]] announced that the season will restart on 20 June, without spectators.<ref>{{cite news|date=4 June 2020|title=篮协：经体育和卫健部门同意 CBA6月20日复赛|language=zh|work=Sinasports|url=https://sports.sina.cn/cba/2020-06-04/detail-iircuyvi6708481.d.html|accessdate=24 June 2020}}</ref>

On 14 February, [[FIBA]] ordered two [[2021 FIBA Asia Cup qualification|qualifying games for the 2021 FIBA Asia Cup]], [[Philippines men's national basketball team|Philippines]] vs [[Thailand national basketball team|Thailand]] in [[Quezon City]], and [[Japan national basketball team|Japan]] vs. [[China men's national basketball team|China]] in [[Chiba (city)|Chiba]] to be postponed to a later date. This brought the postponed games to three, after FIBA earlier ordered the China vs. [[Malaysia national basketball team|Malaysia]] game in [[Foshan]] to be postponed.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.fiba.basketball/asiacup/2021/qualifiers/news/three-fiba-asia-cup-2021-qualifier-games-postponed |title=Three FIBA Asia Cup 2021 Qualifier games postponed |website=FIBA.basketball |language=en|access-date=25 March 2020}}</ref> Later that week, the [[Guam national basketball team|Guam]] vs. [[Hong Kong basketball team|Hong Kong]] game in [[Hagåtña, Guam|Hagåtña]] was also postponed.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.fiba.basketball/asiacup/2021/qualifiers/news/fiba-asia-cup-2021-qualifier-between-guam-and-hong-kong-postponed |title=FIBA Asia Cup 2021 Qualifier game between Guam and Hong Kong postponed |website=FIBA.basketball |language=en|access-date=25 March 2020}}</ref>

The [[Korean Basketball League]] canceled its [[2019–20 KBL season|2019–20 season]] on 24 March, after playing its last game on 29 February. This comes as the [[Women's Korean Basketball League]] canceled its season a week before.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.koreaherald.com/view.php?ud=20200324000415 |title=Men's basketball league cancels season due to coronavirus |last=Herald |first=The Korea |date=24 March 2020 |website=www.koreaherald.com |language=en|access-date=24 March 2020}}</ref>

On 4 March, FIBA announced the cancellation of the [[2019 FIBA Under-16 Asian Championship]] in [[Beirut]] and the 2019 FIBA Under-16 Asian Championship for Women in [[Canberra]]. It also postponed the [[Basketball at the 2020 Summer Olympics – Men's 3x3 qualification|3x3 Olympic qualification tournament]] in [[Bangalore]], and rescheduled the 2020 [[FIBA Asia 3x3 Cup]]s in [[Changsha]] and the 2020 FIBA 3x3 Under-17 Asian Cup in [[Cyberjaya]].<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.fiba.basketball/news/changes-made-to-several-fiba-events-due-to-covid-19-virus |title=Changes made to several FIBA events due to COVID-19 virus |website=FIBA.basketball |language=en|access-date=25 March 2020}}</ref>

The 2019–20 season of the [[Super Basketball League]] in Taiwan continued despite the outbreak. When the Taiwanese government shut down all publicly-controlled arenas on 19 March, the league contemplated of shutting down as well, but ended up on holding all of its games at the HaoYu Basketball Training Center. No less than 100 people are in the arena at any time.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.axios.com/taiwan-basketball-coronavirus-nba-4dca5ee0-7e9c-40c6-a4b7-9e5baabb8549.html|title=Taiwan's basketball bubble could preview the NBA's coronavirus return|last=Baker|first=Kendall|website=Axios|language=en|access-date=29 April 2020}}</ref>

====ASEAN Basketball League====
Several fixtures of the [[ASEAN Basketball League]] [[2019–20 ABL season|2019–20 season]] scheduled in February onwards were rescheduled due to the coronavirus pandemic. In early March 2020, four participating teams, [[Alab Pilipinas]], [[Hong Kong Eastern Basketball Team|Hong Kong Eastern]], [[Macau Black Bears]] and [[Formosa Dreamers]] has released statements urging the suspension of the whole season due to logistical issues posed by COVID-19-related travel measures in Southeast Asia, [[mainland China]] and Taiwan.<ref>{{cite news |title=Alab Pilipinas, three other teams want ABL to suspend season due to COVID-19 |url=https://sports.mb.com.ph/2020/03/12/alab-pilipinas-three-other-teams-want-abl-to-suspend-season-due-to-covid-19/ |accessdate=13 March 2020 |work=Manila Bulletin |date=12 March 2020}}</ref> On 13 March 2020, the league's 2019–20 season was postponed indefinitely.<ref name="pbateams">{{cite news |last1=Dalupang |first1=Denison Rey |title=PBA: Teams can't hold practices, scrimmages |url=https://sports.inquirer.net/389302/pba-teams-cant-hold-practices-scrimmages |accessdate=14 March 2020 |work=Philippine Daily Inquirer |date=14 March 2020}}</ref> On 15 July 2020, the league announced that it canceled the season, without a champion being named.<ref>{{Cite web|date=15 July 2020|title=Asean Basketball League season cancelled without a winner|url=https://www.tnp.sg/sports/basketball/asean-basketball-league-season-cancelled-without-winner|access-date=15 July 2020|website=The New Paper|language=en}}</ref>

====Philippines====
The [[2020 PBA season|2020 season]] of the [[Philippine Basketball Association]] (PBA) and the [[PBA D-League]] was suspended indefinitely on 10 March 2020 after its first game had completed. The inaugural of the PBA's 3x3 tournament was also likewise delayed.<ref name=pba>{{cite news |title=PBA suspends games indefinitely due to COVID-19 threat |url=https://www.gmanetwork.com/news/sports/basketball/729223/pba-suspends-games-indefinitely-due-to-covid-19/story/ |accessdate=13 March 2020 |work=GMA News |date=11 March 2020}}</ref> The PBA management also imposed a two-week prohibition on team "practices, scrimmages and other related activities" which took effect on 14 March 2020.<ref name="pbateams"/>

Several leagues have suspended their tournaments on 12 March: [[Community Basketball Association]], [[National Basketball League (Philippines)|National Basketball League]], [[Maharlika Pilipinas Basketball League]].<ref>[https://www.spin.ph/life/guide/list-of-sports-events-suspended-coronavirus-a1374-20200312 Here's a list of sports events suspended due to coronavirus], [[Sports Interactive Network|spin.ph]], 12 March 2020</ref>
