On 7 April 2020, the PBA Board of Governors have decided to shorten this season into a two-conference season (later revised to a one-conference season on August) following the postponement of the Philippine Cup due to the [[COVID-19 pandemic|outbreak]] of [[Coronavirus disease 2019|COVID-19]] and the enforcement of the Enhanced Community Quarantine in Luzon until 30 April.<ref name = "PBA-COVID">[https://www.pba.ph/news/pba-board-decides-to-shorten-season-45 PBA board decides to shorten Season 45], PBA.ph, 7 April 2020</ref>

On 17 September, the PBA Board of Governors have approved a plan to restart the season on 11 October (originally on 9 October), then was given a provisional approval by the [[Inter-Agency Task Force on Emerging Infectious Diseases]] (IATF-ID) on 24 September. All games will be played in the "PBA bubble"  at the Clark Freeport Zone in Pampanga, the isolation zone specifically created for league operations.<ref name = "pbabubble">[https://www.spin.ph/basketball/pba/pba-to-hold-bubble-season-at-clark-freeport-zone-in-pampanga-a795-20200917 PBA to hold 'bubble season' at Clark Freeport Zone in Pampanga], Reuben Terrado, spin.ph, 17 September 2020</ref><ref name="PBA-ITAFapproval">[https://www.spin.ph/basketball/pba/pba-given-provisional-clearance-for-scrimmages-games-in-bubble-a793-20200924 IATF provisional clearance paves way for PBA scrimmages, games in Clark bubble], Gerry Ramos, spin.ph, 24 September 2020</ref>

===Europe===
[[Jordi Bertomeu]], CEO of the [[Euroleague]], suspended the games from 14 March to 11 April. The Euroleague previously suspended the [[EuroCup Basketball|Eurocup]]. FIBA also suspended the [[Basketball Champions League]] and the [[FIBA Europe Cup]] starting on 14 March. [[Lietuvos krepšinio lyga|Lithuania]], [[Swedish Basketball League|Sweden]], [[Swiss Basketball League|Switzerland]], [[Slovak Basketball League|Slovakia]] and [[Ukrainian Basketball SuperLeague|Ukraine]] canceled outright their respective first division leagues, naming the teams in the top of the standings as champions. Top flight divisions in [[Liga ACB|Spain]], [[LNB Pro A|France]], [[Basketball Bundesliga|Germany]], [[Lega Basket Serie A|Italy]], [[Israeli Basketball Premier League|Israel]], [[Pro Basketball League|Belgium]], [[Korisliiga|Finland]], [[HT Premijer liga|Croatia]], [[Greek Basket League|Greece]], [[Polish Basketball League|Poland]], [[Cyprus Basketball Division A|Cyprus]], and [[National Basketball League (Czech Republic)|Czech Republic]] suspended its games as of 14 March. The [[ABA League|Adriatic League]] and the [[VTB United League]] suspended its competitions until April.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.espn.com/nba/story/_/id/28898393/international-basketball-virtually-shut-coronavirus-concerns |title=International basketball virtually shut down |date=13 March 2020 |website=ESPN.com |language=en|access-date=23 March 2020}}</ref>

The government of Turkey suspended the [[Basketball Super League]] on 19 March, the last major European league to do so.<ref name=":1">{{cite web |url=https://www.si.com/nba/2020/03/19/turkey-basketball-soccer-suspended-coronavirus |title=Turkey Suspends Soccer, Basketball Seasons |last=West |first=Jenna |website=Sports Illustrated |language=en-us|access-date=23 March 2020}}</ref>

On 6 June, the [[2019–20 Basketball Bundesliga]] in Germany restarted with a ten-team closing tournament with the top teams invited.{{citation needed|date=June 2020}}

===North America===

====2019-2020 season====
[[File:Signs during pandemic in Brooklyn (20555).jpg|thumb|In many New York City parks, hoops were removed from basketball courts to discourage people being in groups.]]
On 11 March 2020, the [[National Basketball Association]] (NBA) [[Suspension of the 2019–20 NBA season|suspended its season]] after [[Utah Jazz]] player [[Rudy Gobert]] tested positive for coronavirus prior to tip-off for a scheduled game against the [[Oklahoma City Thunder]].<ref name="nba-suspension-of-season">{{cite web |title=NBA to suspend season following Wednesday's games |url=https://www.nba.com/article/2020/03/11/nba-suspend-season-following-wednesdays-games |website=NBA.com |accessdate=12 March 2020 |date=11 March 2020}}</ref> Commissioner [[Adam Silver]] stated the next day that this suspension "will be most likely at least 30 days, and we don't know enough to be more specific than that".<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.espn.com/nba/story/_/id/28893331/nba-owners-seeking-30-day-reevaluation-suspension-games |title=Silver: NBA hiatus likely to last 'at least' 30 days |date=12 March 2020 |website=ESPN.com |language=en|access-date=13 March 2020}}</ref>

On 12 March, all [[NCAA Division I|Division I]] conferences in [[college basketball]] canceled their respective tournaments in-progress. The [[Ivy League]] had already called off its tournament prior to the decision, while some conferences, as well as the NCAA for its [[2020 NCAA Division I Men's Basketball Tournament|men's]] and [[2020 NCAA Division I Women's Basketball Tournament|women's]] tournaments, had previously announced that they would conduct their games behind closed doors.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.cnbc.com/2020/03/12/coronavirus-ncaa-conference-tournaments-cancellations.html |title=Big Ten, SEC, ACC scrap conference tournaments, adding to wave of coronavirus-related sports cancellations |last=Eudaily |first=Chris |date=12 March 2020 |publisher=CNBC|access-date=12 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.latimes.com/sports/story/2020-03-12/pac-12-mens-basketball-tournament-canceled-over-coronavirus-pandemic |title=Pac-12 cancels all sports competitions 'until further notice' because of coronavirus |date=12 March 2020 |website=Los Angeles Times|access-date=12 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.espn.com/mens-college-basketball/story/_/id/28891602/big-ten-sec-american-cancel-conference-tournaments |title=Conference tournaments shut down over virus |date=12 March 2020 |publisher=ESPN|access-date=12 March 2020}}</ref> The NCAA subsequently canceled its tournaments outright.<ref name=":13" /><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.latimes.com/sports/story/2020-03-12/march-madness-ncaa-tournament-canceled-coronavirus |title=No shining moments: NCAA basketball tournaments are canceled for the first time |date=13 March 2020 |website=Los Angeles Times|access-date=13 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.cbssports.com/college-football/news/coronavirus-updates-ncaa-cancels-championship-competition-for-all-winter-and-spring-sports/ |title=Coronavirus updates: NCAA cancels championship competition for all winter and spring sports |website=CBSSports.com|access-date=13 March 2020}}</ref>

On 14 March, the [[Baloncesto Superior Nacional]] of [[Puerto Rico]] suspended its season.<ref name=":1" />

On 23 March, [[National Basketball League of Canada]] suspended the remainder of the [[2019–20 NBL Canada season|2019–20 season]].<ref>{{cite web |url=https://nblcanada.ca/sports/mbkb/2019-20/releases/20200312nqi4na |title=NBLC Suspends Remainder of 2019–20 Season Until Further Notice |website=National Basketball League of Canada |language=en |date=12 March 2020}}</ref>

On 3 April, the [[Women's National Basketball Association]] (WNBA) announced that they will have postponed the start of training camp and regular season which was originally scheduled for 15 May.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.wnba.com/news/wnba-statement-regarding-the-start-of-the-2020-regular-season/ |title=WNBA Statement Regarding the Start of the 2020 Regular Season |publisher=WNBA |website=wnba.com |date=3 April 2020|access-date=3 April 2020}}</ref> The [[2020 WNBA draft]] was held virtually and televised on 17 April 2020 without players, guests, and media on-site.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.wnba.com/news/wnba-draft-2020-to-be-held-april-17/ |title=WNBA Draft 2020 Presented By State Farm To Be Held As Scheduled On April 17 |publisher=WNBA |website=wnba.com |date=26 March 2020 |accessdate=26 March 2020}}</ref>

On 4 June, it was announced that the season would restart on 31 July for 22 teams still in playoff contention at the time of the suspension, and would finish no later than 12 October. Professional teams such as the [[Houston Rockets]] saw their seasons impacted as players like all-star [[Russell Westbrook]] tested positive for COVID-19.<ref>{{Cite web|last1=Young|first1=Matt|last2=Chronicle|first2=Houston|date=13 July 2020|title=Rockets' Russell Westbrook has COVID-19, says: 'Mask up!'|url=https://www.chron.com/sports/rockets/article/Houston-Rockets-Russell-Westbrook-COVID-19-Mask-Up-15404621.php|access-date=24 July 2020|website=Houston Chronicle}}</ref>

On 30 July, the [[2019–20 NBA season]] officially resumed in the [[2020 NBA Bubble|NBA Bubble]].

====2020-2021 season====
Pandemic impacts continued into the next college basketball season.  The earliest allowable date for games in the 2020-21 season was pushed back from 10 to 25 November, when most campuses would have either concluded their fall term or moved remaining classes online. In addition, the maximum number of games was reduced by four (to 27), and the minimum number of games required to qualify for the national championship tournament was halved from 26 to 13. <ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ncaa.org/about/resources/media-center/news/di-council-approves-nov-25-start-date-men-s-and-women-s-basketball |title=DI Council approves Nov. 25 start date for men’s and women’s basketball |website=NCAA |accessdate=2020-12-14}}</ref> 

Scheduling of games was also disrupted with early season "Multi-Team Events" cancelled, relocated, or rearranged. The [[Maui Invitational]] was moved from [[Lahaina, Hawaii]] to [[Asheville, North Carolina]], while the [[Battle 4 Atlantis]] in [[Nassau, Bahamas]] was also canceled and replaced by a separate event, the Crossover Classic, being held at the [[Sanford Pentagon]] and featuring most of the teams originally invited.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://twitter.com/jasperward94/status/1306675455785873419 |title=Tweet |website=twitter.com |accessdate=2020-12-13}}</ref> Between 25 November<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.heraldsun.com/sports/college/acc/nc-state/article247576975.html|title=So far, so good for Wolfpack men inside NCAA bubble|last=Pope IV|first=Jonas|work=[[The Herald-Sun (Durham, North Carolina)|The Herald-Sun]]|date=3 December 2020|accessdate=5 December 2020}}</ref> and 5 December, almost two weeks of nonconference games were played at [[Mohegan Sun]], in a secured environment marketed as "Bubbleville".<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.cbssports.com/college-basketball/news/how-mohegan-suns-bubbleville-set-a-template-for-how-college-basketballs-season-and-postseason-can-work/|title=How Mohegan Sun's Bubbleville set a template for how college basketball's season, and postseason, can work|last=Norlander|first=Matt|work=[[CBS Sports]]|date=1 December 2020|accessdate=5 December 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url=https://apnews.com/article/connecticut-basketball-jay-wright-coronavirus-pandemic-casinos-01dd6d7d809db3836b7535a15964ae7a|title=Nova's Jay Wright says bubble stay takes mental toll on players|last=Eaton-Robb|first=Pat|work=AP News|date=2 December 2020|accessdate=14 December 2020}}</ref>

Some conference adapted altered scheduling formats intended to limit air travel (divisions, back to back games at one site), and allow opportunities for cancelled games to be rescheduled.<ref>{{cite web|url= https://www.cbssports.com/college-basketball/news/college-basketball-conference-schedules-loaded-with-quirks-and-strange-formats-amid-covid-19-pandemic/|title=College basketball conference schedules loaded with quirks and strange formats amid COVID-19 pandemic|website=CBS Sports |accessdate=2020-12-14}}</ref>

Due to ongoing restrictions on traffic on the [[Canada–United States border]], the [[Toronto Raptors]] will play their home games at [[Amalie Arena]] in [[Tampa, Florida]] when the [[2020–21 NBA season]] begins on 22 December.<ref>{{cite web|url= https://twitter.com/ShamsCharania/status/1329846469168336897|title=Tweet |website=twitter.com |accessdate=2020-12-13}}</ref>

On 25 November, the NBA announced that its annual [[NBA All-Star Game|All-Star Game]] and other weekend events would not be held during the coming season.  The [[Indiana Pacers]] - who were to have hosted the weekend at [[Bankers Life Fieldhouse]] - were given the 2024 game as compensation.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.nba.com/pacers/news/nba-all-star-2021-indianapolis-postponed-2024 |title=NBA All-Star 2021 in Indianapolis Postponed to 2024 |date=25 November 2020 |website=NBA.com |language=en|access-date=28 November 2020}}</ref>

===Oceania===
In Australia's [[National Basketball League (Australia)|National Basketball League]], the [[2020 NBL Finals|2020 NBL Grand Final]] between the [[Sydney Kings]] and [[Perth Wildcats]] was played behind closed doors beginning with Game 2, and the NBL stated that it would be suspended immediately if any player was diagnosed.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.smh.com.au/sport/basketball/nbl-grand-final-series-to-be-completed-behind-closed-doors-20200313-p549xx.html |title=NBL grand final series to be completed behind closed doors |last=Ward |first=Roy |date=13 March 2020 |website=The Sydney Morning Herald |language=en|access-date=23 March 2020}}</ref>

After Game 3—trailing 2–1 in a best-of-five series—the Kings announced 17 March that they would withdraw from the Finals, due to "a critical mass of relevant and actual concerns related to player welfare and the club's social responsibility". The NBL had been considering playing Game 4 of the series on 18 March instead of 20 March as originally scheduled to accelerate its completion.<ref name="auto">{{cite web |url=https://www.foxsports.com.au/basketball/nbl/perth-wildcats-disappointed-with-sydney-kings-nbl-grand-final-decision/news-story/2426c7f70f33f5a06e963a4c971365c4 |title=NBL Grand Final 2020: Perth Wildcats 'disappointed' with Sydney Kings' NBL Grand Final decision |date=17 March 2020 |website=Fox Sports |language=en-AU|access-date=23 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.foxsports.com.au/basketball/nbl/breaking-nbl-season-called-off-midfinals-due-to-coronavirus-crisis/news-story/7f707f71310056816e01d8d99e7748cf |title=NBL Grand Final 2020: NBL season called off mid-finals due to coronavirus crisis, Sydney Kings vs Perth Wildcats |date=17 March 2020 |website=Fox Sports |language=en-AU|access-date=23 March 2020}}</ref> On 18 March, the NBL declared the Perth Wildcats as champions by [[Default (sport)|default]].<ref>{{cite web |url=https://thewest.com.au/sport/perth-wildcats/nbl-grand-final-title-win-the-last-piece-of-the-puzzle-for-stoked-perth-wildcats-ng-b881494184z |title=Title win the last piece of the puzzle for stoked Cats |date=19 March 2020 |website=The West Australian |language=en|access-date=23 March 2020}}</ref>

=== South America ===
[[Novo Basquete Brasil]] canceled its season on 4 May due to the [[COVID-19 pandemic in Brazil]].<ref>{{cite web|date=4 May 2020|title=Após decisão unânime dos clubes, LNB encerra temporada do NBB 2019/2020|trans-title=After unanimous clubs decision, LNB ends the 2019/2020 NBB season|url=https://globoesporte.globo.com/sp/mogi-das-cruzes-suzano/basquete/nbb/noticia/apos-votacao-dos-clubes-lnb-encerra-temporada-do-nbb-20192020.ghtml|website=Globo Esporte|language=Portuguese}}</ref>

==Biathlon==
The [[2019–20 Biathlon World Cup]] ended a week and a day earlier than previously scheduled. The World Cup final in Norway was cancelled as was the last day of the penultimate World Cup in Finland.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.biathlonworld.com/news/detail/ibu-statement-on-world-cup-in-oslo |title=Update: IBU Statement on World Cup in Oslo, Kontiolahti and Junior OECH |date=13 March 2020 |website=Biathlon World |access-date=29 March 2020}}</ref>

Before the races in Finland and Norway, the World Cup races in [[Nové Město na Moravě|Nové Město]], Czech Republic, 5–8 March, were held without spectators.<ref>{{Cite web|title=World Cup Biathlon races held without spectators|url=https://www.radio.cz/en/section/picture-of-week/world-cup-biathlon-races-held-without-spectators|last=|first=|date=9 March 2020|website=[[Radio Prague|Radio Prague International]]|access-date=29 May 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|title=How the Coronavirus Has Disrupted Sports Events|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2020/03/02/sports/coronavirus-sports.html|last=Mather|first=Victor|date=5 March 2020|website=[[The New York Times]]|access-date=29 May 2020}}</ref>

The [[2020–21 Biathlon World Cup]] changed some locations to minimize travel between venues.<ref>{{Cite web|last=Morgan|first=Liam|date=6 October 2020|title=IBU move Biathlon World Cup event from Ruhpolding to Oberhof|url=https://www.insidethegames.biz/articles/1099242/ibu-move-world-cup-event-to-oberhof|url-status=live|archive-url=|archive-date=|access-date=23 October 2020|website=www.insidethegames.biz}}</ref> The 2020–21 IBU Junior Cup and some events of the 2020–21 IBU Cup were cancelled.<ref>{{Cite web|title=IBU adjusts competition schedule for 2020/21 season|url=https://www.biathlonworld.com/news/detail/ibu-adjusts-competition-schedule-for-2020-21-season|access-date=23 October 2020|website=International Biathlon Union - IBU}}</ref>

==Bodybuilding==
Several competitive events in international [[Bodybuilding|competitive bodybuilding]] on the amateur and [[Professional bodybuilding|professional]] levels have seen limitations, postponements, or even cancellations due to concerns about the spread of COVID-19.{{citation needed|date=March 2020}}

Due to these concerns Ohio governor [[Mike DeWine]] reduced the 2020 [[Arnold Sports Festival]] in [[Columbus, Ohio]] on 3 March, before any [[COVID-19 pandemic in Ohio|cases or deaths had been reported in the state]]. The cancellation was widely regarded as 'radical' at the time.<ref>{{cite web |title=The US governor who saw it coming early |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-us-canada-52113186 |website=[[BBC News]] |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20200401045917/https://www.bbc.com/news/world-us-canada-52113186 |archivedate=1 April 2020 |date=1 April 2020 |url-status=live}}</ref><ref name=barrett>{{Cite news |last=Barrett |first=Joe |url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/ohio-governor-on-why-he-ordered-early-tough-coronavirus-lockdowns-11585501200 |title=Ohio Governor on Why He Ordered Early, Tough Coronavirus Lockdowns |date=29 March 2020 |work=Wall Street Journal|access-date=30 March 2020 |language=en-US |issn=0099-9660}}</ref> The Fitness Expo (under orders from the state government) held the bodybuilding and physique competitions, including the Arnold Classic, without spectators with exceptions for parents and guardians of minors participating in the competitions.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.arnoldsportsfestival.com/visitor-info/media/update-March-3/ |title=UPDATED EVENTS SCHEDULE |work=Arnold Sports Festival |accessdate=18 March 2020}}</ref> Similar Arnold Sports Festivals planned to be held in Africa, Australia, and South America were postponed for later in the year.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.arnoldsportsfestival.com/ |title=ARNOLD SPORTS FESTIVALS IN AUSTRALIA, SOUTH AMERICA & AFRICA HAVE BEEN POSTPONED. NEW DATES TBD |work=Arnolds Sports Festival |accessdate=18 March 2020}}</ref>

On 16 March 2020, Jim Manion, president of the [[IFBB Professional League]] and the [[National Physique Committee]] announced that competitions planned through to 10 May 2020 in the United States would be postponed for later in the year or canceled until the 2021 season.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.ifbbpro.com/npc-news/npc-ifbb-professional-league-president-jim-manion-addresses-coronavirus-concerns-for-contests-in-the-united-states/ |title=NPC & IFBB Professional League President Jim Manion Addresses Coronavirus Concerns For Contests In The United States |work=IFBB Professional League – NPC News Online |accessdate=18 March 2020}}</ref>

==Bowls==
The [[2020 World Outdoor Bowls Championship]] scheduled to be held on the [[Gold Coast, Queensland|Gold Coast]] from 23 May to 7 June 2020,<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.bowls.com.au/events-page/international-events/world-bowls-championships/ |title=2020 World Bowls Championship |publisher=Bowls Australia}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.bowlsmalaysia.com/world-events-calendar/ |title=WORLD EVENTS CALENDAR |publisher=Bowls Malaysia |access-date=20 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200126173721/https://www.bowlsmalaysia.com/world-events-calendar/ |archive-date=26 January 2020 |url-status=dead }}</ref> has been postponed until 25 May to 6 June 2021.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.bowls.com.au/2020-world-bowls-championships-to-be-postponed-indefinitely/ |title=2020 World Bowls Championships to be postponed indefinitely |date=17 March 2020 |website=Bowls Australia |language=en-AU|access-date=18 March 2020}}</ref>

==Castells==
In response to the shutdown of extracurricular activities for children in [[Catalonia]], the Coordinadora de Colles Castelleres de Catalunya (CCCC), the governing body for [[castell]]s (Catalan human towers), issued a statement on 10 March 2020, recommending the suspension of all castells practices and performances.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Muñoz |first1=Silvia |title=Primers assajos i diades castelleres suspeses en prevenció pel coronavirus |url=https://www.elmoncasteller.cat/primers-assajos-i-diades-castelleres-suspeses-en-prevencio-pel-coronavirus/ |accessdate=25 March 2020 |work=Món Casteller |date=10 March 2020}}</ref> Subsequently, the [[COVID-19 pandemic in Spain|lockdown imposed throughout Spain]] shut down all castells activities throughout Catalonia as of 15 March.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Prats |first1=David |title=Segon cap de setmana de confinament casteller |url=http://revistacastells.cat/2020/03/segon-cap-de-setmana-de-confinament-casteller/ |accessdate=25 March 2020 |work=Revista Castells |date=20 March 2020}}</ref> The postponement to 2022 of the [[:ca:XXVIII Concurs de castells de Tarragona|Tarragona Castells Contest]], scheduled for 3 and 4 October 2020, was finally announced on 15 July 2020.<ref>{{cite news |title=La XXVIII edició del Concurs de Castells es trasllada al 2022 |url= https://www.elmoncasteller.cat/la-xxviii-edicio-del-concurs-de-castells-es-trasllada-al-2022/ |accessdate=16 July 2020 |work=Món Casteller |date=15 July 2020}}</ref>

Another major castells festival, the [[:ca:Festes Decennals de la Mare de Déu de la Candela|Festes Decennals de la Mare de Déu de la Candela]], held only once every ten years and scheduled for 29 January-7 February 2021, was also postponed. If it is held in 2022 as tentatively planned, it will be the first time since it was founded in 1791 that it will be held in a year not ending in 1.<ref>{{cite news |title=Valls cancel·la les festes de les Decennals per "responsabilitat" davant la incertesa de la crisi del coronavirus |url= https://www.elmoncasteller.cat/valls-cancella-les-festes-de-les-decennals-per-responsabilitat-davant-la-incertesa-de-la-crisi-del-coronavirus/|accessdate=3 August 2020|work=Món Casteller|date=3 August 2020}}</ref>

According to the CCCC, the last April without any castells was in 1966.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Prats |first1=David |title=Camí d'un abril a zero |url=https://revistacastells.cat/2020/04/cami-dun-abril-a-zero/ |accessdate=4 April 2020 |work=Revista Castells |date=2 April 2020}}</ref>

==Chess==
The [[44th Chess Olympiad]] scheduled to take place in [[Moscow]], [[Russia]] from 5–17 August 2020 was postponed and rescheduled for the summer of 2021.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.fide.com/news/460 |title=Statement by the FIDE Council regarding the Chess Olympiad |date=24 March 2020 |website=fide.com |publisher=FIDE |access-date=24 March 2020}}</ref><ref name="postponed">{{cite web |url=https://www.chess.com/news/view/fide-postpones-chess-olympiad-to-2021 |title=FIDE Postpones Chess Olympiad To 2021 |first=Peter |last=Doggers |date=24 March 2020 |publisher=[[Chess.com]] |access-date=24 March 2020}}</ref>

The FIDE [[Candidates Tournament 2020]], held in [[Yekaterinburg]], [[Russia]], was suspended at the mid-point of the tournament on 26 March. FIDE decided to postpone the second half of the tournament after Russia announced it would be interrupting air traffic with other countries starting on 27 March.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://en.chessbase.com/post/breaking-news-fide-stops-the-candidates-tournament |title=Breaking News: FIDE stops the Candidates Tournament! |date=26 March 2020 |website=Chess News |language=en |access-date=26 March 2020}}</ref>

==Combat sports==
{{split section|Impact of the COVID-19 pandemic on combat sports|date=July 2020}}

===Mixed martial arts===
[[ONE Championship]] moved its 28 February "King of the Jungle" event behind closed doors, and announced that its ONE Infinity 1 event on 10 April would move from [[Chongqing]], China to [[Jakarta]], Indonesia.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.espn.com/mma/story/_/id/28725093/one-championship-card-go-minus-fans-due-coronavirus-fears|title=MMA event to go on sans fans due to coronavirus|date=17 February 2020|website=ESPN.com|language=en|access-date=12 April 2020}}</ref> On 13 March, ONE announced that all cards would be held behind closed doors in Singapore until ONE Infinity 1 on 29 May, re-located to [[Manila]], Philippines (which was originally to host ONE Infinity 2). The ONE Championship "Heart of Heroes" event in [[Vietnam]] (originally scheduled for 20 March) was postponed to June.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.thejakartapost.com/news/2020/03/24/one-championship-goes-ahead-with-events-despite-pandemic.html|title=ONE Championship goes ahead with events despite pandemic|website=The Jakarta Post|language=en|access-date=12 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.straitstimes.com/sport/mma-one-championship-suspends-live-events-until-may-due-to-coronavirus|title=MMA: One Championship suspends live events until May due to coronavirus|last=hermesauto|date=13 March 2020|website=The Straits Times|language=en|access-date=12 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.scmp.com/sport/martial-arts/mixed-martial-arts/article/3075055/coronavirus-one-championship-moves-all-events|title=Coronavirus: One Championship moves all events behind closed doors|date=13 March 2020|website=South China Morning Post|language=en|access-date=12 April 2020}}</ref> On 6 April, due to lockdown orders issued by the Singapore government that restrict non-essential business, ONE announced that the two April cards would be postponed.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.mmafighting.com/2020/4/6/21209252/one-championship-postpones-upcoming-events-in-april-due-to-coronavirus-pandemic|title=ONE Championship postpones upcoming events in April due to coronavirus pandemic|last=Martin|first=Damon|date=6 April 2020|website=MMA Fighting|language=en|access-date=12 April 2020}}</ref>

On 9 March, [[Combate Americas]] announced that its March events would be cancelled and replaced by closed-door tapings beginning 3 April.<ref name=":8" /> On 10 March, Polish MMA promotion [[Konfrontacja Sztuk Walki]] (KSW) cancelled its 21 March 2020 event KSW 53 in [[Łódź]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.fightsports.tv/ksw-cancels-upcoming-event-due-to-coronavirus-outbreak/|title=KSW Cancels Upcoming Event Due To Coronavirus Outbreak|date=11 March 2020|website=FIGHT SPORTS|language=en-US|access-date=13 March 2020}}</ref> On 13 March, [[Bellator MMA|Bellator]] canceled [[Bellator MMA in 2020|Bellator 241]] in [[Uncasville, Connecticut]] (which was scheduled to occur later that day), and has since canceled all events through May.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.sherdog.com/news/news/Bellator-MMA-Changes-Course-Cancels-Bellator-241-171477|title=Bellator MMA Changes Course, Cancels Bellator 241|website=[[Sherdog]]|access-date=12 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.si.com/mma/2020/03/31/bellator-canceled-may-coronavirus-crisis|title=Bellator Cancels Events Through May Amid COVID-19 Outbreak|last=Shapiro|first=Michael|website=Sports Illustrated|language=en-us|access-date=12 April 2020}}</ref>

==== Ultimate Fighting Championship ====
The main North American promotion [[Ultimate Fighting Championship|UFC]] went on with its 13 March event [[UFC Fight Night: Lee vs. Oliveira]] in [[Brasília]], [[Brazil]], behind closed doors.<ref name=":8">{{cite web|url=https://www.espn.com/mma/story/_/id/28873544/ufc-bellator-moving-ahead-events-amid-coronavirus-outbreak|title=UFC, Bellator events still on amid virus outbreak|date=9 March 2020|website=ESPN.com|language=en|access-date=12 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.mmafighting.com/2020/3/12/21176396/ufc-brasilia-behind-closed-doors-coronavirus-decree|title=UFC Brasilia to go on behind closed doors after coronavirus decree|last=Cruz|first=Guilherme|date=12 March 2020|website=MMA Fighting|language=en|access-date=12 April 2020}}</ref> On 16 March, UFC announced that the next three UFC Fight Night events, [[UFC Fight Night: Overeem vs. Harris|Overeem vs. Harris]], [[UFC on ESPN: Ngannou vs. Rozenstruik|Ngannou vs. Rozenstruik]], and [[UFC Fight Night: Woodley vs. Edwards|Woodley vs. Edwards]], would be postponed to future dates.<ref name=":4">{{cite web |url=https://mmajunkie.usatoday.com/2020/03/ufc-postpones-three-events-coronavirus-pandemic |title=UFC postpones three events amid growing coronavirus outbreak |date=16 March 2020 |website=MMA Junkie |language=en|access-date=16 March 2020}}</ref>

In regards to its next [[pay-per-view]], [[UFC 249]] on 18 April, UFC president [[Dana White]] stated that the event would likely go on, but at a new venue behind closed doors. It was originally to be held at New York City's [[Barclays Center]], but a [[stay-at-home order]] was issued by the New York state government.<ref name=":4" /> On 18 March, the [[New York State Athletic Commission]] also withdrew its sanctioning for the event.<ref name=":6" /> Due to international travel restrictions and other withdrawals, a revised card for UFC 249 was unveiled 6 April with a location still being determined.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.espn.com/mma/story/_/id/29002048/dana-white-says-tony-ferguson-justin-gaethje-headline-ufc-249|title=Dana White says Tony Ferguson-Justin Gaethje to headline UFC 249|work=ESPN|first=Marc|last=Raimondi|date=6 April 2020|access-date=7 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.mmafighting.com/2020/4/6/21209211/ufc-announces-updated-lineup-for-ufc-249-andrade-vs-namajunas-2-still-co-headlines|title=UFC 249 fight card announced, Andrade vs. Namajunas 2 still co-headlines|work=MMAFighting.com|first=Alexander K.|last=Lee|date=6 April 2020|access-date=7 April 2020}}</ref> On 7 April, White disclosed that he had booked an unspecified venue for two months, in order to host both UFC 249 and other future events involving U.S. fighters. He also disclosed plans to secure a [[private island]] to host events with international fighters.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.mmafighting.com/2020/4/7/21211634/dana-white-covid-19-plans-weekly-fights-at-ufc-249-location-a-private-island-and-joe-rogan|title=Dana White's COVID-19 plan: Two months of weekly fights at UFC 249 location, a private island, and Joe Rogan|publisher=mmafighting.com|first=Steven|last=Marrocco|date=7 April 2020|access-date=7 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.espn.com/mma/story/_/id/29006529/dana-white-secured-us-location-private-island-ufc-fights|title=UFC's White: Secured private island for fights|date=7 April 2020|website=ESPN.com|language=en|access-date=12 April 2020}}</ref>

The new UFC 249 venue was subsequently revealed to be [[Tachi Palace]]—a [[Native American gaming|tribal casino]] in [[Lemoore, California]]; as it is on tribal land, it also fell outside of the jurisdiction of the [[California State Athletic Commission]], meaning that events held there could be self-sanctioned.<ref name=":6">{{Cite news|last=Draper|first=Kevin|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2020/04/07/sports/ufc-249-coronavirus-location.html|title=U.F.C. 249, Skirting Coronavirus Limits, Is Set for Tribal Land in California|date=7 April 2020|work=The New York Times|access-date=12 April 2020|language=en-US|issn=0362-4331}}</ref> On 9 April, UFC announced that UFC 249 had been canceled, and all other UFC events would be suspended until further notice. White cited interventions from high-ranking staff of the UFC's U.S. media rightsholders, [[ESPN Inc.]] and parent [[The Walt Disney Company]].<ref name=":5" /> ''[[The New York Post]]'' reported that Governor of California [[Gavin Newsom]] had contacted Disney chairman and former CEO [[Bob Iger]], urging ESPN and the UFC to not hold the event.<ref name=":7" /> Despite the cancellation, White stated that he was still going on with his "Fight Island" project.<ref name=":5">{{Cite news|last1=Draper|first1=Kevin|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2020/04/09/sports/ufc-249-canceled.html|title=U.F.C. 249 Is Off After Requests From California, Disney and ESPN|date=9 April 2020|work=The New York Times|access-date=12 April 2020|last2=Garcia|first2=Oskar|language=en-US|issn=0362-4331}}</ref><ref name=":7">{{cite web|url=https://nypost.com/2020/04/09/ufc-249-espn-wasnt-only-one-to-tell-dana-white-to-stand-down/|title=ESPN wasn't only one to tell UFC, Dana White to 'stand down'|last=Willis|first=George|date=10 April 2020|website=New York Post|language=en|access-date=12 April 2020}}</ref>

The UFC later announced on 24 April that it would resume its events with a series of three cards held behind closed doors at the [[VyStar Veterans Memorial Arena]] in [[Jacksonville, Florida]], beginning with [[UFC 249 (May 9, 2020 event)|UFC 249]] on 9 May, along with two other cards on 13 May ([[UFC Fight Night: Smith vs. Teixeira]]) and 16 May ([[UFC on ESPN: Overeem vs. Harris]]). Florida had recently exempted sporting events held behind closed doors for a national audience from its stay-at-home order. White also announced a planned card at an undetermined location on 23 May, and plans to begin events at his "[[Fight Island]]" in June.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.espn.com/mma/story/_/id/29094417/ufc-schedules-three-fight-cards-led-ufc-249-9-florida-no-fans|title=UFC returns May 9 with first of 3 cards in Florida|date=24 April 2020|website=ESPN.com|language=en|access-date=24 April 2020}}</ref> The [[Nevada Athletic Commission]] approved the hosting of [[UFC on ESPN: Woodley vs. Burns]] on 30 May, and [[UFC 250]] on 6 June, both at the company's UFC Apex facility in [[Las Vegas]].<ref>{{Cite web|title=UFC 250 among 4 fight cards approved for Vegas|url=https://www.espn.com/mma/story/_/id/29230313/nsac-approves-upcoming-ufc-boxing-events-vegas|date=27 May 2020|website=ESPN.com|language=en|access-date=28 May 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|title=Las Vegas Coming Back To Life, As State Approves UFC Events, Boxing Matches And Casinos For Reopening Dates|url=https://deadline.com/2020/05/las-vegas-reopening-ufc-top_rank-casinos-1202945044/|last=Haring|first=Bruce|date=28 May 2020|website=Deadline|language=en|access-date=28 May 2020}}</ref>

On 9 June, White revealed that the "Fight Island" venue was [[Yas Island]] in [[Abu Dhabi]], [[United Arab Emirates]], which hosted [[UFC 251]] on 11 July and will host three other UFC Fight Night cards. The area includes accommodations and training facilities, and a {{convert|10|sqmi|km2|adj=on}} area restricted to fighters, coaches, and UFC staff.<ref>{{Cite web|date=9 June 2020|title=White: Fight Island is in UAE, will host UFC 251|url=https://www.espn.com/mma/story/_/id/29287612/ufc-fight-island-host-events-next-month|access-date=9 June 2020|website=ESPN.com|language=en}}</ref>

===Kickboxing===
[[Kunlun Fight]] cancelled multiple events due to the [[COVID-19 pandemic]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.ecosports.cn/Home/Consultation/show/id/14744.html |title=首页 氪体 |publisher=Ecosports.cn |date=26 January 2020 |accessdate=11 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.kunlunjue.com/articleDetail?id=6060 |title=昆仑决世界格斗冠军赛 |publisher=Kunlunjue.com |date= |accessdate=11 April 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200410193703/https://www.kunlunjue.com/articleDetail%3Fid%3D6060 |archive-date=10 April 2020 |url-status=dead }}</ref>

[[Glory (kickboxing)|Glory]] cancelled events in [[Lint, Belgium|Lint]], Belgium and [[Miami]], Florida.<ref>{{cite web|last=Sports |first=Fight |url=https://www.fightsports.tv/glory-kickboxing-postpones-antwerp-miami-events/ |title=GLORY Kickboxing Postpones Antwerp, Miami Events &#124; FIGHT SPORTS |publisher=Fightsports.tv |date=12 March 2020 |accessdate=11 April 2020}}</ref>

===Professional wrestling===
Numerous [[Professional wrestling promotion|promotions]] have canceled major events, such as [[Impact Wrestling]]'s [[TNA: There's No Place Like Home]], [[Ring of Honor]]'s [[ROH 18th Anniversary Show|18th Anniversary Show]], and the [[National Wrestling Alliance]]'s [[Crockett Cup (2020)|Crockett Cup]] in the United States.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.rohwrestling.com/news/roh-18th-anniversary-and-past-vs-present-shows-cancellation|title=ROH 18TH ANNIVERSARY AND PAST VS PRESENT SHOWS CANCELLATION|date=12 March 2020|website=Ring of Honor|language=en|access-date=13 March 2020}}</ref> Impact, ROH, and NWA also cancelled future tapings for their respective weekly television shows until further notice.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://impactwrestling.com/our-response-to-covid-19/|title=An Update on Events|date=24 March 2020|website=Impact Wrestling|language=en|access-date=27 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.rohwrestling.com/news/roh-cancels-all-live-events-through-may-31st-2020|title=ROH 18TH ROH CANCELS ALL LIVE EVENTS THROUGH MAY 31ST, 2020|date=17 March 2020|website=Ring of Honor|language=en|access-date=23 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.nationalwrestlingalliance.com/news/nwa-suspends-crockett-cup-amp-nwa-powerrr-live-events|title=NWA SUSPENDS CROCKETT CUP & NWA POWERRR LIVE EVENTS|website=NWA|language=en-US|access-date=17 March 2020}}</ref> In Mexico, [[Consejo Mundial de Lucha Libre]] cancelled tapings for their weekly shows for the foreseeable future and [[Lucha Libre AAA Worldwide]] postponed the [[Rey de Reyes (2020)|2020 Rey de Reyes]] event.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://superluchas.com/funciones-canceladas-por-coronavirus-en-mexico/|title=Primeras funciones canceladas por Coronavirus en México|last=Acosta|first=Carlos|date=13 March 2020|work=[[Súper Luchas]]|language=Spanish|accessdate=14 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://superluchas.com/aaa-se-cancela-rey-de-reyes-2020-por-coronavirus/|title=AAA: Se cancela "Rey de Reyes 2020" por Coronavirus|last=Acosta|first=Carlos|date=13 March 2020|work=[[Súper Luchas]]|language=Spanish|trans-title=AAA: Cancelling "Rey de Reyes 2020" because of the Coronavirus|accessdate=14 March 2020}}</ref> In Japan, [[DDT Pro-Wrestling]] cancelled their marquee event [[DDT Peter Pan|Wrestle Peter Pan 2020]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://411mania.com/wrestling/ddt-pro-wrestling-cancels-wrestle-peter-pan-2020-event/|title=DDT Pro Wrestling Cancels Wrestle Peter Pan 2020 Event|date=23 April 2020|website=411Mania|language=en|access-date=14 May 2020}}</ref>

====New Japan Pro-Wrestling====
In accordance with recommendations from the Japanese Ministry of Health, [[New Japan Pro-Wrestling]] (NJPW) decided to cancel all scheduled shows from 1 March through 15 March.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.f4wonline.com/new-japan-news/njpw-cancels-shows-march-1-15-due-coronavirus-outbreak-305026 |title=NJPW CANCELS SHOWS FROM MARCH 1–15 DUE TO CORONAVIRUS OUTBREAK |first=Joseph |last=Currier |date=26 February 2020 |accessdate=14 March 2020 |work=[[Wrestling Observer Newsletter]]}}</ref> On 10 March, NJPW announced that they were cancelling all shows through 22 March, and postponed most notably the [[New Japan Cup#2020|2020 New Japan Cup]].<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.f4wonline.com/new-japan-news/njpw-cancels-remainder-new-japan-cup-tour-due-coronavirus-306136 |title=NJPW CANCELS REMAINDER OF NEW JAPAN CUP TOUR DUE TO CORONAVIRUS |first=Brian |last=Rose |date=10 March 2020 |accessdate=14 March 2020 |work=[[Wrestling Observer Newsletter]]}}</ref> The [[World Wonder Ring Stardom|Stardom]] promotion, sister company of NJPW also owned by [[Bushiroad]], also made adjustments to their scheduled, cancelling shows from 19 February to 14 March. Their show of 8 March in [[Korakuen Hall]] was held without any spectators in attendance, instead streaming live on their [[YouTube]] channel.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.f4wonline.com/japan/stardom-makes-major-schedule-changes-due-coronavirus-outbreak-304441 |title=STARDOM MAKES MAJOR SCHEDULE CHANGES DUE TO CORONAVIRUS OUTBREAK |first=Josh |last=Nason |date=18 February 2020 |accessdate=14 March 2020 |work=[[Wrestling Observer Newsletter]]}}</ref> On 23 March, NJPW would later cancel the 2020 [[Sakura Genesis]] event that was originally scheduled to take place on 31 March.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.njpw1972.com/tornament/68654 |title=2020.03.31 SAKURA GENESIS 2020 |accessdate=28 December 2019 |work=[[New Japan Pro-Wrestling]] |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20191227133137/https://www.njpw1972.com/tornament/68654 |archive-date=27 December 2019 |url-status=dead }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.njpw1972.com/73631 |title=Sakura Genesis, April 11 Kanagawa events cancelled |accessdate=23 March 2020 | work=[[New Japan Pro-Wrestling]]}}</ref> On 8 April, NJPW would cancel more events from 11 April through 4 May, including the entire [[Wrestling Dontaku]], which was not rescheduled.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.f4wonline.com/new-japan-news/njpw-cancels-events-through-may-4-wrestling-dontaku-included-308401 |title=NJPW cancels events through May 4, Wrestling Dontaku included |publisher=F4wonline.com |date=7 April 2020 |accessdate=11 April 2020}}</ref> On 6 May, NJPW cancelled their annual [[Best of the Super Juniors]] tournament.<ref>{{Cite web|title=Best of the Super Junior 27 Tour Events Cancelled {{!}} NEW JAPAN PRO-WRESTLING|url=https://www.njpw1972.com/74453|last=NJPW|website=NJPW|language=en|access-date=8 May 2020}}</ref> The next day, NJPW postponed their Wrestle Dynasty event to 2021, which was to take place in [[Madison Square Garden]] in New York.<ref>{{Cite web|title=Wrestle Dynasty postponed to 2021 【NJoA】【WD1】 {{!}} NEW JAPAN PRO-WRESTLING|url=https://www.njpw1972.com/74418|last=NJPW|website=NJPW|language=en|access-date=8 May 2020}}</ref> On 9 June, NJPW announced their return with special show with a mystery match card called ''Together Special'' on 15 June and the rescheduled New Japan Cup would now be held from 16 June until 11 July, with the finals being held at [[Osaka-jō Hall]] in [[Osaka]] alongside [[Dominion in Osaka-jo Hall (2020)|Dominion in Osaka-jo Hall]] being rescheduled to 12 July 2020.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.njpw1972.com/75303|title=New Japan Cup 2020 a NJPW World Special this June! {{!}} NEW JAPAN PRO-WRESTLING|last=NJPW|website=NJPW|language=en|access-date=9 June 2020}}</ref><ref name="dominion">{{Cite web|url=https://www.njpw1972.com/75361|title=NJPW welcomes the fans back to Osaka Jo Hall July 11 & 12! {{!}} NEW JAPAN PRO-WRESTLING|last=NJPW|website=NJPW|language=en|access-date=9 June 2020}}</ref>

====WWE====
American promotion [[WWE]] began to move the broadcasts of its weekly programs ''[[WWE SmackDown|SmackDown]]'' and ''[[WWE Raw|Raw]]'' (which usually broadcast from arenas) behind closed doors to its [[Orlando]] [[Wrestling school|training facility]], the [[WWE Performance Center]], beginning with ''SmackDown'' on 13 March, with no audience and only essential staff in attendance.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.cbssports.com/wwe/news/wwe-raw-results-recap-grades-steve-austin-celebrates-new-wrestlemania-36-matches-made/live/ |title=WWE Raw results, recap, grades: Steve Austin celebrates, new WrestleMania 36 matches made |website=CBSSports.com |language=en|access-date=17 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://variety.com/2020/tv/news/coronavirus-wwe-smackdown-live-1203532469/ |title=WWE Moves 'SmackDown Live' to Orlando Performance Center With No Live Audience Due to Coronavirus |last=Otterson |first=Joe |date=12 March 2020 |website=Variety|access-date=12 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.cbssports.com/wwe/news/wwe-smackdown-results-recap-grades-john-cena-caps-surreal-empty-arena-showy-you-have-to-see/live/ |title=WWE SmackDown results, recap, grades: John Cena caps surreal empty arena show you have to see |website=CBSSports.com|access-date=14 March 2020}}</ref> The promotion also postponed some of its upcoming [[house show]]s.<ref name=":0">{{cite web |url=http://slam.canoe.com/Slam/Wrestling/2020/03/13/22805585.html |title=WWE house shows cancelled, AEW alters plans |website=canoe.com|access-date=15 March 2020}}</ref>

[[WrestleMania 36]]—WWE's flagship [[pay-per-view]] event—was originally scheduled to be held at [[Raymond James Stadium]] in [[Tampa, Florida|Tampa]]. On 16 March, WWE announced that it would also be produced from the Performance Center and air across two nights (4 and 5 April).<ref>{{cite web |url=https://deadline.com/2020/03/wrestlemania-canceled-coronavirus-wwe-tampa-1202881422/ |title=WrestleMania To Stream Live Without Audience Due To Coronavirus Outbreak |last=Ramos |first=Dino-Ray |date=16 March 2020 |website=Deadline |language=en|access-date=17 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.thewrap.com/wwe-splits-audience-less-wrestlemania-36-into-two-nights/ |title=WWE Splits Audience-Less WrestleMania 36 Into Two Nights |last=Maglio |first=Tony |date=18 March 2020 |website=TheWrap |language=en-US|access-date=18 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.wwe.com/shows/wrestlemania/wrestlemania-36/article/wrestlemania-36-two-night-wwe-network-rob-gronkowski-host |title=Unprecedented two-night WrestleMania to be hosted by Rob Gronkowski on WWE Network |date=17 March 2020 |work=WWE |accessdate=17 March 2020}}</ref> WrestleMania Weekend's associated events, such as the [[NXT TakeOver: Tampa Bay]] [[Card (sports)|card]] (which was scheduled for [[Amalie Arena]]) and [[WWE Hall of Fame]] induction ceremony were also postponed to unannounced dates, though TakeOver was ultimately canceled with its planned matches moved to weekly episodes of ''[[WWE NXT|NXT]]''.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.pwinsider.com/article/134766/wwe-hall-of-fame-nxt-takeover-off.html?p=1 |title=WWE HALL OF FAME, NXT TAKEOVER OFF |work=PW Insider |first=Mike |last=Johnson |date=16 March 2020 |accessdate=16 March 2020}}</ref> Matches for WrestleMania, as well as the final two episodes of ''SmackDown'' and final episode of ''Raw'' before WrestleMania, were recorded in advance at the Performance Center between 21 and 26 March.<ref name="taped">{{cite web |url=https://www.pwinsider.com/article/134908/wwe-scheduled-to-tape-everything-through-wrestlemania-this-week.html?p=1 |title=WWE SCHEDULED TO TAPE EVERYTHING THROUGH WRESTLEMANIA THIS WEEK |last=Johnson |first=Mike |date=21 March 2020 |publisher=PWInsider |accessdate=21 March 2020}}</ref> While the majority of matches were filmed in Performance Center arena and presented plausibly live, two matches were filmed off-site in different, cinematic styles.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.tvguide.com/news/wwe-triple-h-wrestlemania-coronavirus-impact/ |title=WWE's Triple H Explains What It's Like to Film WrestleMania Without the Fans |date=2 April 2020 |website=TVGuide.com|access-date=4 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.cbssports.com/wwe/news/wwe-wrestlemania-36-results-recap-grades-huge-title-changes-epic-special-matches-on-unique-2020-show/live/|title=WWE WrestleMania 36 results, recap, grades: Huge title changes, epic special matches on unique 2020 show|website=CBSSports.com|language=en|access-date=6 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.prowrestlingsheet.com/john-cena-bray-wyatt-firefly-fun-house-win-wrestlemania/|title=Bray Wyatt Defeats John Cena in Firefly Fun House Match at WrestleMania|last=Satin|first=Ryan|date=6 April 2020|website=Pro Wrestling Sheet {{!}} Insider Wrestling News and Reports|language=en-US|access-date=6 April 2020}}</ref>

After continuing with pre-taped episodes for the [[go-home show]]s after WrestleMania, WWE announced that its weekly series would resume live broadcasts on 13 April, with ''Raw'' and ''SmackDown'' from the Performance Center as before, and ''NXT'' taped from its existing studio at [[Full Sail University]] in [[Winter Park, Florida|Winter Park]].<ref name="cbs-wwelive">{{cite web|url=https://www.cbssports.com/wwe/news/wwe-to-resume-live-matches-on-tv-starting-with-the-next-monday-night-raw/|title=WWE to resume live matches on TV starting with the next 'Monday Night Raw'|website=CBSSports.com|language=en|access-date=13 April 2020}}</ref><ref name=":9">{{cite web|url=https://www.espn.com/wwe/story/_/id/29024319/wwe-resume-live-tv-matches-starting-monday|title=WWE to resume live TV matches starting Monday|date=11 April 2020|website=ESPN.com|language=en|access-date=13 April 2020}}</ref> WWE told ESPN that "it is now more important than ever to provide people with a diversion from these hard times", and that its programming "bring[s] families together and deliver a sense of hope, determination and perseverance".<ref name=":9" /> WWE also confirmed that one of its employees had contracted COVID-19 after a meeting with two health care workers on 26 March, but that the exposure occurred after production had wrapped; the employee had not made any contact with WWE staff since and they made a complete recovery.<ref name=":9" /><ref>{{cite web|url=https://deadline.com/2020/04/wwe-confirms-coronavirus-case-1202906432/|title=WWE Confirms First Known Coronavirus Case|last=Bennett|first=Anita|date=12 April 2020|website=Deadline|language=en|access-date=13 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.prowrestlingsheet.com/wwe-positive-covid-19-test-confirmed/|title=Positive COVID-19 Test Confirmed by WWE|last=Satin|first=Ryan|date=11 April 2020|website=Pro Wrestling Sheet|language=en-US|access-date=13 April 2020}}</ref> Wrestling journalists [[Dave Meltzer]] noted that WWE's television contracts with [[Fox Broadcasting Company|Fox]] and [[USA Network]] likely restricted the number of non-live episodes it could broadcast per-year (accommodating breaks in live broadcasts usually held around the [[Christmas]] and [[New Year]] holidays).<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.f4wonline.com/wwe-news/wwe-resume-live-raw-smackdown-nxt-tv-shows-308611|title=WWE to resume live Raw, SmackDown & NXT TV shows|date=10 April 2020|website=WON/F4W|language=en|access-date=13 April 2020}}</ref>

WWE's next PPV, [[Money in the Bank (2020)|Money in the Bank]], was expected to be held at [[Baltimore]]'s [[Royal Farms Arena]] in May, but was canceled by the arena on 9 April.<ref>{{cite web|last=Johnson|first=Mike|title=WWE MONEY IN THE BANK WILL NOT TAKE PLACE IN BALTIMORE, ROYAL FARMS ARENA ANNOUNCES CANCELLATION|url=https://www.pwinsider.com/article/135465/wwe-money-in-the-bank-will-not-take-place-in-baltimore-royal-farms-arena-announces-cancellation.html?p=1|work=PWInsider|date=9 April 2020|access-date=9 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|last=Wilen|first=Jerome|title=WWE Money in the Bank pay-per view canceled due to COVID-19 outbreak|url=https://www.wrestleview.com/wwe-news/153495-wwe-money-in-the-bank-pay-per-view-canceled-covid-19/|work=WrestleView|date=9 April 2020|access-date=9 April 2020}}</ref> On 17 April, WWE announced that the show's [[Money in the Bank ladder match|eponymous Money in the Bank matches]] (where wrestlers compete to retrieve a [[briefcase]] suspended above the ring with a [[Ladder match|ladder]], containing a contract granting rights to challenge one of WWE's world championships at any point within the next year) would take place at its [[Titan Towers|world headquarters building]] in [[Stamford, Connecticut]], with a new "[[Career ladder|corporate ladder]]" gimmick where the briefcases would be suspended above a ring on the building's roof; the wrestlers began on the ground floor of the building and fought their way to the roof. The rest of the event occurred live at the Performance Center.<ref name=MOVED>{{cite web|url=https://www.cbssports.com/wwe/news/wwe-smackdown-results-live-recap-grades-as-tag-title-match-money-in-the-bank-qualifiers-highlight/live/|title=WWE SmackDown results: Live recap, grades as tag title match, Money in the Bank qualifiers highlight|date=17 April 2020|accessdate=17 April 2020|work=[[CBS Sports]]|author=Brookhouse, Brent}}</ref>

On 9 April, Florida's Division of Emergency Management added an exemption to the state stay-at-home order for employees of a "professional sports and media production with a national audience", if closed to the general public.<ref name="tampabaytimes-littlecontent">{{cite web|url=https://tampabay.com/news/health/2020/04/14/in-defense-of-wwe-decision-ron-desantis-said-he-wants-more-sporting-events/|title='Starved for content': Ron DeSantis explains why sporting events are needed now|website=Tampa Bay Times|language=en|access-date=16 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://thehill.com/homenews/state-watch/492894-desantis-defends-labeling-wwe-sporting-events-essential-people-are|title=DeSantis defends labeling WWE, sporting events 'essential': 'People are starved for content'|last=Wise|first=Justin|date=15 April 2020|website=The Hill|language=en|access-date=16 April 2020}}</ref> On 13 April, Mayor of [[Orange County, Florida|Orange County]] [[Jerry Demings]] acknowledged the change during a news conference, stating that they were made following consultations with the office of Governor of Florida [[Ron DeSantis]], and that they would allow WWE to continue its operations.<ref name=":10">{{Cite news|last=Zaveri|first=Mihir|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2020/04/14/us/wwe-essential-business-florida-coronavirus.html|title=The WWE Is Now Considered an 'Essential Service' in Florida|date=14 April 2020|work=The New York Times|access-date=15 April 2020|language=en-US|issn=0362-4331}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.cbssports.com/wwe/news/wwe-to-resume-live-tv-tapings-after-being-deemed-essential-business-by-florida-governors-office/|title=WWE to resume live TV tapings after being deemed 'essential business' by Florida governor's office|website=CBSSports.com|language=en|access-date=15 April 2020}}</ref> It was reported that WWE had received repeated warnings by state officials over the stay-at-home order, but that DeSantis considered the operation critical to the state economy, and accommodated them by allowing the aforementioned changes.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://slam.canoe.com/Slam/Wrestling/2020/04/14/22806307.html|title=Florida media: WWE was warned before, Linda McMahon promised millions to Florida|website=canoe.com|access-date=15 April 2020}}</ref><ref name=":10" />

DeSantis acknowledged the changes the next day, explaining that viewers were "starved" for sports content, and that the new exception could also be theoretically used by other sporting events.<ref name="tampabaytimes-littlecontent" /> The same day, U.S. president [[Donald Trump]] announced that he was forming an economic advisory group to address the country's emergence and "reopening" from the pandemic; WWE owner and chairman [[Vince McMahon]] was named to the group (alongside other major sports commissioners and team owners). McMahon has been an ally of Trump, who has also made appearances on WWE programming in the past, and is also a member of the celebrity wing of the company's [[WWE Hall of Fame|Hall of Fame]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.cbssports.com/nfl/news/donald-trump-tired-of-watching-old-games-adds-team-owners-dana-white-vince-mcmahon-to-advisory-group/|title=Donald Trump 'tired of watching old games,' adds team owners, Dana White, Vince McMahon to advisory group|website=CBSSports.com|language=en|access-date=15 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2020/04/15/business/dealbook/coronavirus-trump-reopening-ceo-council.html|title=Who Tells Trump When to Restart the Economy|date=15 April 2020|work=The New York Times|access-date=15 April 2020|language=en-US|issn=0362-4331}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|last=Lutz|first=Tom|url=https://www.theguardian.com/sport/2020/apr/15/donald-trump-sports-reopen-coronavirus-shutdown|title='We have to get our sports back': Trump says he is sick of watching baseball repeats|date=15 April 2020|work=The Guardian|access-date=15 April 2020|language=en-GB|issn=0261-3077}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.orlandosentinel.com/coronavirus/os-sp-coronavirus-wwe-mike-bianchi-0415-20200415-akmmkzmfazfdbgzmvrakhu37ci-story.html|title=Is WWE Hall-of-Famer Donald Trump why pro wrestling is an 'essential business' in Florida?|last=Bianchi|first=Mike|website=Orlando Sentinel|access-date=15 April 2020}}</ref>

On 28 August, WWE moved its weekly ''Raw'' and ''SmackDown'' shows, as well as pay-per-views, to the [[Amway Center]] which is also in Orlando. The centerpiece of the new setup is "ThunderDome," an in-arena staging incorporating a virtual audience and larger-scale arena show.<ref>{{Cite news|last=Satin|first=Ryan|url=https://www.prowrestlingsheet.com/wwe-thunderdome-amway-center-virtual-fan-wall/#.Xzq5wDV7nIU|title=Details on "WWE ThunderDome" Amway Center Residency with Virtual Fan Wall|date=17 August 2020|work=Pro Wrestling Sheet|access-date=5 September 2020|language=en-US}}</ref> In October 2020, NXT re-located to the Performance Center from Full Sail University, using a remodeled main arena adding a virtual audience (similar to the ThunderDome staging) alongside limited in-person attendance,<ref>{{Cite web|last=Barrasso|first=Justin|title=NXT Unveiling the Capitol Wrestling Center at Sunday’s TakeOver 31|url=https://www.si.com/wrestling/2020/10/04/nxt-unveiling-capitol-wrestling-center|access-date=30 October 2020|website=Sports Illustrated|language=en-us}}</ref> which is called "Capitol Wrestling Center."

As of 11 December, the ThunderDome set is to be relocated to [[Tropicana Field]] in [[St. Petersburg, Florida]], as WWE must vacate Amway Center to make room for its professional sports co-tenants.<ref>{{Cite news|last=|first=|url=https://www.wwe.com/shows/raw/article/wwe-thunderdome-will-head-to-tampa-bays-tropicana-field-beginning-friday-dec-11|title=WWE ThunderDome will head to Tampa Bay's Tropicana Field beginning Friday, Dec. 11|date=19 November 2020|work=WWE.com|access-date=3 December 2020|language=en-US}}</ref>

====All Elite Wrestling====
On 12 March, [[All Elite Wrestling]] (AEW) announced the relocation of its two remaining live broadcasts of ''[[AEW Dynamite|Dynamite]]'' on [[TNT (American TV network)|TNT]] for the month of March, scheduled for [[Rochester, New York]] and [[Newark, New Jersey]] respectively (with the latter originally scheduled to feature AEW's "[[AEW Blood and Guts|Blood and Guts]]" event, also indefinitely postponed),<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.allelitewrestling.com/post/message-from-aew-president-ceo-tony-khan |title=Message From AEW President & CEO Tony Khan |date=21 March 2020 |website=All Elite Wrestling |language=en|access-date=5 April 2020}}</ref> to an alternative location with no audience. AEW stated that it had re-booked the two cities for future episodes in July.<ref name=":0" /><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.cbr.com/aew-dynamite-coronavirus-venue-changes/ |title=AEW Announces Venue Changes, Including Blood & Guts Show, Due to COVID-19 |date=13 March 2020 |website=CBR |language=en-US|access-date=15 March 2020}}</ref>  AEW subsequently cancelled on-location ''Dynamite'' broadcasts through at least 13 May.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://prowrestling.net/site/2020/03/23/aew-postpones-additional-events-still-planning-to-air-dynamite/ |title=AEW postpones additional events, still planning to air Dynamite |date=23 March 2020 |website=Pro Wrestling Dot Net |language=en-US|access-date=5 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://prowrestling.net/site/2020/03/13/aew-announces-additional-postponements-of-dynamite-events/ |title=AEW announces additional postponements of Dynamite events |date=13 March 2020 |website=Pro Wrestling Dot Net |language=en-US|access-date=5 April 2020}}</ref>

Beginning on 15 March, AEW began to originate ''Dynamite'' from a closed stage at [[TIAA Bank Field]]'s [[Daily's Place]] amphitheater in [[Jacksonville, Florida]].<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.news4jax.com/news/local/2020/03/13/aew-moves-show-from-rochester-to-jacksonville-due-to-coronavirus/ |title=AEW moves show from Rochester to Jacksonville due to coronavirus |last=Mealey |first=Jason |date=13 March 2020 |website=WJXT |language=en|access-date=22 March 2020}}</ref> Beginning with 1 April episode, ''Dynamite'' moved to an undisclosed location to prevent fans from attempting to interact with the wrestlers;<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.f4wonline.com/aew-news/aew-filming-dynamite-dark-undisclosed-location-307786 |title=AEW filming Dynamite & Dark in undisclosed location |date=31 March 2020 |website=WON/F4W |language=en|access-date=5 April 2020}}</ref> the location was later reported to be in [[Norcross, Georgia]]. On 3 April, after a state-wide stay-at-home order was issued, it was reported that AEW had also pre-recorded content for ''Dynamite'' on 1 and 2 April, and that they had amassed enough content "for weeks if not months if necessary."<ref>{{cite web |url=https://prowrestling.net/site/2020/04/03/aew-taped-weeks-of-television-georgia-state-official-attended-this-weeks-taping/ |title=AEW taped weeks of television, Georgia state official attended this week's taping |last=Papaleo |first=Dennis |date=3 April 2020 |website=Pro Wrestling Dot Net |language=en-US|access-date=5 April 2020}}</ref>

AEW's next pay-per-view event, [[Double or Nothing (2020)|Double or Nothing]], was originally scheduled to take place at the [[MGM Grand Garden Arena]] in [[Paradise, Nevada]] on 23 May. The venue, however, canceled all events up through 31 May due to the pandemic.<ref name="MGMcancelation">{{cite web|url=https://411mania.com/wrestling/aew-double-or-nothing-venue-shut-down-until-further-notice/|title=AEW Double Or Nothing Venue Shut Down Until Further Notice|date=9 April 2020|last=Thomas|first=Jeremy|work=411mania|accessdate=10 April 2020}}</ref> The event was subsequently moved to Daily's Place (with nearby [[TIAA Bank Field]] hosting a deliberate [[Empty arena match|empty arena]] "Stadium Stampede" match).<ref>{{Cite web|title=2020 AEW Double or Nothing results, recap, grades: Stadium Stampede chaos, two new champions highlight|url=https://www.cbssports.com/wwe/news/2020-aew-double-or-nothing-results-results-recap-grades-stadium-stampede-chaos-two-new-champions-highlight/live/|website=CBSSports.com|language=en|access-date=24 May 2020}}</ref>

On 27 August, AEW began to hold events with spectators, again at Daily's Place.  These events are ticketed and will carry between 10%-15% capacity.

===Sumo===
Despite the March ''[[honbasho]]'' in [[Osaka]] taking place behind closed doors without a hitch, bar one wrestler ([[Chiyomaru]]) having temporarily withdrawn from the tournament with a fever whilst undergoing tests; both the Natsu ''honbasho'' in May and Nagoya ''honbasho'' in July were initially postponed by two weeks on 4 April. The July tournament had been previously moved forward a week to avoid conflict with the 2020 Olympics in Tokyo, which have since been postponed a year.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://mainichi.jp/english/articles/20200317/p2g/00m/0sp/107000c|title=Sumo: Hakuho suffers upset, falls into 2-way tie for lead on Day 10|date=17 March 2020|work=The Mainichi|accessdate=17 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200318170848/https://mainichi.jp/english/articles/20200317/p2g/00m/0sp/107000c|archive-date=18 March 2020|url-status=dead}}</ref><ref name=kyodopostpone>{{cite web|url=https://english.kyodonews.net/news/2020/04/e6a03e47c65f-breaking-news-grand-sumo-tournament-in-may-to-be-postponed-2-weeks-due-to-virus.html |title=May Sumo tournament to be postponed 2 weeks due to virus |publisher=English.kyodonews.net |date= |accessdate=6 April 2020}}</ref>

A week later, the [[Japan Sumo Association]] confirmed the sport's first case when an undisclosed wrestler in the lower ranks, was tested positive after developing a fever some six days earlier. This led to all wrestlers and officials being ordered to stay indoor until further notice.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://english.kyodonews.net/news/2020/04/d25d0f1d5acb-breaking-news-1st-sumo-wrestler-tests-positive-for-coronavirus.html|title=1st sumo wrestler tests positive for coronavirus
|author=<!--Not stated--> |date=10 April 2020|website=english.kyodonews.net|publisher=Kyodo|access-date=10 April 2020}}</ref>

Following the extension of Japan's national state of emergency until 31 May, the Sumo Association officially cancelled the [[2020 in sumo#Natsu basho|May Grand Sumo Tournament]] on 4 May. It is the second cancellation of a ''honbasho'' since 1946, and the first since March 2011 amidst a [[Match-fixing in professional sumo#2011 investigation|match-fixing scandal]].<ref name=kyodo04May2020>{{cite web |url=https://english.kyodonews.net/news/2020/05/496ae3514a37-urgent-sumo-grand-tournament-in-may-canceled-due-to-virus.html|title=Sumo grand tournament in May canceled due to virus|date=4 May 2020|website=english.kyodonews.net|publisher=Kyodo|access-date=4 May 2020}}</ref>

The wrestler who caught the virus was later confirmed to be the ''Sandanme'' 11 wrestler [[Shobushi]] of [[Takadagawa stable]], who passed away from multiple organ failure on 13 May.<ref name=kyodo130520A>{{cite web |url=https://english.kyodonews.net/news/2020/05/2710c4489399-breaking-news-sumo-wrestler-dies-after-being-infected-with-new-coronavirus.html|title=28-year-old sumo wrestler dies after coronavirus infection
|author=<!--Not stated--> |date=13 May 2020|website=english.kyodonews.net|publisher=Kyodo|access-date=13 May 2020}}</ref>

The July tournament, originally to be held in [[Nagoya]], was moved to Tokyo and began on 19 July, with a maximum of 2500 spectators per day allowed, about a quarter of the [[Ryōgoku Kokugikan]]'s 11,000 capacity.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.newsweek.com/japan-coronavirus-sumo-tournament-1518886|title=Japan Holds Sumo Tournament After Praying For Success Amid Coronavirus Risk|date=19 July 2020|work=Newsweek|accessdate=21 July 2020}}</ref>

===General issues===
An October 2020 story by [[ESPN]] journalist Marc Raimondi made the case that combat sports face long-lasting negative effects from the pandemic. While many top-flight competitions and promotions have returned to operation, Raimondi pointed out,{{blockquote|The coronavirus pandemic has ravaged the regional and local scenes in combat sports, doing untold damage to the long-term future of MMA, boxing and professional wrestling. The next [[Floyd Mayweather Jr.|Floyd Mayweather]] or [[Conor McGregor]] has probably not fought in 2020. Many athletes cannot even train with consistency due to gym closures. The combat-sports pipeline -- from amateur to prospect to contender to superstar -- has cracked, and stakeholders aren't sure how or when it will be fully repaired.<ref name=Raimondi>{{cite web|url=https://www.espn.com/mma/story/_/id/30056977/how-combat-sports-pipeline-broke-2020 |title='It's a real problem': How the combat sports pipeline broke in 2020 |first=Marc |last=Raimondi |website=ESPN.com |date=October 7, 2020 |accessdate=October 8, 2020}}</ref>
}}
The ''Tapology'' website, which tracks MMA fights worldwide, reported that the worldwide number of sanctioned MMA fights dropped by over 80% from 2019 to 2020, as measured from 1 March to 1 September of each year. The U.S. saw an even greater drop in total fights during that time frame. During the March–September 2019 period, [[Zuffa]], the parent company of UFC, accounted for 4.4% of U.S. MMA fights. The company was responsible for more than 20% of U.S. MMA fights during the same period in 2020—despite only running [[UFC 248|one event]] in the country in March, April, or July. Boxing also saw slightly less dramatic declines in the same period; the ''BoxRec'' website reported a drop in total bouts of over 65% worldwide and over 55% in the U.S.<ref name=Raimondi/>

==Cricket==
