== Cross-country skiing ==

===2019–20 FIS Cross-Country World Cup===

The 2020 [[Holmenkollen Ski Festival]] in [[Oslo]], Norway, part of the [[2019–20 FIS Cross-Country World Cup]], was held on 7–8 March, without spectators in the stadium part of the [[Holmenkollen National Arena]].<ref>{{Cite web|title=Besked: Tvingas tävla utan publik|url=https://www.expressen.se/sport/langdskidor/besked-tvingas-tavla-utan-publik/|last=Larsson|first=Jonathan|date=5 March 2020|language=Swedish|website=[[Expressen]]|access-date=23 May 2020}}</ref>

The final two events of the World Cup season, the 2020 Sprint Tour (14–17 March, in [[Quebec City]], Canada and [[Minneapolis]], United States) and the [[FIS Cross-Country World Cup Finals|2020 World Cup Finals]] (20–21 March, in [[Canmore, Alberta|Canmore]], Canada), were cancelled on 12 and 13 March.<ref>{{Cite web|last=Blount|first=Rachel|date=13 March 2020|title=World Cup cross-country ski races scheduled for next week in Minneapolis called off because of virus threat|url=https://m.startribune.com/world-cup-cross-country-ski-races-scheduled-for-next-week-in-minneapolis-called-off-because-of-virus-threat/568732522/|url-status=live|archive-url=|archive-date=|access-date=23 November 2020|website=[[Star Tribune]]}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |title=World Cup cross-country ski event cancelled in Quebec City due to coronavirus outbreak |url=https://globalnews.ca/news/6671851/quebec-city-world-cup-skiing-cancelled-coronavirus/ |publisher=[[Global News]] |accessdate=23 May 2020 |date=13 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |title=Coronavirus In Minnesota: World Cup Ski Race In Minneapolis Canceled |url=https://minnesota.cbslocal.com/2020/03/12/coronavirus-world-cup-ski-race-in-minneapolis-cancelled-due-to-coronavirus-concerns/ |publisher=[[WCCO-TV]] |access-date=25 November 2020 |date=12 March 2020}}</ref>

===2020–21 FIS Cross-Country World Cup===

The [[Swedish Ski Association]] elected not to send a full squad of skiers and support staff for the first round of the [[2020–21 FIS Cross-Country World Cup]] in [[Rukatunturi]], Finland, 27–29 November.<ref>{{cite web |title=Trots coronapandemin: Norge skickar full trupp till Ruka |url=https://www.svt.se/sport/langdskidor/trots-coronapandemin-norge-skickar-full-trupp-till-ruka |publisher=[[Sveriges Television|SVT Sport]] |access-date=2 December 2020 |language=Swedish |date=23 November 2020}}</ref>

The second round of the World Cup, to be held in [[Lillehammer]], Norway, 4–6 December, was postponed on 12 November, due to the current status of COVID-19 prevention measures, with a new date to be announced later.<ref>{{cite web |title=Lillehammers världscuptävling skjuts upp |url=https://www.svt.se/sport/langdskidor/norge-ber-om-att-fa-skjuta-upp-tavlingarna-i-lillehammer |publisher=[[Sveriges Television|SVT Sport]] |access-date=2 December 2020 |language=Swedish |date=12 November 2020}}</ref>

On 1 December, the [[Norwegian Ski Federation]] (NSF) announced that they would not send any skiers to take part in the World Cup events in [[Davos]], Switzerland, and [[Dresden]], Germany, in December, and possibly not take part in the [[Tour de Ski]], which is planned to begin on 1 January 2021. [[Espen Bjervig]], manager of the NSF's cross-country section said the decision was based on "the risk of travelling, we have experienced that keeping distance and avoiding close contact in the World Cup arena is more demanding than we first assumed”, and that "endurance athletes have their lungs as a tool, and we do not know the after-effects of COVID-19. Therefore, we must take precautions".<ref>{{cite web |last1=O’Connor |first1=Philip |title=Norway pull out of World Cup events over COVID-19 fears |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/uk-nordic-skiing-worldcup/norway-pull-out-of-world-cup-events-over-covid-19-fears-idUKKBN28B5O6 |publisher=[[Reuters]] |access-date=3 December 2020 |date=1 December 2020}}</ref>

On 2 December, the Swedish Ski Association and the [[Finnish Ski Association]] announced that they would mirror Norway's decision, and not send any skiers to the events in Davos and Dresden. [[International Ski Federation]] (FIS) marketing director [[Jürg Capol]] was critical of the three countries pulling out of the events and said "We need solidarity. If it's not given it's going to be hard to find (competition) arrangers in the future", and added that "Of course all nations must make their own decisions. The problem is not that they can not get to the competitions, but that they themselves have chosen not to go there".<ref>{{cite web |last1=Walker-Roberts |first1=James |title=Sweden and Finland follow Norway in withdrawing from cross-country skiing World Cup events |url=https://www.eurosport.com/cross-country-skiing/sweden-and-finland-follow-norway-in-withdrawing-from-cross-country-skiing-world-cup-events_sto8016091/story.shtml |publisher=[[Eurosport]] |access-date=3 December 2020 |date=2 December 2020}}</ref>

On 4 December, the FIS cancelled the World Cup races in [[Beijing]], China, citing travel restrictions amid the coronavirus pandemic, “including a current mandatory 14-day quarantine for all international visitors” in China. The races were supposed to be held 19–21 March, and would have acted as a dress rehearsal for the upcoming [[2022 Winter Olympics]] in Beijing. The FIS said they would be looking for a replacement host for the races.<ref>{{cite web |title=Ski events canceled at 2022 Beijing Olympic venues |url=https://apnews.com/article/travel-winter-olympics-ski-jumping-beijing-coronavirus-pandemic-ec4d3accba5c3c753a14d4e633af2775 |publisher=[[Associated Press]] |access-date=5 December 2020 |date=4 December 2020}}</ref>

===2021 FIS Nordic World Ski Championships===

The [[FIS Nordic World Ski Championships 2021|2021 FIS Nordic World Ski Championships]], from 22 February to 7 March, in [[Oberstdorf]], Germany, are planned to go ahead as scheduled. The organiser has set a limit of two thousand spectators around the cross-country trails.<ref>{{cite web |title=Oberstdorf plant mit Zuschauern bei Ski-Nordisch-WM im Allgäu |url=https://www.br.de/nachrichten/sport/oberstdorf-plant-mit-zuschauern-bei-ski-nordisch-wm-im-allgaeu,SDVJ8rY |publisher=[[Bayerischer Rundfunk]] |access-date=4 December 2020 |language=German |date=15 October 2020}}</ref>

==Curling==
The [[2019–20 curling season|curling season]] typically ends in May but was cut short by the pandemic, effectively ending in early March. The [[World Curling Federation]] cancelled the last five championships scheduled for the 2019–20 curling season, most importantly the [[2020 World Women's Curling Championship]], [[2020 World Men's Curling Championship]], and [[2020 World Mixed Doubles Curling Championship]].<ref>{{cite web |title=2019–2020 season ends with event cancellations |url=https://worldcurling.org/2020/03/2019-2020-season-ends/ |website=World Curling Federation |accessdate=24 March 2020 |date=19 March 2020}}</ref>

==Cycling==

===Road cycling===
[[File:2020 Tour de France, 2nd stage, interviews, Marc Hirschi.jpg|thumb|[[Marc Hirschi]] wearing a face mask is interviewed after the 2nd stage of the [[2020 Tour de France]]. The journalist is maintaining a physical distance between him and the cyclist using a pole with the microphone attached to the end.]]
The [[2020 UAE Tour]] was scheduled to run until 29 February, but was abandoned following stage five after two support staff tested positive for coronavirus. Of the following nineteen [[2020 UCI World Tour]] races scheduled to take place up to 31 May, only [[2020 Omloop Het Nieuwsblad|Omloop Het Nieuwsblad]] and [[2020 Paris–Nice|Paris–Nice]], which also had the final day of racing removed, took place at the intended time, some with the stated hope of taking place at a later date. The postponed races in this block include the [[2020 Giro d'Italia]] and four of the five annual [[Cycling monument|monuments]], and many lower category races were also cancelled or postponed. Also races of the [[2020 UCI Women's World Tour]] were cancelled or postponed.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.uci.org/news/2020/novel-coronavirus-important-information |title=Novel coronavirus: important information |website=UCI |language=en|access-date=21 February 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last=Farrand |first=Stephen |title=RCS Sport cancels Strade Bianche in light of coronavirus measures |url=https://www.cyclingnews.com/news/rcs-sport-cancels-strade-bianche-in-light-of-coronavirus-measures/ |work=[[Cyclingnews.com]] |publisher=[[Future plc]] |accessdate=5 March 2020 |date=5 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last=Frattini |first=Kirsten |title=Coronavirus: Women's WorldTour Trofeo Alfredo Binda postponed until June 2 |url=https://www.cyclingnews.com/news/coronavirus-womens-worldtour-trofeo-alfredo-binda-postponed-until-june-2/ |work=[[Cyclingnews.com]] |publisher=[[Future plc]] |accessdate=5 March 2020 |date=5 March 2020 |quote=They are still awaiting the authorisation of the new date from the UCI.}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.cyclingnews.com/news/coronavirus-womens-worldtour-ronde-van-drenthe-cancelled/ |title=Coronavirus: Women's WorldTour Ronde van Drenthe cancelled |first=Lukas |last=Knöfler |work=[[Cyclingnews.com]] |publisher=[[Future plc]] |accessdate=12 March 2020 |date=12 March 2020 |quote=Sadly, this means that our races will not go ahead [...] We hope to be back next year.}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=Geen koers tot en met drie april, Ronde van Vlaanderen maakt nog een waterkansje maar houdt rekening met annulering |language=Dutch|trans-title=No race until 3 April, Tour of Flanders still has a remote chance but takes cancellation into account |url=https://www.nieuwsblad.be/cnt/dmf20200312_04887671 |work=[[Het Nieuwsblad]] |publisher=[[Mediahuis]] |accessdate=12 March 2020 |date=12 March 2020 |quote=We besluiten bij deze om onze wedstrijd Driedaagse Brugge De Panne ook uit te stellen naar een later tijdstip. We hopen dat we een plaatsje krijgen op de kalender in het najaar. [We hereby decide to postpone our match Three Days Bruges De Panne to a later date. We hope that we will have a place on the calendar in the autumn].}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=https://sporza.be/nl/2020/03/12/alle-sportactiviteiten-in-belgie-tot-en-met-3-april-worden-gean~1584050395120/ |title=Alle sportactiviteiten in België tot en met 3 april worden geannuleerd |language=Dutch|trans-title=All sports activities in Belgium until 3 April will be canceled |work=[[Sporza]] |publisher=[[Vlaamse Radio- en Televisieomroeporganisatie]] |date=12 March 2020 |accessdate=12 March 2020 |quote=In het wielrennen worden Nokere Koerse (18 maart), de Bredene Koksijde Classic (20 maart), de Driedaagse Brugge-De Panne (25 maart), de E3 Harelbeke (27 maart), Gent-Wevelgem (29 maart) en Dwars door Vlaanderen (1 april) geschrapt. [In cycling Nokere Koerse (March 18), the Bredene Koksijde Classic (March 20), the Driedaagse Brugge-De Panne (March 25), the E3 Harelbeke (March 27), Ghent-Wevelgem (March 29) and Dwars door Vlaanderen (April 1) are scrapped.]}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=https://womenstour.co.uk/womens-tour-2020-postponed |title=Women's Tour 2020 postponed |first=Nick |last=Bull |work=[[The Women's Tour]] |publisher=SweetSpot Group |date=13 March 2020 |accessdate=13 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.cyclingnews.com/news/paris-roubaix-fleche-wallonne-and-liege-bastogne-liege-postponed-due-to-coronavirus-pandemic/ |title=Paris-Roubaix, Flèche Wallonne and Liège-Bastogne-Liège postponed due to coronavirus pandemic |first=Barry |last=Ryan |work=[[Cyclingnews.com]] |publisher=[[Future plc]] |date=17 March 2020 |accessdate=17 March 2020 |quote=As part of the fight against the spread of Coronavirus (COVID19), Amaury Sport Organisation, with the agreement of the Union Cycliste Internationale (UCI), has decided to not organise Paris-Roubaix (12th April), the Flèche Wallonne and the Flèche Wallonne Women (22nd April) and Liège-Bastogne-Liège and Liège-Bastogne-Liège Women (26th April) races on their scheduled dates.}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.cyclingnews.com/news/tour-of-flanders-cancelled-over-coronavirus-concerns/ |title=Tour of Flanders cancelled over coronavirus concerns |work=[[Cyclingnews.com]] |publisher=[[Future plc]] |date=17 March 2020 |accessdate=17 March 2020 |quote=Organisers of the Tour of Flanders made the long-anticipated decision to cancel their April 5 race, saying they will work with the UCI and |url=https://www.velonews.com/2020/03/news/rolling-report-impact-of-coronavirus-on-pro-racing_505843 |title=Rolling report: Impact of coronavirus on pro racing |work=[[VeloNews]] |publisher=Pocket Outdoor Media, LLC |date=13 March 2020 |accessdate=18 March 2020 |quote=March 18, 5:15 a.m. (MT): Amstel Gold race postponed}}</ref>{{citation overkill|date=May 2020}}

On 15 March, [[Union Cycliste Internationale|UCI]] requested to suspend all UCI-sanctioned events in affected territories until 3 April, and the qualification for the Tokyo 2020 Olympic Games and Paralympic Games to stop retroactively as of 3 March.<ref name="uci20200315">{{cite web |url=https://www.uci.org/inside-uci/press-releases/the-uci-takes-strong-measures-faced-with-the-development-of-the-coronavirus |title=The UCI takes strong measures faced with the development of the coronavirus |date=15 March 2020 |publisher=Union Cycliste Internationale |accessdate=24 March 2020}}</ref> On 18 March, the suspension of events were extended at least until the end of April.<ref name="uci20200318">{{cite web |url=https://www.uci.org/inside-uci/press-releases/the-uci-and-its-partners-unite-to-face-the-consequences-of-the-coronavirus-for-road-cycling |title=The UCI and its partners unite to face the consequences of the coronavirus for road cycling |date=18 March 2020 |publisher=Union Cycliste Internationale |accessdate=24 March 2020}}</ref> On 1 April, the suspension was extended until 1 June,<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.uci.org/inside-uci/press-releases/the-uci-prolongs-the-suspension-of-cycling-events-until-1-june-2020-and-continues-consultations-for-the-reorganisation-of-the-uci-international-road-calendar |title=The UCI prolongs the suspension of cycling events until 1 June 2020 and continues consultations for the reorganisation of the UCI International Road Calendar |date=1 April 2020 |publisher=Union Cycliste Internationale |accessdate=3 April 2020}}</ref> and on 15 April, it was extended until 1 July for the international races, and until 1 August for the [[UCI World Tour]] races.<ref name=uci20200415>{{cite web |url=https://www.uci.org/road/news/2020/the-uci-reveals-the-broad-lines-of-the-revised-2020-uci-international-road-calendar |title=The UCI reveals the broad lines of the revised 2020 UCI International Road Calendar |publisher=Union Cycliste Internationale |date=15 April 2020 |accessdate=15 April 2020}}</ref>

On 14 April, the annual [[2020 Tour de France|Tour de France]], originally scheduled for 27 June – 19 July, was postponed due to the [[COVID-19 pandemic in France|country's strict measures with the coronavirus]] as [[Government of France|the government]] extended a ban on mass gatherings until July.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.espn.com/olympics/cycling/story/_/id/29033546/tour-de-france-postponed-no-new-dates-set|title=Tour de France postponed no new dates set |work=ESPN |accessdate=14 April 2020}}</ref> The following day, [[Amaury Sport Organisation|ASO]] and UCI rescheduled the race for 29 August to 20 September, and it was ultimately held at that time.<ref name=uci20200415 /> A virtual race was conducted every weekend with bikers and teams racing against each other from their homes.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.pbs.org/newshour/show/this-years-tour-de-france-is-a-virtual-ride|title= This year's Tour de France is a virtual ride|accessdate=12 July 2020|website=PBS NewsHour}}</ref>

A revised calendar for both the men and the women was issued on 5 May, which was updated on 12 June.

On 15 July, the first UCI-sanctioned race after the suspension, [[Dookoła Mazowsza]] was commenced.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.cyclingnews.com/news/first-post-lockdown-international-race-stopped-due-to-motorbike-incident/ |title=First post-lockdown international race stopped due to motorbike incident |publisher=Cyclingnews |date=15 July 2020 |accessdate=17 July 2020}}</ref> The first [[UCI World Tour]] race after the suspension was [[Strade Bianche]] on 1 August, which was moved from its original schedule in March.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.cyclingnews.com/races/strade-bianche-2020/elite-men/preview/ |title=WorldTour resumes at Strade Bianche – Preview |date= |first=Barry |last=Ryan |publisher=Cyclingnews.com |accessdate=2 August 2020}}</ref>

On 23 July, the GP de Québec and the GP de Montréal races scheduled for September in Quebec City and Montreal were cancelled.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.cyclingnews.com/news/quebec-and-montreal-gps-cancelled-due-to-coronavirus/|title=Québec and Montréal GPs cancelled due to coronavirus|first=Barry Ryan 23|last=July 2020|website=cyclingnews.com}}</ref>  On 9 October [[2020 Paris-Roubaix|Paris-Roubaix]], originally scheduled for 25 October, was added to the listed of cancelled races.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://cyclingtips.com/2020/10/paris-roubaix-has-been-cancelled/|title=Paris-Roubaix has been cancelled|date=9 October 2020|website=CyclingTips}}</ref>

===BMX===
Race days of the 2020 [[UCI BMX Supercross World Cup]] were cancelled including 2 to 3 May in Papendal, the Netherlands.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://myprivacy.dpgmedia.net/?siteKey=Oom2kBLTny5zJUeO&callbackUrl=https%3a%2f%2fwww.gelderlander.nl%2fprivacy-gate%2faccept%3fredirectUri%3d%252fsport-arnhem%252fwereldbeker-bmx-papendal-ook-van-de-agenda-geld-terug-voor-deelnemers-en-fans%257ea71539c9%252f%253freferrer%253dhttps%253a%252f%252fwww.google.nl%252f |title=Privacy settings |website=myprivacy.dpgmedia.net |accessdate=27 March 2020}}</ref>

The 2020 [[UCI BMX World Championships]], scheduled to take place in [[Houston]], United States on 26–31 May, are postponed.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://nos.nl/l/2328063 |title=Ook wereldkampioenschappen BMX uitgesteld wegens coronavirus |website=nos.nl |accessdate=27 March 2020}}</ref>

===Other===
The annual [[Cape Epic]] endurance race scheduled from 15 to 22 March was cancelled.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.cape-epic.com/riders/the-2020-race/official-statement-2020-absa-cape-epic-cancellation |title=The Official Statement regarding the cancellation of the 2020 Absa Cape Epic {{!}} Absa Cape Epic|website=cape-epic.com|access-date=16 March 2020}}</ref>

==Darts==
The [[Professional Darts Corporation]]'s [[PDC European Tour|European Tour]] was impacted by the coronavirus; with the [[2020 European Darts Grand Prix]], the [[2020 European Darts Open]] and the [[2020 German Darts Grand Prix]] all being postponed following restrictions on gatherings implemented by federal governments in [[Baden-Württemberg]], [[North Rhine-Westphalia]] and [[Bavaria]], respectively. The tournaments were officially cancelled on 29 May, with the PDC announcing the European Tour would downsize from the initial plan of thirteen events to five, including one from before the restrictions came in.<ref name="PDCCoronavirus"/> The two [[2020 Premier League Darts]] rounds to be held in [[Rotterdam]] at the end of March were postponed to September following restrictions on gatherings in the Netherlands; and the round to be held in [[Newcastle upon Tyne|Newcastle]] a week earlier was subsequently postponed to October. The next five rounds, in [[Belfast]], [[Sheffield]], [[Manchester]], [[Berlin]] and [[Birmingham]] were also postponed to later dates, with the Sheffield dates now serving as the Play-Off Round. All ProTour events from 16 March to the end of June were postponed.<ref name="MayAndJune">{{cite web |last1=Phillips |first1=Josh |title=Events Update: May & June 2020
|url=https://www.pdc.tv/news/2020/04/22/events-update-may-june-2020|website=[[Professional Darts Corporation]] |accessdate=31 July 2020}}</ref>

On 15 July it was announced that the [[2020 Premier League Darts]] rounds which were to be held in Rotterdam, Birmingham, Belfast, Leeds and Berlin would be cancelled, and instead be played at the [[Marshall Arena]] in Milton Keynes.  As well, the Play-offs were shifted back to London. On 17 August the rounds in Manchester, Glasgow, Newcastle and Sheffield were cancelled, and instead would also be played at Milton Keynes. Finally on 30 September the Play-offs were moved to the [[Ricoh Arena]] in Coventry. The [[2020 World Matchplay]] was also relocated to Milton Keynes and held behind closed doors, rather than the usual venue of [[Blackpool]]. The 2020 [[Champions League of Darts]] was cancelled, and the [[PDC World Cup of Darts]] was postponed from June to November and moved from [[Hamburg]], Germany originally to [[Graz]], Austria, before being moved again to [[Salzburg]].<ref name="PDCCoronavirus"/>

The planned first event on the [[2020 World Series of Darts]], the US Darts Masters, was canceled for 2020, and the [[2020 Nordic Darts Masters]] was originally postponed from June to October before being cancelled on 14 August. The three Australian events The PDC's North American affiliate, the Championship Darts Corporation, cancelled the first weekend of its season in [[Ontario]], and the New Zealand affiliate DartPlayers tour was ended for 2019/20 following the cancellation of events in [[Queenstown, New Zealand|Queenstown]].<ref name="PDCCoronavirus">{{cite web |title=Coronavirus – Latest re PDC events |url=https://www.pdc.tv/Coronavirus |publisher=[[Professional Darts Corporation]] |accessdate=13 March 2020}}</ref>

==Esports==
{{Main|Impact of the COVID-19 pandemic on the video game industry#Esports}}
Impact of the pandemic on [[esports]] have primarily affected events and leagues that host competitions in-person (typically to reduce [[Latency (engineering)|latency]] between players that can impact games played [[Multiplayer video game|over the internet]], and to allow for spectators akin to traditional sports), which have led to cancellations and postponements, and competitions being held behind closed doors—either in the traditional sense, or with competition being conducted entirely over the internet rather than in-person, with [[Video game live streaming|streaming]] broadcasts (as is typical for esports).<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.theverge.com/2020/3/6/21167652/coronavirus-esports-impact-league-of-legends-pubg-csgo-iem-katowice |title=The coronavirus' human impact on esports |last=Garst |first=Aron |date=6 March 2020 |website=The Verge |language=en|access-date=23 March 2020}}</ref><ref name=":2">{{cite web |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/video-games/esports/2020/03/17/esports-streamers-coronavirus-sports-canceled/ |title=While the sports world falls silent, esports and streamers fill the void |last=Smith |first=Noah |date=17 March 2020 |website=Washington Post|access-date=22 March 2020}}</ref><ref name="espn-cancelled-esports">{{cite web|title=How coronavirus is affecting esports and gaming events|url=https://www.espn.com/esports/story/_/id/28852881/how-coronavirus-affecting-esports-gaming-events|last=|first=|date=13 March 2020|website=ESPN.com|language=en|access-date=22 March 2020}}</ref>

Sportcal suggested that the esports industry had an opportunity to attract mainstream sports fans as a "viable alternative" to traditional sporting events.<ref>{{cite web|title=Analyst: "Coronavirus a significant opportunity for eSports"|url=https://advanced-television.com/2020/03/18/analyst-coronavirus-a-significant-opportunity-for-esports/|last=|first=|date=|website=advanced-television.com|language=en-GB|access-date=23 March 2020}}</ref> Roundhill Investments CEO Will Hershey predicted that games that are straightforward for casual viewers to understand (such as sports games) could see particular interest among this new audience.<ref name=":2" />

===Crossover with traditional sports===
The suspension of sports competitions has allowed professional athletes to increase their involvement in video game streaming as a means to engage with fans.<ref name=":2" /> Esports organisations have also invited professional athletes to compete in specific competitions (often alongside, or in competition with professional players); [[FaZe Clan]] organized a charity ''[[Call of Duty: Warzone]]'' pro-am entitled "Fight 2 Fund" in support of coronavirus-related charities, where professional players were partnered with celebrity participants (such as [[Ben Simmons]], [[Chad Johnson]], and [[JuJu Smith-Schuster]]),<ref name=":2" /> and several [[sim racing]] competitions similarly invited professional race drivers.<ref>{{cite web|title=F1 drivers and other pros switch to esports in the age of the coronavirus|url=https://arstechnica.com/cars/2020/03/esports-fills-the-gap-as-coronavirus-cancels-in-person-sporting-events/|last=Gitlin|first=Jonathan M.|date=16 March 2020|website=Ars Technica|language=en-us|access-date=23 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=Pro drivers are competing with gamers after F1 and NASCAR canceled races|url=https://www.theverge.com/2020/3/22/21184192/sim-racing-coronavirus-f1-nascar-iracing-veloce-esports-max-verstappen-lando-norris|last=O'Kane|first=Sean|date=22 March 2020|website=The Verge|language=en|access-date=23 March 2020}}</ref>

Some sports teams have taken advantage of [[sports game]]s in a similar manner, such as the [[Phoenix Suns]] holding ''[[NBA 2K20]]'' streams with guest players, between the teams the Suns were scheduled to play that night if the season had continued.<ref>{{cite web|title=Luka's 50 lead Mavericks past Suns – on Twitch|url=https://www.espn.com/esports/story/_/id/28900417/luka-doncic-50-leads-mavs-suns-twitch|date=14 March 2020|website=ESPN.com|language=en|access-date=29 March 2020}}</ref><ref name=":3">{{cite web|title=Bridges leads Suns to victory in first NBA 2K game broadcast on radio|url=https://www.espn.com/esports/story/_/id/28964373/bridges-leads-suns-victory-first-nba-2k-game-broadcast-radio|date=28 March 2020|website=ESPN.com|language=en|access-date=29 March 2020}}</ref> This culminated with a game actually being commentated by the team's radio broadcasters on team flagship [[KMVP-FM]].<ref name=":3" /> Sports broadcasters have also taken advantage of esports as a form of [[Impact of the COVID-19 pandemic on television#New programming created in response|replacement programming]], with leagues partnering to hold televised tournaments in sports games featuring their players, or in some cases (such as [[ESPN2]] simulcasting the 2020 [[2020 LCS season|''League of Legends'' Championship Series]]) acquiring professional esports events to air on television.<ref>{{cite web|title=ESPN becomes the official broadcast home for League of Legends' Spring Split Playoffs|url=https://www.theverge.com/2020/4/8/21213617/espn-league-of-legends-spring-split-playoffs-broadcast-stream|last=Alexander|first=Julia|date=8 April 2020|website=The Verge|language=en|access-date=21 April 2020}}</ref><ref name="fortune esports">{{cite web|title=From NBA2K to eNASCAR, are e-sports the new, well, sports?|url=https://fortune.com/2020/04/09/coronavirus-esports-surge-nascar-nba-indycar/|last=Morris|first=Chris|date=9 April 2020|work=[[Fortune (magazine)|Fortune]]|accessdate=9 April 2020}}</ref>

The [[IndyCar Series]] and [[NASCAR]] announced partnerships with sim racing platform ''[[iRacing]]'' to hold online invitational events featuring series regulars.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.usatoday.com/story/sports/nascar/2020/03/22/nascar-iracing-pro-invitational-series-fox-sports-1-high-marks/2894874001/ |title=FS1 broadcast of NASCAR iRacing comes extremely close to the real thing |last=Gardner |first=Steve |website=USA Today |language=en-US|access-date=23 March 2020}}</ref><ref name="espn.com">{{cite web |url=https://www.espn.com/racing/nascar/story/_/id/28919500/with-nascar-season-postponed-drivers-compete-esports-series |title=NASCAR greats set to compete in esports series |date=18 March 2020 |website=ESPN.com |language=en|access-date=23 March 2020}}</ref> The inaugural [[eNASCAR iRacing Pro Invitational Series]] event drew a television audience of 903,000 on [[Fox Sports 1]]—making it the most-watched esports broadcast on U.S. linear television since a 2016 ''[[Mortal Kombat X]]'' tournament aired by [[The CW]]. This record was surpassed the following week with a Texas Motor Speedway race — also aired by the main [[Fox Broadcasting Company|Fox network]] — which attracted 1.339 million viewers.<ref name="AW">{{cite web |last1=Weaver |first1=Matt |title=Texas eNASCAR iRacing Event Breaks TV Record for Esports Broadcast |url=https://www.autoweek.com/racing/nascar/a31996587/texas-enascar-iracing-event-breaks-tv-record-for-esports-broadcast/ |website=Autoweek.com |publisher=Autoweek |accessdate=1 April 2020 |ref=AW}}</ref>

==Fencing==
On 3 March 2020, the [[Fédération Internationale d'Escrime]] (FIE) issued its first bulletin on COVID-19 precautions.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://fie.org/articles/942 |title=INTERNATIONAL FENCING FEDERATION - The International Fencing Federation official website |publisher=Fie.org |date= |accessdate=6 April 2020}}</ref> On 10 March FIE strongly recommended that all participants in its competitions (athletes and other members of national delegations) fill and carry with them a questionnaire about their health status.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://fie.org/articles/947 |title=INTERNATIONAL FENCING FEDERATION - The International Fencing Federation official website |publisher=Fie.org |date= |accessdate=6 April 2020}}</ref> On 12 March a FIE circular reported the postponement of six World Cup or Grand Prix competitions and the World Junior/Cadet Championship.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://fie.org/articles/948 |title=INTERNATIONAL FENCING FEDERATION - The International Fencing Federation official website |publisher=Fie.org |date= |accessdate=6 April 2020}}</ref> Since the World Cup and Grand Prix events were part of the [[Fencing at the 2020 Summer Olympics – Qualification|qualifications for the 2020 Tokyo Olympics]], the circular warned on the need to postpone the zonal qualifications tournament for the Olympics. No news was given on other events, and their possible postponement or cancellation.{{citation needed|date=May 2020}}

FIE reported on its web site<ref>{{cite web|url=https://fie.org/articles/949 |title=INTERNATIONAL FENCING FEDERATION - The International Fencing Federation official website |publisher=Fie.org |date= |accessdate=6 April 2020}}</ref> the postponement of the Olympic Games, but hasn't yet given any information on the [[World Fencing Championships]], which is supposed to happen in non-Olympic years, so there is a 2021 Championship planned (assigned to Cairo), but not a 2020 Championship.{{citation needed|date=May 2020}}

Individual countries had different decisions. For example, on 4 April the [[Federazione Italiana Scherma]] announced it was suspending all competitions until 31 August.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.federscherma.it/homepage/media/news/14-news/top-news/30976-il-consiglio-federale-sospende-l-attivita-agonistica-fino-al-31-agosto-in-pedana-solo-per-allenarsi,-quando-sara-consentito.html |title=Federazione Italiana Scherma - IL CONSIGLIO FEDERALE SOSPENDE L'ATTIVITA' AGONISTICA FINO AL 31 AGOSTO. IN PEDANA SOLO PER ALLENARSI, QUANDO SARA' CONSENTITO |publisher=Federscherma.it |date= |accessdate=6 April 2020}}</ref>

==Field hockey==
Many field hockey leagues in Europe have been suspended or curtailed, including in Spain,<ref>{{cite web |title=Comunicado Oficial RFEH |url=https://www.rfeh.es/comunicado-oficial-rfeh-7/ |accessdate=20 March 2020 |language=es}}</ref> England,<ref>{{cite web |title=England Hockey suspends national hockey activity |url=https://www.englandhockey.co.uk/news.asp?itemid=49019&itemTitle=England+Hockey+suspends+national+hockey+activity&section=22 |accessdate=20 March 2020}}</ref> Germany,<ref>{{cite web |title=Feldhockey-Bundesligen: Spielverkehr bis Ende April ausgesetzt |url=https://web.hockey.de/news/lgtz22.html |accessdate=20 March 2020 |language=de}}</ref> and the Netherlands.<ref>{{cite web |title=Geen competitie en hockeyactiviteiten tot 1 april|date=12 March 2020 |url=https://zh-cn.facebook.com/hgcheren1/posts/2850250291758662/ |accessdate=5 September 2020 }}</ref>

The [[2019–20 Euro Hockey League]] Final 8 and [[2020 Euro Hockey League Women]] seasons were suspended on 12 March.<ref name="EHL">{{cite web |title=EHL Final8 Put on Hold |url=https://ehlhockey.tv/2020/03/12/ehl-final8-put-on-hold/ |website=ehlhockey.tv |publisher=[[Euro Hockey League]] |accessdate=12 March 2020 |date=12 March 2020}}</ref> The [[2020 Men's EuroHockey Club Trophy I]], [[2020 Men's EuroHockey Club Trophy II]], [[2020 Boys' EuroHockey Youth Championships]], and [[2020 Girls' EuroHockey Youth Championships]] were cancelled.<ref>{{cite web |title=EHF cancels all EuroHockey Club Trophy and Challenge events, 2020 |url=https://eurohockey.org/2020/03/24/ehf-cancels-all-eurohockey-club-trophy-and-challenge-events-2020/ |website=eurohockey.org |publisher=[[European Hockey Federation]] |accessdate=25 March 2020 |date=24 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |title=EuroHockey U18 Championships boys and girls 2020 are cancelled |url=https://eurohockey.org/2020/03/31/eurohockey-u18-championships-boys-and-girls-2020-are-cancelled/ |website=eurohockey.org |publisher=[[European Hockey Federation]] |accessdate=1 April 2020 |date=31 March 2020}}</ref>

In Asia, the [[2020 Men's Hockey Junior Asia Cup]], [[2020 Women's Asian Champions Trophy]], and [[2020 Women's Hockey Junior Asia Cup]] were postponed.<ref name="AHF2020">{{cite web |title=Announcement: Postponement of the Bangabandhu Al-Arafah Islami Bank Junior Asia Cup Dhaka 2020 & the Women's Asian Champions Trophy Donghae 2020 |url=http://www.asiahockey.org/news/announcement-postponement-of-the-bangabandhu-al-arafah-islami-bank-junior-asia-cup-dhaka-2020-the-womens-asian-champions-trophy-donghae-2020/ |website=asiahockey.org |publisher=[[Asian Hockey Federation]] |accessdate=26 March 2020 |date=25 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |title=Women's Junior Asia Cup Gifu Kakamigahara 2020 – Formal Announcement of Postponement |url=http://www.asiahockey.org/news/womens-junior-asia-cup-gifu-kakamigahara-2020-formal-announcement-of-postponement/ |website=asiahockey.org}}</ref> The [[2020 Sultan Azlan Shah Cup]] was originally postponed to 24 September.<ref>{{cite web |title=Coronavirus: Azlan Shah Cup Hockey Tournament Postponed |url=https://sports.ndtv.com/hockey/coronavirus-azlan-shah-cup-hockey-tournament-postponed-2188516 |website=ndtv.com |publisher=[[NDTV]]}}</ref> But on 2 May the Sultan Azlan Shah Cup was officially cancelled.<ref>{{cite web |title=Barren year for hockey with Azlan Shah Cup off |url=https://www.thestar.com.my/sport/hockey/2020/05/02/barren-year-for-hockey-with-azlan-shah-cup-off |website=thestar.com.my |publisher=[[The Star (Malaysia)]] |accessdate=2 May 2020 |date=2 May 2020}}</ref>

==Figure skating==
The [[2020 World Figure Skating Championships]], originally scheduled for 16–22 March 2020 in [[Montreal]], [[Canada]], were first postponed on 11 March by the Quebec Health Ministry.<ref name=CBC-200311>{{cite web|url=https://www.cbc.ca/sports/olympics/winter/figureskating/canada-figure-skating-world-championships-1.5493642|title=World figure skating championships cancelled in Montreal|publisher=[[CBC News]]|date=11 March 2020}}</ref> On 12 April 2020, [[International Skating Union|ISU]] Vice-President for Figure Skating, Alexander Lakernik, told media that the chances of rescheduling the championship were slim, due to the ongoing pandemic.<ref name=RGRU-200412>{{cite web|url=https://rg.ru/2020/04/12/lakernik-iz-za-pandemii-shansov-na-provedenie-chempionata-mira-2020-malo.html|title=Лед подождет и дождется|trans-title=The ice will wait and wait|language=Russian|first=Nikolai|last=Dolgopolov|date=12 April 2020}}</ref> The ISU confirmed a complete cancellation of the event, with no chance of postponement to a later date, on 16 April 2020.<ref name=ISU-200416>{{cite web|url=https://www.isu.org/isu-news/news/145-news/13139-isu-statement-definite-cancellation-of-pending-2020-isu-championships?templateParam=15|title=ISU Statement – Definite cancellation of pending 2020 ISU Championships|publisher=[[International Skating Union]]|date=16 April 2020}}</ref>

The [[2020–21 ISU Junior Grand Prix]] series was cancelled on 20 July 2020.<ref name=ISU-200720>{{cite web|url=https://www.isu.org/isu-news/news/126-junior-grand-prix-news/13222-isu-junior-grand-prix-series-2020-21-cancelled?templateParam=15|title=ISU Junior Grand Prix Series 2020/21 cancelled|publisher=[[International Skating Union]]|date=20 July 2020}}</ref> Over half of the events of the [[2020–21 ISU Challenger Series]] were either also cancelled by the host federations or postponed to an unspecified later date. The Challenger Series events were held as individual events, and thus did not award prize money based on overall series rank.

The [[2020–21 ISU Grand Prix of Figure Skating]] events were heavily modified to accommodate ongoing travel restrictions and the series' culminating event, the [[2020–21 Grand Prix of Figure Skating Final|2020–21 Grand Prix Final]], was postponed from its original date of 10–13 December in [[Beijing]], [[China]].<ref name=ISU-200930>{{cite web|url=https://www.isu.org/isu-news/news/145-news/13267-cancellation-postponement-of-isu-events-season-2020-21?templateParam=15|title=Cancellation / Postponement of ISU Events season 2020/21|publisher=[[International Skating Union]]|date=30 September 2020}}</ref> It was later removed from being held in China altogether.<ref name=ISU-201113>{{cite web|url=https://www.isu.org/isu-news/news/145-news/13322-beijing-2022-olympic-winter-games-adapted-sports-testing-programme?templateParam=15|title=Beijing 2022 Olympic Winter Games – Adapted Sports Testing Programme|publisher=[[International Skating Union]]|date=13 November 2020}}</ref> On 14 October 2020, the second event in the Grand Prix series, the [[2020 Skate Canada International]], was cancelled by the [[Skate Canada|host federation]].<ref name=SC-201014>{{cite web|url=https://skatecanada.ca/2020/10/cancelled-2020-skate-canada-international/|title=Cancelled: 2020 Skate Canada International|publisher=[[Skate Canada]]|date=14 October 2020}}</ref> On 19 October 2020, the fourth event in the series, the [[2020 Internationaux de France]], was also cancelled.<ref name=IdF-201019>{{cite web|url=https://www.isu.org/isu-news/news/125-grand-prix-news/13283-isu-grand-prix-of-figure-skating-internationaux-de-france-cancelled?templateParam=15|title=ISU Grand Prix of Figure Skating – Internationaux de France cancelled|publisher=[[International Skating Union]]|date=19 October 2020}}</ref>

On 16 October 2020, the ISU announced the cancellation of the [[2021 Four Continents Figure Skating Championships|2021 Four Continents Championships]].<ref name=ISU-201016>{{cite press release|url=https://www.isu.org/media-centre/press-releases/2020-6/25124-cancellation-of-isu-four-continents-championships-2021-and-provisional-allotments-of-isu-championships-2022-and-2023/file|title=Cancellation of ISU Four Continents Championships 2021 and Provisional allotments of ISU Championships 2022 and 2023|publisher=[[International Skating Union]]|date=16 October 2020}}</ref> On 24 November 2020, the [[2021 World Junior Figure Skating Championships|2021 World Junior Championships]] were also cancelled.<ref name=ISU-201124>{{cite web|url=https://isu.org/isu-news/news/145-news/13336-update-on-isu-event-calendar-season-2020-21?templateParam=15|title= Update on ISU Event Calendar season 2020/21|publisher=[[International Skating Union]]|date=24 November 2020}}</ref>

Several countries postponed or cancelled their [[2020–21 national figure skating championships|national championships]]. [[U.S. Figure Skating]] relocated the [[2021 U.S. Figure Skating Championships|2021 U.S. Championships]] to be able to create an isolated bubble environment.<ref name=USFSA-201109>{{cite web|url=https://usfigureskatingfanzone.com/news/2020/11/9/2021-toyota-us-figure-skating-championships-relocated-to-las-vegas.aspx|title=2021 Toyota U.S. Figure Skating Championships Relocated to Las Vegas|publisher=[[U.S. Figure Skating]]|date=9 November 2020}}</ref>

Due to skaters' limited availability to travel to competitions, the ISU announced that [[ISU World Standings and Season's World Ranking]] points would not be awarded at early season events, including the [[ISU Challenger Series]] and the [[ISU Grand Prix of Figure Skating|ISU Grand Prix]]. Scores earned at the domestic Grand Prix events also did not count as official ISU scores for the purposes of achieving minimum TES requirements or as personal/season's bests.<ref name=ISU-FAQ>{{cite web|url=https://isu.org/docman-documents-links/isu-files/event-documents/figure-skating-4/2020-21/grand-prix-1/series-files-33/25163-faq-isu-grand-prix-of-figure-skating-season-2020-21/file|title=Frequently Asked Questions: ISU Grand Prix of Figure Skating Season 2020/21|publisher=[[International Skating Union]]}}</ref>

==Futsal==
On 9 March 2020, FIFA and AFC announced that the [[2020 AFC Futsal Championship]] in [[Ashgabat]] was postponed to 5–16 August.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.fifa.com/worldcup/news/update-on-upcoming-fifa-world-cup-qualifiers|title=Update on upcoming FIFA World Cup qualifiers|publisher=FIFA.com|date=9 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.the-afc.com/competitions/afc-asian-cup/news/update-on-upcoming-fifa-world-cup-qualifiers|title=Update on upcoming FIFA World Cup qualifiers|publisher=AFC|date=9 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://futsalfeed.com/original-content/robert-grdovic-talks-about-postponed-afc-futsal-championship-and-predicts-the-outcome|title=Robert Grdovic talks about postponed AFC Futsal Championship and predicts the outcome|publisher=futsallfeed.com|accessdate=8 April 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200514121335/https://futsalfeed.com/original-content/robert-grdovic-talks-about-postponed-afc-futsal-championship-and-predicts-the-outcome|archive-date=14 May 2020|url-status=dead}}</ref>

==Golf==
Many elite golf tournaments, both professional and amateur, have either been postponed or canceled in response to the pandemic, including the [[Men's major golf championships|major championships]].<ref name=golftourneys/> On 13 March, it was announced that the [[2020 Masters Tournament|Masters Tournament]] (scheduled for 9–12 April) had been postponed.<ref>{{cite web |title=2020 Masters Tournament Postponed |url=https://www.masters.com/en_US/news/articles/2020-03-13/2020_masters_tournament_postponed.html |publisher=Masters.com |date=13 March 2020 |accessdate=13 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Harig |first1=Bob |title=Augusta National announces Masters will be postponed |url=https://www.espn.com/golf/story/_/id/28897249/augusta-national-announces-masters-postponed-played |accessdate=13 March 2020 |work=ESPN.com |date=13 March 2020}}</ref> The [[2020 PGA Championship]] (scheduled for 11–17 May) was postponed the following week.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2020/03/18/sports/golf/pga-championship-postponed.html |title=P.G.A. Championship Is Postponed |newspaper=The New York Times |last=Pennington |first=Bill |date=18 March 2020}}</ref> On 6 April, [[The R&A]] announced the cancellation of the [[2020 Open Championship]], the first cancellation since World War II.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.skysports.com/golf/news/12176/11969376/the-149th-open-cancelled-for-this-year-and-will-return-to-sandwich-in-2021 |title=The 149th Open cancelled for this year and will return to Sandwich in 2021 |website=Sky Sports |first=Keith |last=Jackson |date=6 April 2020 |accessdate=6 April 2020}}</ref> This was soon followed by the [[United States Golf Association|USGA]] announcing the rescheduling of the [[2020 U.S. Open (golf)|2020 U.S. Open]] from 18–21 June to 17–20 September (the week before the [[2020 Ryder Cup]], which itself was postponed for a year when organizers chose cancellation to playing the event [[behind closed doors (sport)|behind closed doors]]<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/sport/golf/53246674 |title=2020 Ryder Cup postponed until 2021 because of impact of coronavirus| accessdate=8 July 2020|website=BBC Sport}}</ref>) and to 12–15 November for the Masters (the first ever iteration of the tournament to be played in November) and 6–9 August for the PGA Championship.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/sport/golf/52135613 |title=The Open cancelled; Masters, US Open & US PGA Championship rescheduled |website=BBC Sport |date=6 April 2020 |accessdate=6 April 2020}}</ref> The ladies majors have been similarly affected, with the [[LPGA Tour]] postponing the [[ANA Inspiration]] until September.<ref name=lpga1/>

On 12 March 2020, midway through the first round of the [[2020 Players Championship]], the [[PGA Tour]] announced that the remainder of the tournament and the next three events, the [[Valspar Championship]], [[WGC Match Play]], and the [[Valero Texas Open]], would continue without fan attendance. Subsequently, after completion of the day's play, the tour decided to cancel the remainder of tournament and the three following events.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Harig |first1=Bob |title=Players Championship, other events won't have fans in attendance |url=https://www.espn.com/golf/story/_/id/28890609/players-starts-autograph-ban-place |accessdate=13 March 2020 |date=12 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Harig |first1=Bob |title=PGA Tour cancels Players Championship after first round |url=https://www.espn.com/golf/story/_/id/28894497/pga-tour-cancels-players-championship-first-round |accessdate=13 March 2020 |work=ESPN.com |date=13 March 2020}}</ref> On 17 March, the tour announced the cancellation of all scheduled tournaments through 10 May.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.pgatour.com/company/2020/03/17/pga-tour-news-tournament-cancellations-rbc-heritage-zurich-classic-new-orleans-wells-fargo-championship-att-byron-nelson-pga-championship.html |title=PGA Tour statement regarding additional tournament cancellations |publisher=PGA Tour |date=17 March 2020 |accessdate=17 March 2020}}</ref> The [[European Tour]] have also cancelled or postponed many tournaments, mostly those scheduled from mid-March through to the end of May,<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.europeantour.com/european-tour/news/articles/detail/update-on-european-tour-events/ |title=Update on European Tour events |website=European Tour |date=27 March 2020 |accessdate=1 April 2020}}</ref> including the [[Irish Open (golf)|Irish Open]], a [[Rolex Series]] event.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/sport/golf/52092416 |title=Irish Open: Mount Juliet European Tour event postponed because of coronavirus |website=BBC Sport |date=30 March 2020 |accessdate=30 March 2020}}</ref> The [[Ladies European Tour]] originally postponed the 2020 [[Evian Championship]], originally scheduled for 23–26 July, to 6–9 August,<ref>{{cite news|author=<!--Staff writer(s); no by-line.-->|title=The Evian Championship Moves to Early August |url=https://www.progolfnetwork.com/the-evian-championship-moves-to-early-august/ |accessdate=5 September 2020 |work=Pro Golf Network |date=27 March 2020 }}</ref> but on 9 June announced that the tournament (one of two [[Women's major golf championships|women's majors]] outside of the United States) had been cancelled.<ref>{{Cite web|date=9 June 2020|title=Evian Championship cancelled due to coronavirus|url=https://www.eurosport.com/golf/golf-news-evian-championship-cancelled-due-to-coronavirus_sto7770450/story.shtml|access-date=10 June 2020|website=Eurosport}}</ref> The [[Women's British Open|Women's Open Championship]] was still played, despite the cancellation of its parent men's event.<ref>{{Cite news|last=Corrigan|first=James|date=9 June 2020|title=Women's British Open still hoping to take place in August despite Evian Championship cancellation|language=en-GB|work=The Telegraph|url=https://www.telegraph.co.uk/golf/2020/06/09/womens-british-open-still-hoping-take-place-august-despite-evian/|access-date=10 June 2020|issn=0307-1235}}</ref>

Other leading professional tours have announced similar measures, as have the bodies responsible for organising leading amateur events.<ref name=golftourneys/> On 1 April, the R&A and the USGA jointly announced that the [[2020 Curtis Cup|Curtis Cup]] was being postponed until 2021, and the British [[The Amateur Championship|men's]] and [[The Womens Amateur Championship|women's]] amateur championships were being rescheduled from June to August.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.golfchannel.com/news/curtis-cup-postponed-2021-british-amateur-championships-rescheduled |title=Curtis Cup postponed to 2021; British Ams rescheduled |website=Golf Channel |date=1 April 2020 |accessdate=1 April 2020}}</ref> The LPGA Tour have canceled three tournaments and postponed five others including the ANA Inspiration,<ref name=lpga1>{{cite news |title=LPGA to reschedule 3 events, including first major, the ANA Inspiration |url=https://www.espn.com/golf/story/_/id/28893923/lpga-reschedule-3-events-including-first-major-ana-inspiration |accessdate=13 March 2020 |work=ESPN.com |date=13 March 2020}}</ref><ref name=golftourneys>{{cite web |url=https://www.golfdigest.com/story/here-are-all-the-golf-tournaments-that-have-been-canceled-or-postponed-due-to-the-coronavirus |title=Here are all the golf tournaments that have been canceled or postponed due to the coronavirus |website=Golf Digest |publisher=Golf World |first=Ryan |last=Herrington |accessdate=1 April 2020}}</ref> and the [[Japan LPGA Tour]] cancelled twelve tournaments scheduled from March into May.<ref name=sched>{{cite web |url=https://www.lpga.or.jp/tournament/jlpgatour/2020 |title=2020年度 JLPGAツアースケジュール |trans-title=2020 JLPGA Tour Schedule |publisher=JLPGA |language=ja}}</ref>

On 16 April 2020, the PGA Tour announced a condensed schedule for a proposed resumption of play on 11 June with the [[Charles Schwab Challenge]] in [[Fort Worth, Texas]]. It aims to play most of the remaining tournaments of the [[2019–20 PGA Tour|2019–20 season]] (preserving at least three quarters of the original schedule in total), concluding with the [[FedEx Cup Playoffs]] and the season-ending [[Tour Championship]] on [[Labor Day]] weekend, followed immediately by the beginning of the 2020–21 season (which will have a modified early-season schedule to accommodate the rescheduled majors) with the [[Safeway Open]]. Officials planned the events behind closed doors, although most events were held at courses with residences and/or rental units, and residents were allowed to "attend" the events from their yards on their property, or in the case of the RBC Heritage, from boats traveling the Calibogue Sound. Spectators were expected to return for the [[Memorial Tournament]], but on 14 July it was announced that the remaining tournaments of the 2019–20 season would be played behind closed doors.  The extra delay was intended to give the Tour more time for preparations, as well as take advantage of weeks opened by the cancellation and postponements of majors and the [[Golf at the 2020 Summer Olympics|Summer Olympics]]; only one of the three remaining majors—the PGA Championship—fell within the remainder of the 2019–20 season's schedule.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.pgatour.com/news/2020/04/16/pga-tour-schedule-adjustments-2019-2020-fedexcup-season-2020-2021-regular-season-coronavirus.html|title=PGA TOUR announces schedule adjustments for remainder of 2019-20 FedExCup season, releases fall portion of 2020-21 PGA TOUR Regular Season schedule|website=PGATour.com|language=en|access-date=16 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.espn.com/golf/story/_/id/29043368/pga-revises-schedule-targeting-june-8-start-charles-schwab-challenge|title=PGA Tour revises schedule, targets June 11 return|date=16 April 2020|website=ESPN.com|language=en|access-date=16 April 2020}}</ref>  The [[Sanford International]] in [[Sioux Falls, South Dakota]], a PGA Tour Champions event in September, became the first PGA Tour-sanctioned event to allow spectators since the pandemic.  The [[Corales Puntacana Resort and Club Championship]] became the first tournament with a pro-am since the pandemic, and the Tour intends to have the 2020 [[Bermuda Championship]] to be the first with spectators on the premier tour.

A charity [[skins game]], [[TaylorMade Driving Relief]], was held 17 May at [[Seminole Golf Club]] in [[Juno Beach, Florida]], featuring Rory McIlroy, Dustin Johnson, Rickie Fowler and Matthew Wolff; televised by [[NBC]] and [[Golf Channel]], it was the first televised event at Seminole, and the first in the United States since the suspension of PGA Tour play.<ref>{{Cite web|title=Seminole Golf Club, one of golf's most exclusive enclaves, is ready for its TV debut|url=https://www.golfdigest.com/story/seminole-golf-club-one-of-golfs-most-exclusive-enclaves-is-ready-for-its-tv-debut|website=Golf Digest|language=en|access-date=17 May 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|title=Televised charity skins match pitting Rory-DJ vs. Fowler-Wolff set for May 17|url=https://www.golfdigest.com/story/itll-be-mcilroy-johnson-vs-fowler-wolff-in-televised-charity-match-on-may-17|website=Golf Digest|language=en|access-date=17 May 2020}}</ref> A sequel to [[Tiger Woods]] and [[Phil Mickelson]]'s 2018 match play event ''[[The Match: Tiger vs. Phil|The Match]]'', ''The Match: Champions for Charity'', was announced for 24 May in a simulcast across [[WarnerMedia Entertainment]] networks, with the two participating in a four-ball match at Medalist Golf Club in [[Hobe Sound, Florida]], with NFL quarterbacks [[Peyton Manning]] and [[Tom Brady]] as their respective partners.<ref>{{Cite web|title=Woods, Mickelson, Brady, Manning Golf Match Set for May 24|url=https://www.si.com/golf/2020/05/07/woods-mickelson-brady-manning-golf-may-24|last=Pickman|first=Ben|website=Sports Illustrated|language=en-us|access-date=17 May 2020}}</ref>

Fox Sports opted out of its 12-year contract to broadcast the championships of the [[USGA]] and sold the rights to [[NBC Sports]], with reports suggesting that Fox did not want to work around programming conflicts with its NFL and college football coverage, and that the USGA vetoed a proposal to move the tournament entirely to pay television channel [[Fox Sports 1]].<ref>{{Cite web|last=Goldsmith|first=Jill|date=29 June 2020|title=Fox Sells Rights For United States Golf Association, Including U.S. Open, To NBC Sports|url=https://deadline.com/2020/06/fox-ssports-sells-rights-united-states-golf-association-u-s-open-nbc-sports-1202972535/|access-date=29 June 2020|website=Deadline}}</ref><ref>{{cite magazine|last=Beall|first=Joel|date=29 June 2020|title=USGA announces U.S. Open will move to NBC, ending relationship with FOX|url=https://www.golfdigest.com/story/usga-announces-u-s--open-will-move-to-nbc--ending-relationship-w|magazine=Golf Digest|access-date=29 June 2020}}</ref>

Recreational golf has also been affected, with many countries and regions ordering the closure of golf [[country club|clubs]] and [[golf course|courses]].<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.ctvnews.ca/health/coronavirus/golf-canada-ceo-applebaum-asks-golfers-to-stay-home-during-covid-19-pandemic-1.4863339 |title=Golf Canada CEO Applebaum asks golfers to stay home during COVID-19 pandemic |first=John |last=Chidley-Hill |agency=The Canadian Press |date=22 March 2020 |accessdate=1 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://7news.com.au/sport/golf/australian-golf-courses-told-to-close-immediately-as-coronavirus-restrictions-take-hold-c-772433 |title=Australian golf courses told to close immediately as coronavirus restrictions take hold |first=Glenn |last=Valencich |website=Seven News |date=30 March 2020 |accessdate=30 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.golfdigest.com/story/heres-a-state-by-state-breakdown-of-where-golfs-allowed-and-where-it-isnt |title=Here's a state-by-state breakdown of where golf's allowed and where it isn't |website=Golf World (Golf Digest) |first=Mike |last=Stachura |date=25 March 2020 |accessdate=30 March 2020}}</ref> To enforce social distancing, regulations may require golf clubs to stagger tee times or restrict how services such as pro shops and golf carts are used.  The game was played under no-touch rules.  Ball washers and bunker rakes were decommissioned and "pin in" rules were placed on the green.  To accommodate no-touch golf, holes were modified with an elevated rim or made shallow with a piece of foam (most often a cut pool noodle) or drain pipe or a safety plate.  Some courses deployed a lift system that could be lifted with a putter head.  If the edge of the hole was above the ground level, the ball is deemed to have been holed if the ball comes in contact with the raised rim or cylinder.<ref>{{Cite web|title=With Ontario courses set to open, here's how golf has changed as province eases restrictions|url=https://www.cbc.ca/news/canada/london/covid-golf-courses-1.5569570|last=|first=|date=15 May 2020|website=CBC News|access-date=17 May 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|title=Ask Golf Advisor: Can you post scores of rounds you play during the coronavirus pandemic?|url=https://www.golfadvisor.com/articles/coronavirus-usga-golf-round-score-posting|date=26 March 2020|website=Golf Advisor|language=en|access-date=17 May 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|title=Here's one big way the USGA is relaxing the Rules of Golf to cope with the coronavirus|url=https://www.golfdigest.com/story/here-is-one-big-way-the-usga-is-relaxing-the-rules-of-golf-to-cope-with-the-coronavirus|website=Golf Digest|language=en|access-date=17 May 2020}}</ref>

==Greyhound racing==
The [[2020 English Greyhound Derby]] was postponed on 16 March.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://greyhoundstar.co.uk/derby-postponed-statement/ |title=DERBY POSTPONED – ARC STATEMENT |website=Greyhound Star}}</ref> The [[Arena Racing Company]] tracks announced a behind closed doors policy from 24 March<ref>{{cite web |url=http://greyhoundstar.co.uk/arc-meetings-staged-behind-closed-doors/ |title=ALL ARC MEETINGS TO BE STAGED BEHIND CLOSED DOORS |website=Greyhound Star}}</ref> and [[Greyhound racing in Ireland|racing in Ireland]] continued behind closed doors.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.igb.ie/talking-dogs/covid-19-update-racing-behind-closed-doors/ |title=COVID 19 UPDATE: RACING BEHIND CLOSED DOORS |publisher=Irish Greyhound Board |access-date=20 March 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200320114034/https://www.igb.ie/talking-dogs/covid-19-update-racing-behind-closed-doors/ |archive-date=20 March 2020 |url-status=dead }}</ref> Subsequently, all racing in the United Kingdom and Ireland was postponed<ref>{{cite web|url=http://greyhoundstar.co.uk/greyhound-racing-suspended-press-release/|title=Greyhound racing suspended – Press release|publisher=Greyhound Star}}</ref> until 1 June.

On 12 June it was announced that the [[2020 English Greyhound Derby]] will be run on 31 October.

==Gridiron football==
===Canadian football===

==== CFL ====
On 12 March, the [[Canadian Football League]] (CFL) announced the cancellation or modification of several pre-season events in response to the pandemic. Several scouting combines across Canada and the United States were cancelled, while other events such as rules committee meetings were held remotely. The CFL initially planned to hold both its International and National Drafts in April, but it was announced on 24 March that the Global Draft would be postponed indefinitely.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.cfl.ca/2020/03/12/statement-cfl-coronavirus-situation/ |title=A statement from the CFL on the Coronavirus situation |website=cfl.ca|access-date=14 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.cfl.ca/2020/03/24/cfl-global-draft-rescheduled-lead-event-prior-training-camp/ |title=CFL GLOBAL DRAFT RESCHEDULED AS LEAD-IN EVENT PRIOR TO TRAINING CAMP |website=cfl.ca|access-date=7 April 2020}}</ref>

The [[2020 CFL season|2020 regular season]] had originally been scheduled to begin on 11 June.<ref>{{cite web|title=2020 CFL Schedule|url=https://www.cfl.ca/schedule/?season=2020|access-date=7 April 2020|publisher=cfl.ca}}</ref> On 7 April, Commissioner [[Randy Ambrosie]] announced that the season would not begin until at least July. In a press statement, he announced that the CFL was exploring multiple options to ensure that the league will be able to play as close to a full season as possible.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.cfl.ca/2020/04/07/ambrosie-issues-statement-behalf-cfl/ |title=AMBROSIE ISSUES STATEMENT ON BEHALF OF CFL |website=cfl.ca|access-date=7 April 2020}}</ref>  On 20 May, Ambrosie announced that the season would begin no earlier than September, and the [[108th Grey Cup]] festivities in [[Regina, Saskatchewan]] had been cancelled — with the game being hosted by [[home advantage]] instead.<ref>{{Cite web|last=|first=|date=20 May 2020|title=Grey Cup week in Regina cancelled, CFL says|url=https://regina.ctvnews.ca/grey-cup-week-in-regina-cancelled-cfl-says-1.4946928|access-date=20 May 2020|website=CTV News Regina|language=en}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|last=|first=|date=20 May 2020|title=CFL eyes September return, changes Grey Cup format|url=https://www.cbc.ca/sports/football/cfl/cfl-eyes-september-return-1.5577178|access-date=20 May 2020|website=CBC News}}</ref> The league has explored the possible use of centralized "hub" cities,<ref>{{Cite web|last=Gray|first=Britton|title=Moe open to Regina being a hub city for CFL in 2020|url=https://www.cjme.com/2020/05/29/moe-open-to-regina-being-a-hub-city-for-cfl-in-2020/|access-date=2 June 2020|website=980 CJME|language=en}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|date=14 May 2020|title=CFL, CFLPA discussing two hub-city approach for 2020 season|url=https://www.tsn.ca/cfl-cflpa-discussing-two-hub-city-approach-for-2020-season-1.1475693|access-date=17 May 2020|website=TSN|language=en}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|last=Reid|first=Glenn|date=15 May 2020|title=Tough decisions being made in the Riderville office due to COVID-19|url=https://www.cbc.ca/news/canada/saskatchewan/riders-employees-1.5572796|access-date=17 May 2020|website=CBC News}}</ref> and has requested $30 million in financial assistance from the federal government, and up to $130 million in the event the 2020 season must be scrapped entirely.<ref>{{Cite web|title=Does the CFL need federal funding to survive the COVID-19 pandemic? Sports economist raises questions|url=https://globalnews.ca/news/6884484/cfl-federal-funding-requests/|access-date=17 May 2020|website=Global News|language=en}}</ref>

On 17 August 2020, the CFL announced that the entire 2020 season, including the Grey Cup, would be cancelled as the league's request for funding was rejected by the federal government.<ref>{{cite web | title=CFL cancels season after request for financial help turned down - CBC Sports | website=CBC | date=2020-08-17 | url=https://www.cbc.ca/sports/football/cfl/cfl-cancel-season-pandemic-1.5689252 | access-date=2020-12-13}}</ref>

==== University football ====
[[U Sports]] announced on 8 June 2020 that all fall semester national championships had been cancelled. This resulted in the cancellation of the [[Vanier Cup]] for the first time since its inception in 1965.<ref name=":17" /> [[Atlantic University Sport]], [[Canada West Universities Athletic Association|Canada West]], and [[Ontario University Athletics]] (OUA) all announced that fall semester competition would be cancelled for the season, including football.<ref name=":17" /><ref name=":18" /><ref>{{Cite web|last=Raymond|first=Ted|date=8 June 2020|title=Ontario University Athletics cancels sports and championships until end of 2020|url=https://ottawa.ctvnews.ca/ontario-university-athletics-cancels-sports-and-championships-until-end-of-2020-1.4975280|access-date=18 July 2020|website=CTV News Ottawa|language=en}}</ref>

===American football ===
====NFL====
The [[National Football League]] (NFL) had been in its off-season since [[Super Bowl LIV]] in early February. Experts acknowledged that the [[2019 San Francisco 49ers season|San Francisco 49ers]]' loss in Super Bowl LIV may have averted early community transmission in California via post-game celebrations and [[victory parade]]s.<ref>{{Cite news|last=Cohen|first=Andrew Beaton and Ben|url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/the-49ers-lost-the-super-bowl-and-may-have-saved-lives-11586858401|title=The 49ers Lost the Super Bowl and May Have Saved Lives|date=14 April 2020|work=Wall Street Journal|access-date=24 April 2020|language=en-US|issn=0099-9660}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |last=Bengel |first=Chris |url=https://www.cbssports.com/nfl/news/coronavirus-49ers-super-bowl-loss-helped-prevent-covid-19-spread-experts-claim/ |title=Coronavirus: 49ers' Super Bowl loss helped prevent COVID-19 spread, experts claim |website=CBSSports.com |language=en |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200427060309/https://www.cbssports.com/nfl/news/coronavirus-49ers-super-bowl-loss-helped-prevent-covid-19-spread-experts-claim/ |archive-date=27 April 2020 |access-date=24 April 2020}}</ref>

On 12 March, various NFL teams began to suspend travel by their coaches and [[Scout (sport)|player scout]]s, while the league itself had advised its non-critical staff to work from home.<ref name=":12">{{cite web |last=Walker |first=Patrik |url=https://www.cbssports.com/nfl/news/nfl-coronavirus-updates-league-prohibits-pre-draft-visits-mulls-draft-changes-xfl-player-tests-positive/ |title=NFL coronavirus updates: League prohibits pre-draft visits, mulls draft changes, XFL player tests positive |website=CBSSports.com |language=en |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200316073700/https://www.cbssports.com/nfl/news/nfl-coronavirus-updates-league-prohibits-pre-draft-visits-mulls-draft-changes-xfl-player-tests-positive/ |archive-date=16 March 2020 |access-date=14 March 2020}}</ref> The league will not allow teams to re-open their facilities until restrictions are sufficiently lifted in all U.S. states that contain NFL teams.<ref name=":11" />

The pandemic had an impact on the [[2020 NFL Draft]]; draft-eligible players were prohibited by the league from travelling to meet team personnel, and vice versa.<ref name=":12" />  The draft went on as scheduled, but public festivities in [[Las Vegas]] were canceled,<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.nfl.com/news/nfl-draft-to-proceed-april-23-25-sans-public-events-in-las-vega-0ap3000001106351 |title=NFL draft to proceed April 23–25 sans public events in Las Vegas |author=<!--Not stated--> |website=NFL.com |language=en |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200623042302/https://www.nfl.com/news/nfl-draft-to-proceed-april-23-25-sans-public-events-in-las-vega-0ap3000001106351 |archive-date=23 June 2020 |access-date=16 March 2020}}</ref> and the draft switched to a remote format where team staff convened from home, with all 32 teams being linked to each other and league staff via [[Microsoft Teams]] and other communication software. NFL Commissioner [[Roger Goodell]] announced the first-round picks from his home in [[Bronxville, New York]].<ref name=":11">{{cite web |last1=Seifert |first1=Kevin |title=The 2020 NFL draft is going virtual: How it will work, and what you should know |url=https://www.espn.com/nfl/draft2020/story/_/id/29026049/the-2020-nfl-draft-going-virtual-how-work-should-know |website=ESPN |accessdate=19 April 2020 |date=18 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://variety.com/2020/tv/news/nfl-draft-espn-abc-2020-coronavirus-1234578514/|title=NFL Draft Will Get April Showcase on ESPN, ABC, NFL Network|last=Steinberg|first=Brian|date=13 April 2020|website=Variety|access-date=14 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://profootballtalk.nbcsports.com/2020/04/12/roger-goodell-to-announce-first-round-picks-from-his-basement/|title=Roger Goodell to announce first-round picks from his basement|last=Alper|first=Josh|date=12 April 2020|website=ProFootballTalk|access-date=14 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|last=Belson|first=Ken|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2020/03/27/sports/football/nfl-draft-coronavirus.html|title=How the N.F.L. Draft Process Works From Home|date=27 March 2020|work=The New York Times|access-date=29 March 2020|language=en-US|issn=0362-4331}}</ref> The NFL hosted a charity appeal throughout the draft, supporting aid-related charities.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.nfl.com/news/story/0ap3000001109828/article/roger-goodell-nfl-draftathon-great-way-to-give-back|title=Roger Goodell: NFL Draft-A-Thon great way to 'give back'|website=NFL.com|language=en|access-date=20 April 2020}}</ref> During the broadcast, Goodell announced that Las Vegas would instead host the [[2022 NFL Draft]].<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.reviewjournal.com/sports/nfl-draft/las-vegas-scores-second-shot-at-nfl-draft-in-2022-2013400/|title=Las Vegas scores second shot at NFL draft in 2022|date=24 April 2020|website=Las Vegas Review-Journal|language=en-US|access-date=24 April 2020}}</ref>

The NFL released its regular season schedule for the {{nfly|2020}} season on 7 May. While the league intends to play its full season as scheduled, the schedule was formulated so that two weeks of games from the 16-week schedule could be removed without repercussions and [[Super Bowl LV]] could be delayed to late February in the event the start of the season has to be delayed to late-October.  This follows a blueprint from the {{nfly|2011}} season, in which a [[2011 NFL lockout|lockout]] threatened the season.<ref>{{cite web|title=NFL is ready to call an audible or two if coronavirus forces schedule changes|url=https://www.latimes.com/sports/story/2020-05-07/nfl-2020-schedule-release-goodell-changes-coronavirus|author=Fraser, Sam|date=7 May 2020|work=[[Los Angeles Times]]|accessdate=8 May 2020}}</ref> In addition, the league had to work around [[2020 Masters Tournament|The Masters]], which was postponed to November, in order to avoid a broadcasting conflict on CBS.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.usatoday.com/story/sports/nfl/2020/05/08/bradys-move-to-tampa-bay-posed-late-challenges-for-networks/111676756/|title=Brady's move to Tampa Bay posed late challenges for networks|work=AP|publisher=USA Today|date=8 May 2020}}</ref> Due to logistical issues associated with the pandemic, the NFL suspended its [[NFL International Series|international games]] in London and Mexico City for the season.<ref>{{Cite web|title=League cancels all international games in London, Mexico City for the 2020 NFL season|url=https://www.cbssports.com/nfl/news/nfl-cancels-all-international-games-in-london-mexico-city-for-the-2020-nfl-season/|last=|first=|date=|website=CBSSports.com|language=en|access-date=5 May 2020}}</ref>

On 25 June, the [[Pro Football Hall of Fame]] announced that [[Pro Football Hall of Fame Game|the game]] between the [[2020 Pittsburgh Steelers season|Pittsburgh Steelers]] and [[2020 Dallas Cowboys season|Dallas Cowboys]] scheduled for 6 August would be postponed to August 2021.  In addition, the ceremony for the five "modern era" inductees will be consolidated with the 2021 class to be announced prior to Super Bowl LV.  A separate "Centennial Class" of 15 members was to be inducted on 18 September; that ceremony has yet to be rescheduled.<ref>{{cite web|title=Pro Football Hall of Fame Enshrinement Week Postponed Amid COVID-19 Pandemic|url=https://www.profootballhof.com/pro-football-hall-of-fame-enshrinement-week-postponed-amid-covid-19-pandemic/|author=|date=25 June 2020|work=[[Pro Football Hall of Fame]]|accessdate=29 June 2020}}</ref>  On 25 July, the remaining 64 preseason games were also scrapped.<ref>{{cite web|title=Roger Goodell writes letter to NFL fans as training camps start across U.S.|url=https://www.nfl.com/news/roger-goodell-letter-nfl-fans-training-camps|last=Shook|first=Nick|date=27 June 2020|work=NFL.com|accessdate=5 September 2020}}</ref>

[[File:Washington Football Team entering empty MetLife Stadium.jpg|thumb|NFL game between the [[New York Giants]] and [[Washington Football Team]] at [[MetLife Stadium]] without fans in October 2020]]
Whether fans will be allowed to attend games will be on a case-by-case basis, dependent on local regulations. [[Fox NFL|Fox Sports]]' lead NFL commentator [[Joe Buck]] stated that the network already had plans to employ simulated crowds on its telecasts, including sound effects and the possibility of using [[Computer-generated imagery|computer-rendered]] spectators to provide the illusion of a filled stadium.<ref>{{Cite web|title=Joe Buck: FOX Might Pump In Crowd Noise During Games|url=https://www.si.com/nfl/2020/05/14/joe-buck-nfl-games-crowd-noise-virtual-fans-coronavirus-fox|last=Selbe|first=Nick|website=Sports Illustrated|language=en-us|access-date=15 May 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|title=With the prospect of empty stadiums, how will the NFL move forward?|url=https://www.sandiegouniontribune.com/sports/chargers-rams/story/2020-05-08/coronavirus-outbreak-leaves-nfl-season-under-layer-uncertainty|date=8 May 2020|website=San Diego Union-Tribune|language=en-US|access-date=15 May 2020}}</ref>

On 10 July, the [[National Football League Players Association]] (NFLPA) said that 72 NFL players, or 2.5 percent of players on rosters had tested positive for COVID-19.<ref name="NFL-72-players-positive">{{cite news |last=Patra |first=Kevin |date=16 July 2020 |title=NFLPA: 72 players tested positive for COVID-19, as of July 10 |url=https://www.nfl.com/news/nflpa-72-players-tested-positive-for-covid-19-as-of-july-10 |url-status=live |work=NFL.com |location= |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200717095641/https://www.nfl.com/news/nflpa-72-players-tested-positive-for-covid-19-as-of-july-10 |archive-date=17 July 2020 |access-date= 18 July 2020}}</ref>

On 30 September, the NFL announced its first regular-season game postponement resulting from the pandemic.  Due to an outbreak among the [[2020 Tennessee Titans season|Tennessee Titans]], the team's scheduled home game on 4 October against the Steelers was postponed.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://twitter.com/diannaespn/status/1311321551665586176?s=21 |title=Tweet |website=twitter.com |accessdate=2020-12-13}}</ref>  It was eventually rescheduled for 25 October, with the Steelers' road game against the [[2020 Baltimore Ravens season|Baltimore Ravens]] pushed back from 25 October to 1 November.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://twitter.com/NFLprguy/status/1312064340674187265 |title=Tweet |website=twitter.com |accessdate=2020-12-13}}</ref>

On 14 October, the NFL announced cancellation of the [[2021 Pro Bowl]], which was to have been held at [[Allegiant Stadium]].<ref>{{Cite web|title=NFL cancels 2021 Pro Bowl Game due to COVID-19|url=https://www.nfl.com/news/nfl-cancels-2021-pro-bowl-game-due-to-covid-19|date=14 October 2020|website=NFL.com|language=en-US|access-date=15 October 2020}}</ref>

As of 27 November 20 games had either been postponed or rescheduled due to outbreaks.  The [[2020 Los Angeles Chargers season|Los Angeles Chargers]] were to be involved in four of the affected games, with the Titans and [[2020 New England Patriots season|New England Patriots]] changing two each.  In addition, both the ''[[NBC Sunday Night Football|Sunday Night Football]]'' and ''[[Thursday Night Football]]'' packages saw schedule changes.

The second game [[Ravens–Steelers rivalry|between the Ravens and Steelers]] became the first to be postponed three times. Originally set for the night of [[Thanksgiving (United States)|U.S. Thanksgiving]] (26 November) at [[Heinz Field]], it was first pushed back to 29 November,<ref>{{Cite web|title=Ravens-Steelers game moved from Thursday to Sunday|url=https://www.nfl.com/news/ravens-steelers-game-moved-from-thursday-to-sunday|date=25 November 2020|website=NFL.com|language=en-US|access-date=25 November 2020}}</ref> then to 1 December,<ref>{{Cite web|title=Ravens-Steelers game moved again from Sunday to Tuesday|url=https://www.nfl.com/news/ravens-steelers-game-moved-again-from-sunday-to-tuesday|date=27 November 2020|website=NFL.com|language=en-US|access-date=27 November 2020}}</ref> and finally to 2 December.<ref>{{Cite web|title=Week 12 Ravens-Steelers game moved to Wednesday at 3:40 PM ET on NBC|url=https://nflcommunications.com/Pages/Week-12-Ravens-Steelers-game-moved-to-Wednesday-at-3.40-PM-ET-on-NBC.aspx|date=30 November 2020|website=NFL Communications|language=en-US|access-date=1 December 2020}}</ref>

Nearly every team had at least one player placed on a new reserve/COVID-19 list, which means either the player tested positive or was in close contact with someone who was.  Examples included [[Cam Newton]], [[Ben Roethlisberger]], [[Matthew Stafford]], and [[Josh Norman]].  On 2 November, the Broncos announced that Pro Football Hall of Fame quarterback - and current general manager - [[John Elway]] had tested positive, perhaps the most notable NFL figure to be diagnosed.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://twitter.com/MikeKlis/status/1323673088186343424? |title=Tweet |website=twitter.com |accessdate=2020-12-13}}</ref>  The previous spring, Broncos linebacker and [[Super Bowl 50]] most valuable player [[Von Miller]] had COVID-19.  In addition, the NFL enforced strict safety protocols, with fines and draft pick reductions possible for violations.

On 28 October, it was reported that the NFL planned to cap [[Raymond James Stadium]] at 20% of its 65,000-seat capacity for [[Super Bowl LV]].<ref>{{Cite web|date=28 October 2020|title=NFL planning to hold fan capacity to 20% for SB|url=https://www.espn.com/nfl/story/_/id/30211775/nfl-plans-limit-fan-capacity-20-super-bowl-masks-mandatory|access-date=20 November 2020|website=ESPN.com|language=en}}</ref>

Due to new restrictions imposed by [[Santa Clara County, California]], the [[2020 San Francisco 49ers season|San Francisco 49ers]] had to move two home games - against the [[2020 Buffalo Bills season|Buffalo Bills]] on 7 December and the [[2020 Washington Football Team season|Washington Football Team]] on 13 December - to [[State Farm Stadium]] in [[Glendale, Arizona]].<ref>{{Cite web|title=Statement from the San Francisco 49ers|url=https://www.49ers.com/news/statement-from-the-san-francisco-49ers-arizona-week-13-week-14|date=29 November 2020|website=49ers.com|language=en-US|access-date=1 December 2020}}</ref>  Practices are to be held somewhere in the Phoenix area.

==== College football ====
On 1 June, the [[National Collegiate Athletic Association|NCAA]] began allowing players to begin voluntary on-campus team activities (such as workouts); cases began to emerge among players and staff afterward.<ref>{{cite news |last=Cooper |first=Sam |date=20 June 2020 |title=Kansas State shuts down football workouts after positive COVID-19 tests, LSU reportedly has 'at least 30' in quarantine |url=https://sports.yahoo.com/kansas-state-reports-14-positive-covid-19-tests-lsu-reportedly-has-30-players-in-quarantine-194724833.html |url-status=live |work=Yahoo!
