Sports |location= |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200624110147/https://sports.yahoo.com/kansas-state-reports-14-positive-covid-19-tests-lsu-reportedly-has-30-players-in-quarantine-194724833.html |archive-date=24 June 2020 |access-date=18 July 2020}}</ref> By 24 June, it was reported that at least 37 schools (about one quarter overall) of  schools in the [[NCAA Division I Football Bowl Subdivision|Division I Football Bowl Subdivision]] (FBS) — the highest level of competition in U.S. college football — had reported positive cases among student-athletes or staff.<ref>{{cite news |last=Myerberg |first=Paul |date=24 June 2020 |title=Return of college athletes for workouts brings COVID-19 issues that could threaten fall schedule |url=https://www.usatoday.com/story/sports/ncaaf/2020/06/24/college-football-covid-19-positives-other-factors-raise-questions/3239780001/ |url-status=live |work=[[USA Today]] |location= |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200715090909/https://www.usatoday.com/story/sports/ncaaf/2020/06/24/college-football-covid-19-positives-other-factors-raise-questions/3239780001/ |archive-date=15 July 2020 |access-date=18 July 2020 }}</ref>

In July 2020, the [[Big Ten Conference]] and [[Pac-12 Conference]] — two of the "[[Power Five conferences|Power Five]]" [[List of college athletic conferences in the United States|conferences]] in Division I FBS — announced that if fall sports and the [[2020 NCAA Division I FBS football season|2020 season]] were played, all games would be played against conference opponents only. Other Power Five conferences have been expected to potentially follow suit. In the second level of Division I football, the [[NCAA Division I#Football Championship Subdivision|Football Championship Subdivision]] (FCS), the [[Colonial Athletic Association]], [[Ivy League]], [[MEAC]], and [[Patriot League]] have cancelled all fall semester sports (although the CAA is still allowing teams to compete independently if they so choose).<ref>{{Cite web|last=Gantt|first=Darin|date=17 July 2020|title=CAA suspends fall football, but some schools may try to play|url=https://profootballtalk.nbcsports.com/2020/07/17/caa-suspends-fall-football-but-some-schools-may-try-to-play/|access-date=18 July 2020|website=ProFootballTalk|language=en-US}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last=Scarborough |first=Alex |date=13 July 2020 |title=Patriot League cancels fall sports due to coronavirus |url=https://www.espn.com/college-sports/story/_/id/29455357/source-patriot-league-cancel-fall-sports |access-date=17 July 2020 |website=ESPN.com |language=en |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200715020826/https://www.espn.com/college-sports/story/_/id/29455357/source-patriot-league-cancel-fall-sports |archive-date=15 July 2020}}</ref><ref name=":02">{{cite web |date=11 July 2020 |title=What do Pac-12 and Big Ten decisions mean for college football? |url=https://www.espn.com/college-football/story/_/id/29442565/what-do-pac-12-big-ten-decisions-mean-college-football |access-date=11 July 2020 |website=ESPN.com |language=en |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200713071837/https://www.espn.com/college-football/story/_/id/29442565/what-do-pac-12-big-ten-decisions-mean-college-football |archive-date=13 July 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|title=MEAC-SWAC 2020 football matchups in Atlanta canceled|url=https://www.ajc.com/sports/meac-swac-2020-football-matchups-in-atlanta-canceled/TSNUIF3BUFFR3FE5F34K6EQVQA/|access-date=18 July 2020|website=Atlanta Journal-Constitution|language=English}}</ref>

The [[NCAA Division I FBS independent schools|FBS independent]] [[2020 Notre Dame Fighting Irish football team|Notre Dame Fighting Irish]] cancelled its [[Emerald Isle Classic]] game in Ireland [[Navy–Notre Dame football rivalry|against]] [[Navy Midshipmen football|Navy]], rescheduling it at [[Navy–Marine Corps Memorial Stadium]] before it was eventually canceled outright. It also saw three marquee games cancelled due to the Big Ten and Pac-12 restrictions, including a [[Notre Dame–USC football rivalry|long-running rivalry game against USC]]); Notre Dame's head coach [[Brian Kelly (American football coach)|Brian Kelly]] stated that the team was evaluating alternatives, and hinted at the possibility of playing additional games against trams from the [[Atlantic Coast Conference]] (ACC), where Notre Dame is a member outside of football and ice hockey (as part of its membership, Notre Dame usually schedules five games per-season against ACC opponents).<ref>{{Cite web|title=Brian Kelly: 'there's plenty of games for us to play'|url=https://247sports.com/Article/Brian-Kelly-Notre-Dame-Fighting-Irish-says-there-are-plenty-of-games-for-them-to-play-in-the-2020-college-football-season-conference-only-schedule-ACC--149176687/|access-date=17 July 2020|website=247Sports|language=en-US}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|date=2 June 2020|title=Notre Dame-Navy game moved from Ireland|url=https://www.espn.com/college-football/story/_/id/29254539/notre-dame-navy-game-moving-ireland-maryland|accessdate=14 June 2020|website=ESPN.com|language=en}}</ref>

The [[2020 NCAA Division I FBS football season]] became bifurcated, with schools in the ACC, [[Big 12 Conference|Big 12]], and [[Southeastern Conference|SEC]] committing to play their usual fall seasons with the Big Ten and Pac-12 postponing.  In addition, Notre Dame is playing a full schedule of ACC games (plus one non-conference contest), with the ACC scrapping its usual division structure.

However, a dramatic series of events occurred in September:
*The Big Ten announced on 16 September that it would indeed play in the fall, with the first game set for 23 October.<ref>{{cite web|date=16 September 2020|title=Big Ten football to announce 2020 season will start on October 24 with daily rapid testing|url=https://www.cbssports.com/college-football/news/big-ten-football-to-announce-2020-season-will-start-oct-24-with-daily-rapid-testing/?ftag=SPM-16-10abi8e|accessdate=18 September 2020|website=CBSSports.com|language=en}}</ref>  Each team will play eight games.
*Presidents of Pac-12 colleges voted on 24 September to move up its football season to fall, with a seven-game schedule per school starting on 6 November.<ref>{{cite news |last=Wilner|first=Jon|date=24 September 2020|title=Pac-12 football returns: CEOs vote to restart 2020 season|url=https://www.mercurynews.com/2020/09/24/pac-12-football-returns-ceos-vote-to-restart-2020-season/?utm_campaign=socialflow&utm_source=twitter.com&utm_content=tw-mercnews&utm_medium=social|accessdate=26 September 2020|website=San Jose Mercury News|language=en}}</ref>
*On the same day, the [[Mountain West Conference]] agreed to advance its football season to the fall.  The first games are scheduled for 24 October and each team will play seven games.<ref>{{cite web|date=25 September 2020|title=Mountain West Football Season to Begin on October 24|url=https://themw.com/news/2020/9/25/2020-mountain-west-football-season-to-begin-on-october-24.aspx|accessdate=26 September 2020|website=Mountain West Conference|language=en}}</ref>
*On 25 September, the [[Mid-American Conference]] also revealed its plan to go ahead with fall games starting on 4 November and with six games per team.<ref>{{cite web|date=25 September 2020|title=MACtion is Back!|url=https://getsomemaction.com/news/2020/9/25/football-maction-is-back.aspx|accessdate=26 September 2020|website=Mid-American Conference|language=en}}</ref>
*In all instances, the only opponents are within each conference.

That left only three FBS programs with no plans to play during the usual season: [[UConn Huskies football|Connecticut]], [[New Mexico State Aggies football|New Mexico State]], and [[Old Dominion Monarchs football|Old Dominion]].

The NCAA is considering a plan in which any team could be eligible to play in a [[bowl game|postseason]], regardless of team records, and allowing games to honour contracts with conferences since the six-win threshold would have been reached by some teams with non-conference games that were cancelled, and thereby making it based on conference records.<ref>{{cite web|date=24 September 2020|title=Waiving bowl qualification requirements recommended|url=http://www.ncaa.org/about/resources/media-center/news/waiving-bowl-qualification-requirements-recommended|accessdate=26 September 2020|website=NCAA.com|language=en}}</ref>

As of 16 December 114 regular-season games were postponed or canceled due to COVID-19 outbreaks throughout the season.{{efn|That does not include the game between [[2020 Utah State Aggies football team|Utah State]] and [[2020 Colorado State Rams football team|Colorado State]] that was not played when USU refused to travel as a political protest against their school president.  In addition, the game between [[2020 Appalachian State Mountaineers football team|Appalachian State]] and [[2020 Marshall Thundering Herd football team|Marshall]] was incorrectly reported as postponed; it was played on 19 September.}}  The highest for a single week was 18, in the week before the [[Thanksgiving (United States)|U.S. Thanksgiving]] holiday.  The [[2020 Houston Cougars football team|University of Houston program]] was the most affected, with eight games postponed, canceled, or rescheduled.  The worst outbreak by program was at [[2020 Wisconsin Badgers football team|Wisconsin]], which had 27 combined cases, including players and head coach [[Paul Chryst]], and had consecutive games canceled.  Later, a third Badger game was scrapped - the [[Paul Bunyan's Axe|Battle for Paul Bunyan's Axe]] against [[2020 Minnesota Golden Gophers football team|Minnesota]] - making them ineligible to participate in the [[Big Ten Football Championship Game|Big Ten championship game]].  (The game was later rescheduled for 19 December; otherwise, this would have been the first season since 1906 in which the game was not played.) The school was investigated for possible violations of the conference protocol regarding COVID-19, but no violations were found.<ref>{{Cite web|date=29 October 2020|title=Badgers report 16 active cases of COVID-19|url=https://www.espn.com/college-football/story/_/id/30219261/wisconsin-badgers-football-program-16-active-cases-covid-19|access-date=7 December 2020|website=ESPN.com|language=en}}</ref>  Later that season, the [[Michigan–Ohio State football rivalry|rivalry game]] between [[2020 Michigan Wolverines football team|Michigan]] and [[2020 Ohio State Buckeyes football team|Ohio State]] was scrapped due to a large number of cases in the Wolverines' program; the last time that game wasn't played was 1916.  That should have made the Buckeyes ineligible to play in the Big Ten title game; however, the conference later changed its rule to allow the Buckeyes to represent the East Division in the game, with [[2020 Northwestern Wildcats football team|Northwestern]] being the opponent.  The [[Old Oaken Bucket]] game between [[2020 Purdue Boilermakers football team|Purdue]] and [[2020 Indiana Hoosiers football team|Indiana]] was canceled on 13 December due to outbreaks at both schools; the last year the game wasn't played was 1919.

On the other hand, two significant games were hastily arranged: [[2020 California Golden Bears football team|California]] versus [[2020 UCLA Bruins football team|UCLA]] on 15 October with a 9 a.m. Pacific time kickoff, after both teams saw their original games that week against other opponents canceled,<ref>{{cite web|title=Cal, UCLA unexpectedly get to continue long rivalry|url=https://sports.yahoo.com/cal-ucla-unexpectedly-continue-long-rivalry-035840289--ncaaf.html|accessdate=15 November 2020|website=Yahoo Sports}}</ref> and a [[2020 BYU vs. Coastal Carolina football game|battle of undefeated teams]] - 13th-ranked [[2020 BYU Cougars football team|BYU]] versus 18th-ranked [[2020 Coastal Carolina Chanticleers football team|Coastal Carolina]] - on 5 December; CCU's original opponent [[2020 Liberty Flames football team|Liberty]] had to cancel, while BYU had an open date.<ref>{{cite web|date=3 December 2020|first=Ross|last=Dellenger|title=Two Men and a Truck: The Last-Minute, 2,200-Mile Journey to Get BYU on the Field at Coastal Carolina|url=https://www.si.com/college/2020/12/03/byu-equipment-truck-coastal-carolina-football-schedule|accessdate=11 December 2020|website=Sports Illustrated}}</ref>

Twelve bowl games have been canceled: [[Bahamas Bowl]], [[Hawaii Bowl]],<ref>{{cite web|date=2 October 2020|title=ESPN Cancels Two Postseason Bowls for 2020 Season|url=https://www.thehawaiibowl.com/espn-events-cancels-two-postseason-bowls-for-2020-season/|accessdate=2 October 2020|website=ESPN Events|language=en}}</ref> [[Redbox Bowl]],<ref>{{cite web|last=Curtis|first=Jake|date=1 August 2020|title=Redbox Bowl Canceled for This Season: The 2019 Game Gave Cal Hope|url=https://www.si.com/college/cal/news/redbox-bowl-canceled-for-2020|accessdate=3 August 2020|website=SI.com|language=en}}</ref> [[Holiday Bowl]],<ref>{{cite news |last=Kenney|first=Kirk|date=23 October 2020|title=SDCCU Holiday Bowl will not be played this year|url=https://www.sandiegouniontribune.com/sports/college/story/2020-10-22/2020-sdccu-holiday-bowl-canceled-college-football-acc-pac-12|accessdate=23 October 2020|website=San Diego Union-Tribune|language=en}}</ref> [[Celebration Bowl]], [[Fenway Bowl]], [[Quick Lane Bowl]], [[Pinstripe Bowl]].<ref>[[ESPN Bottom Line]], retrieved 25 November 2020</ref>, [[Sun Bowl]], [[Las Vegas Bowl]],<ref>{{cite web|url= https://twitter.com/slmandel/status/1334273353972998144|title=Tweet |website=twitter.com |accessdate=2020-12-13}}</ref> [[LA Bowl]].<ref>{{cite web|url= https://twitter.com/LABowlGame/status/1335992473970085890|title=Tweet |website=twitter.com |accessdate=2020-12-13}}</ref>, and [[Frisco Bowl]]<ref>{{cite web|date=14 December 2020|title=Source: UTSA will play in First Responder Bowl|url=https://www.expressnews.com/sports/college_sports/utsa/article/Source-UTSA-will-play-in-First-Responder-Bowl-15801919.php|accessdate=16 December 2020|website=San Antonio Express-News|language=en}}</ref>  The Fenway Bowl, whose inaugural game has been postponed until 2021, will be replaced by a temporary game called the Montgomery Bowl.<ref>{{cite web|date=30 October 2020|title=2020-21 BOWL SEASON SCHEDULE ANNOUNCED|url=https://bowlseason.com/news/2020/10/30/2020-21-bowl-season-schedule-announced.aspx|accessdate=3 November 2020|website=Football Bowl Association|language=en}}</ref>

The [[Army–Navy Game]] scheduled for 12 December was relocated from [[Philadelphia]] to [[Michie Stadium]] on the [[United States Military Academy]] campus on 23 October; officials cited restrictions on the number of military members from each side allowed to attend.  It was to be the first game in the rivalry played somewhere other than a neutral site since 1943.<ref>{{cite news |last=U.S. Naval Academy sports information department|first=|date=23 October 2020|title=2020 Army-Navy Game Presented by USAA to be played at West Point|url=https://navysports.com/news/2020/10/23/football-2020-army-navy-game-presented-by-usaa-to-be-played-at-west-point.aspx|accessdate=23 October 2020|website=Navy Sports|language=en}}</ref>

On 14 November, it was announced that the [[Heisman Trophy]] ceremony for the 2020 season will be revamped as a virtual event with the origination moved from the [[PlayStation Theater]] in the [[Times Square]] area of [[Manhattan]] to the [[ESPN]] studios in [[Bristol, Connecticut]].<ref>[[ESPN Bottom Line]], retrieved on 14 November 2020</ref>

The first semifinal for the 2021 [[College Football Playoff]] was relocated from the [[Rose Bowl (stadium)|Rose Bowl]] in [[Pasadena, California]] to [[AT&T Stadium]] in [[Arlington, Texas]], in part because [[Los Angeles County, California|Los Angeles County]] (of which Pasadena is part) denied officials of the CFP and the [[Rose Parade|Pasadena Tournament of Roses]] permission to allow family members to attend.  Whether the game will be called "[[Rose Bowl Game|Rose Bowl]]" or something else had yet to be determined.<ref>{{cite news |date=19 December 2020|title=CFP Semifinal at the Rose Bowl Stadium to be relocated at AT&T Stadium in Dallas on January 1, 2021|url=https://tournamentofroses.com/cfp-semifinal-at-the-rose-bowl-stadium-to-be-relocated-to-att-stadium-in-dallas-on-january-1-2021/|accessdate=20 December 2020|website=Pasadena Tournament of Roses Association|language=en}}</ref>  Eventually, officials decided that it would be called the Rose Bowl Game, marking the second time the contest would be played outside California and the first since [[1942 Rose Bowl|1942]].

====XFL====
On 12 March, the [[XFL (2020)|XFL]] (a revival of the one-season [[XFL (2001)|2001 league]] owned by [[WWE]] founder [[Vince McMahon]]) announced the suspension of the 2020 season, with all players to be paid their base pay and benefits for the full [[2020 XFL season|2020 regular season]]; the season was officially canceled on 20 March, with half of its ten-week regular season schedule played.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.cbssports.com/nfl/news/xfl-officially-cancels-inaugural-season-reveals-when-players-can-sign-with-nfl-or-cfl-teams/ |title=XFL officially cancels inaugural season, reveals when players can sign with NFL or CFL teams |last=Dajani |first=Jordan |date=20 March 2020 |publisher=[[CBSSports.com]] |accessdate=31 March 2020}}</ref> On 10 April, the league announced that it would suspend all operations and lay off all but a few critical executives, and said it was unlikely a 2021 season would be organized and played, with those executives remaining to wind down the league's business and operations after a [[Chapter 11, Title 11, United States Code|Chapter 11 bankruptcy]] filing three days later.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.espn.com/xfl/story/_/id/29021347/xfl-suspends-operations-lays-employees-no-plans-return-2021|title=XFL suspends operations, lays off employees and has no plans for 2021 season|last=Siefert|first=Kevin|date=10 April 2020|work=[[ESPN.com]]|accessdate=11 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.espn.com/xfl/story/_/id/29030763/xfl-files-chapter-11-bankruptcy-suspending-operations|title=XFL files for Chapter 11 bankruptcy after suspending operations|last=Seifert|first=Kevin|date=13 April 2020|work=ESPN.com|accessdate=16 April 2020}}</ref>

Shortly before the league's assets had been set to be sold in a bankruptcy auction, an investment group led by actor and former WWE performer [[Dwayne Johnson]] purchased the league.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.espn.com/xfl/story/_/id/29614209/sale-xfl-group-includes-dwayne-johnson-gets-approval |title=Sale of XFL to group that includes actor Dwayne Johnson gets approval |first=Kevin |last=Seifert |website=ESPN.com |date=7 August 2020 |accessdate=19 August 2020}}</ref> Johnson announced in a tweet on 1 October that the league would not play in 2021 but planned to play in 2022; the league issued a confirmation later that day.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.espn.com/nfl/story/_/id/30014827/dwayne-johnson-rock-tweet-says-xfl-plans-return-2022 |title=Dwayne 'The Rock' Johnson tweet says XFL plans to return in 2022 |first=Kevin |last=Seifert |website=ESPN.com |date=1 October 2020 |accessdate=1 October 2020}}</ref>

== Gymnastics ==
=== Artistic ===
Multiple international artistic gymnastics competitions, many of which were [[Gymnastics at the 2020 Summer Olympics|Olympic]] qualifying events, were either canceled or postponed. On 13 March, after already having completed qualifications, the [[2020 FIG Artistic Gymnastics World Cup series|Baku World Cup]] canceled its event finals.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.gymnastics.sport/site/news/displaynews.php?idNews=2836 |title=Finals of Baku World Cup cancelled |work=[[International Gymnastics Federation]] |date=13 March 2020}}</ref> The Stuttgart, Birmingham, and Tokyo World Cups (scheduled to take place between 21 March – 5 April) were all postponed to 2021.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.gymnastics.sport/site/news/displaynews.php?idNews=2827 |title=Impact of the COVID-19 outbreak on the upcoming FIG events |work=[[International Gymnastics Federation]] |date=11 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.british-gymnastics.org/news-and-events/news/latest-news/9015-british-gymnastics-national-events-announcement-including-fig-world-cup |title=British Gymnastics national events announcement, including FIG World Cup |work=[[British Gymnastics]] |date=16 March 2020}}</ref><ref name=tokyowc>{{cite tweet |number=1239945252183703553 |user=FIG_media |date=17 March 2020 |title=Japan Gymnastics Association has decided to cancel the #Tokyo All-Around World Cup that was scheduled on 4–5 April 2020}}</ref> The [[2020 European Women's Artistic Gymnastics Championships]] (scheduled to take place 30 April – 3 May) and the [[European Men's Artistic Gymnastics Championships|2020 European Men's Artistic Gymnastics Championships]] (scheduled to take place 27–31 May) were both canceled.<ref name=euros2020>{{cite web |url=https://www.ueg.org/news/covid-19-update-event-cancellations |title=COVID-19 update – event cancellations |work=[[European Union of Gymnastics]] |date=17 March 2020}}</ref> They were later both rescheduled to be held on 17–20 December and 9–13 December, respectively.<ref name=UEG-201005>{{cite web|url=https://www.europeangymnastics.com/news/decisions-regarding-2020-artistic-europeans|title=Decisions regarding the 2020 Artistic Europeans|website=[[European Gymnastics]]|date=5 October 2020}}</ref> The [[Pacific Rim Championships]] (scheduled to take place 17–19 April) was postponed until 2021.<ref name=pacrim>{{cite web |url=https://www.gymnasticsnz.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/2020-Pacific-Rim-postponement-announcement-final-17Mar20.pdf |title=2020 Pacific Rim Championships Postponed |date=17 March 2020 |work=Gymnastics New Zealand}}</ref>

==Handball==
The 25–29 March, [[2020 European Women's Handball Championship qualification]] matches in Rotterdam, the Netherlands were cancelled.<ref name="nu.nl">{{cite web |url=https://www.nu.nl/sport-overig/6033687/deze-sportevenementen-zijn-afgelast-vanwege-het-coronavirus.html |title=Deze sportevenementen zijn afgelast vanwege het coronavirus |date=27 February 2020 |website=NU |accessdate=27 March 2020}}</ref>

==Horse racing==
Horse racing is one sport that has been less directly impacted by the COVID-19 pandemic than most others; some countries and regions never stopped operating horse racing events, and racing was one of the first sports to be resumed in other regions.

In the early stages of the outbreak, most horse racing events remained scheduled as normal, but with restricted attendance at racecourses. This included Hong Kong, France,<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.leparisien.fr/sports/hippisme/coronavirus-les-courses-hippiques-et-les-turfistes-s-adaptent-10-03-2020-8276982.php |title=Coronavirus : Les courses hippiques et les turfistes s'adaptent |first1=Par Stéphan FlourentLe 10 mars 2020 |last1=à 19h56 |first2=Modifié Le 10 Mars 2020 |last2=À 19h57 |date=10 March 2020 |website=leparisien.fr}}</ref> Japan,<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.bloodhorse.com/horse-racing/articles/238823/coronavirus-forces-bettors-online-in-japan |title=Coronavirus Forces Bettors Online in Japan |website=[[The Blood-Horse]] |first=Naohiro |last=Goda |date=2 March 2020}}</ref> United Arab Emirates,<ref>{{cite web |url=https://gulfnews.com/sport/horse-racing/the-35-million-dubai-world-cup-show-must-go-on-1.70362919 |title=The $35 million Dubai World Cup show must go on |website=gulfnews.com}}</ref> United States, Australia,<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.racenet.com.au/news/all-star-mile-slated-to-go-ahead-yet-fans-banned-from-australian-grand-prix-20200313 |title=LATEST BREAKING NEWS – All-Star Mile to go ahead but crowd lockout |website=www.racenet.com.au}}</ref> Ireland,<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.racingpost.com/news/latest/dundalk-to-race-behind-closed-doors-as-ireland-launches-coronavirus-restrictions/427842 |work=[[Racing Post]] |title=Racing in Ireland to go ahead behind closed doors until March 29 &#124; Horse Racing News &#124; Racing Post }}</ref> United Kingdom, Germany, New Zealand, and Singapore.

The [[Macau Jockey Club]] suspended racing events from 31 January to 15 February and resumed racing from 22 February. The [[Korea Racing Authority]] suspended horse racing from 8 March. [[Sunland Park Racetrack & Casino|Sunland Park Racetrack]] in the United States canceled its race meeting from 16 March, which included the [[Sunland Derby]], part of the [[2020 Road to the Kentucky Derby]].<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.bloodhorse.com/horse-racing/articles/239094/maryland-new-mexico-close-tracks-simulcast-facilities |title=Maryland, New Mexico Close Tracks, Simulcast Facilities |website=[[The Blood-Horse]] |date=15 March 2020}}</ref> Many tracks in North America followed suit over the following weeks, although some remained open depending on state-by-state decisions. In Britain, although the [[Cheltenham Festival]] proceeded as normal in mid-March,<ref>{{cite web |last1=Oliphant |first1=Vickiie |title=Cheltenham coronavirus advice: How to avoid COVID-19 – Festival guidelines in FULL |url=https://www.express.co.uk/sport/horseracing/1252795/Cheltenham-coronavirus-advice-guidelines-in-full-cheltenham-festival-races |website=Express.co.uk |accessdate=17 March 2020 |language=en |date=12 March 2020}}</ref> the [[Grand National]] meeting at Aintree in April was cancelled.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.racingpost.com/news/coronavirus/grand-national-meeting-cancelled-due-to-coronavirus-outbreak/428688 |work=[[Racing Post]] |title=Grand National cancelled as Aintree card lost to spiralling coronavirus crisis &#124; Horse Racing News &#124; Racing Post }}</ref> By mid-March [[Republic of Ireland|Ireland]] had become the only major horse racing country in Europe where the sport continued, albeit strictly regulated and behind closed doors.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.theguardian.com/sport/2020/mar/18/talking-horses-racing-industry-left-to-contemplate-cost-of-suspension |title=Ireland goes it alone as racing continues behind closed doors |work=[[The Guardian]] |first=Greg |last=Wood |date=18 March 2020 |accessdate=22 March 2020}}</ref> Ireland finally closed down racing on 25 March.<ref name=IrelandCancelled />

[[Churchill Downs]] announced that the [[2020 Kentucky Derby]], normally the first leg of the [[Triple Crown of Thoroughbred Racing (United States)|American Triple Crown]], would be delayed to 5 September.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.bloodhorse.com/horse-racing/articles/239121/the-146th-kentucky-derby-moved-to-sept-5 |title=The 146th Kentucky Derby Moved to Sept. 5 |website=[[The Blood-Horse]] |date=17 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |first1=Eric |last1=Mitchell |first2=Byron |last2=King |title=Owners, Trainers React to Kentucky Derby Postponement |url=https://www.bloodhorse.com/horse-racing/articles/239123/owners-trainers-react-to-kentucky-derby-postponement |website=[[The Blood-Horse]] |accessdate=17 March 2020 |date=17 March 2020 |language=en}}</ref> They had hoped to run the rescheduled race before a live (though reduced crowd) – this plan was eventually abandoned due to an increase in cases in the Louisville area.<ref>{{cite web |title=Kentucky Derby reverses course, will run without fans |url=https://sports.nbcsports.com/2020/08/21/kentucky-derby-reverses-course-will-run-without-fans/ |website=NBC Sports |accessdate=30 August 2020 |date=21 August 2020}}</ref> The change in dates for the Derby caused a cascading effect through the 2020 racing schedule, with the [[Maryland Jockey Club]] delaying the [[2020 Preakness Stakes]] to 3 October. The [[Belmont Stakes]], normally the third leg of the Triple Crown, [[2020 Belmont Stakes|was run]] at a shortened distance of {{frac|1|1|8}} miles on 20 June as the first leg.<ref>{{cite web |title=NYRA Moves Shortened Belmont Stakes to June 20 |url=https://www.bloodhorse.com/horse-racing/articles/241294/nyra-moves-shortened-belmont-stakes-to-june-20 |website=BloodHorse.com |accessdate=20 May 2020 |language=en}}</ref>

On 22 March, it was announced that the [[Dubai World Cup]], due to celebrate its 25th anniversary running on 28 March, had been cancelled.<ref>{{cite web |title=2020 Dubai World Cup night is called off at Meydan |url=https://gulfnews.com/sport/2020-dubai-world-cup-night-is-called-off-at-meydan-1.1584882198359 |website=Gulf News |accessdate=22 March 2020}}</ref>

On 7 April, [[Jockey Club|Jockey Club Racecourses]] announced that the first four [[British Classic Races|Classics]] of the British flat racing season – the [[2000 Guineas Stakes|2000]] and [[1000 Guineas Stakes|1000 Guineas]], scheduled to be held on 2–3 May, and the [[Epsom Oaks]] and [[Epsom Derby|Derby]], scheduled to be held on 5–6 June – would be postponed until later in the season. Ascot Racecourse also announced that [[Royal Ascot]], scheduled to be held from 16–20 June, would take place [[Behind closed doors (sport)|behind closed doors]] if it gets the go-ahead.<ref>{{cite web |title=Guineas and Derby meetings to be held later in the season, Jockey Club announces |work=[[Racing Post]] |url=https://www.racingpost.com/news/coronavirus/guineas-and-derby-meetings-to-be-held-later-in-the-season-jockey-club-announces/431135 |accessdate=7 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |title=Royal Ascot to take place behind closed doors if given green light |work=[[Racing Post]] |url=https://www.racingpost.com/news/coronavirus/royal-ascot-to-take-place-behind-closed-doors-due-to-the-coronavirus/431128 |accessdate=7 April 2020}}</ref>

To reduce the risk of transmission, horsemen may be limited from traveling to some racecourses or other horse racing facilities.<ref>{{cite web |title=Backstretch Ban for Jockeys, Agents at Multiple Tracks |url=https://www.bloodhorse.com/horse-racing/articles/239345/backstretch-ban-for-jockeys-agents-at-multiple-tracks |website=BloodHorse.com |accessdate=15 May 2020 |language=en}}</ref> Hong Kong-based jockey [[Keith Yeung]] felt unwell on 22 March night, but his test for COVID-19 PCR was negative.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.scmp.com/sport/racing/article/3076478/hong-kong-jockey-keith-yeungs-covid-19-test-comes-back-negative |title=Hong Kong jockey Keith Yeung's Covid-19 test comes back negative |website=South China Morning Post |accessdate=27 March 2020}}</ref> On 26 March, jockey [[Javier Castellano]] was the first American-based jockey to announce that he had tested positive.<ref>{{cite web |last1=King |first1=Byron |title=Jockey Castellano Tests Positive for COVID-19 |url=https://www.bloodhorse.com/horse-racing/articles/239301/jockey-castellano-tests-positive-for-covid-19 |website=BloodHorse.com |accessdate=27 March 2020 |language=en}}</ref> In July, fifteen jockeys in the Del Mar riding colony tested positive, forcing a brief closure of the Del Mar meeting.<ref>{{cite web |title=Del Mar Set for July 24 Return to Racing |url=https://www.bloodhorse.com/horse-racing/articles/242486/del-mar-set-for-july-24-return-to-racing |website=BloodHorse.com |accessdate=30 August 2020 |language=en}}</ref>

Some stakes races' prize money were reduced. In [[Randwick Racecourse]], Racing NSW announced all Group One and some Group two races in The Champions meeting prize reduced 50%.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.racing.com/news/2020-03-29/news-sydney-carnival-prizemoney-changes|title=Racing NSW cut prizemoney for The Championships|website=RACING.COM}}</ref> Inglis Easter Yearlings Sales are many others horse auction held at fully online. While [[France Galop]] resume racing form 11 May, but their prize money dropped by 20-40%.<ref>[http://www.france-galop.com/en/content/2020-prize-money-emergency-measures-support-resumption-racing-current-health-crisis 2020 Prize money Emergency measures in support of the resumption of racing in the current health crisis]</ref> All [[Royal Ascot]] Group One races prize money are reduced to 250,000 GBP only.

In the U.S., horse racing gained an increased following as a form of live sports content on television, with efforts by the [[New York Racing Association]] and [[TVG Network]] (which also reached agreements with [[Fox Sports 1]] and [[NBCSN]] respectively to help fill schedules with simulcast programming) to try and attract new viewers and customers for [[off-track betting]] at tracks still in operation. Mainstream attention to horse racing in the United States is usually focused upon the Triple Crown, and to a lesser degree the Breeders' Cup. Simulcasts also increased the prominence of lesser-known venues such as [[Fonner Park]] in [[Grand Island, Nebraska]] — which saw its average daily [[Parimutuel betting|parimutuel]] handle surpass its previous single-day record of US$1.2 million on a regular basis.<ref name=":15">{{Cite web|title=Minnesota-fed horse racing network seizes moment almost all its own|url=https://www.startribune.com/horse-racing-network-seizes-a-moment-nearly-all-its-own/569364752/|website=Star Tribune|access-date=24 May 2020}}</ref><ref name=":16">{{Cite web|title=Fonner Park, in the heart of Nebraska, is now the center of the horse racing world|url=https://www.theindependent.com/news/local/fonner-park-in-the-heart-of-nebraska-is-now-the-center-of-the-horse-racing/article_ad3bbef6-8afe-11ea-9e21-bf815b9059f0.html|website=The Grand Island Independent|language=en|access-date=24 May 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|title="The Only Game in Town": Horse Racing Handle Up 176% Per Day in April|url=https://www.actionnetwork.com/horse-racing/horse-racing-betting-handle-surge-coronavirus|last=|first=|date=7 May 2020|website=The Action Network|language=en-US|access-date=25 May 2020}}</ref>

;Cancelled race meetings and reopenings<ref>{{cite web |title=COVID-19 Updates/Announcements |url=https://www.bloodhorse.com/horse-racing/articles/section/covid-19-updates-announcements |website=www.bloodhorse.com |accessdate=21 March 2020 |language=en}}</ref>

* [[Turf Paradise Race Course]], Arizona - cancel remaining meetings from 10 March and 2020-21 meeting are canceled.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.paulickreport.com/news/the-biz/we-are-not-going-to-take-on-that-liability-turf-paradise-cancels-meet-due-to-covid-19/|title='We Are Not Going To Take On That Liability': Turf Paradise Cancels Meet Due To COVID-19|date=13 August 2020|website=Horse Racing News &#124; Paulick Report}}</ref>

Government gives green light for British resumption on Monday &#124; Horse Racing News &#124; Racing Post}}</ref> Wales racing resume from 15 June <ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.igamingbusiness.com/news/welsh-horse-racing-resume-15-june|title=Welsh horse racing to resume from 15 June|date=2 June 2020|website=iGaming Business}}</ref> Scotland racing resume from 22 June.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.racingpost.com/news/racings-return/ayr-and-perth-primed-to-resume-as-scottish-government-begins-easing-lockdown/435262|work=[[Racing Post]]|title=Ayr and Perth primed to resume as Scottish government begins easing lockdown &#124; Horse Racing News &#124; Racing Post}}</ref>

April in Deutschland! &#124; Turf-Times Deutschland |website=www.turf-times.de |accessdate=27 March 2020}}</ref> racing resumed on 7 May.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.racingpost.com/news/coronavirus/germany-given-go-ahead-for-behind-closed-doors-meeting-at-hanover-on-thursday/433211|work=[[Racing Post]]|title=Germany given go-ahead for behind-closed-doors meeting at Hanover on Thursday &#124; Horse Racing News &#124; Racing Post}}</ref>

*[[Kawasaki Racecourse]] - 24 to 26 August and rescheduled on 31 August to 2 September,<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://news.netkeiba.com/?pid=news_view&no=175678|title=【地方競馬】重賞含む取り止めとなった川崎開催3日間は次週に代替開催 &#124; 競馬ニュース|website=netkeiba.com}}</ref> as one confirmed case on a [[Funabashi Racecourse|Funabashi]] based jockey.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://race.sanspo.com/nationalracing/news/20200825/nranws20082514120006-n1.html|title=２６日の川崎競馬も取りやめ|date=25 August 2020|website=サンスポZBAT！競馬}}</ref> Later, a total of six Funabashi jockeys are positive on COVID-19. Funabashi canceled five days of meetings from 29 August to 2 September.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://news.netkeiba.com/?pid=news_view&no=175636|title=【地方競馬】27・28日の川崎は騎手の所属を限定して開催、代替開催も決定 27日の船橋所属馬はすべて除外に &#124; 競馬ニュース|website=netkeiba.com}}</ref>

Also, Victorian Racing and New South Wales Metro racing are canceled by two days, during jockey [[Mark Zahra]] taken same flight with one confirm case.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.racenet.com.au/news/mark-zahra-tests-negative-to-coronavirus---racing-to-resume-20200326|title=Mark Zahra tests negative to coronavirus - racing to resume|website=www.racenet.com.au}}</ref>

==Ice hockey==

===International===
The [[2020 IIHF Women's World Championship|IIHF Women's World Championship]], [[2020 IIHF World Championship Division IV|IIHF World Championship Division IV]] and [[2020 Women's Ice Hockey World Championships|Women's Ice Hockey World Championships]] were all cancelled by the [[International Ice Hockey Federation]] due to the coronavirus.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://iihf.com/en/events/2020/ww/news/18296/women%E2%80%99s-worlds-cancelled |title=Women's Worlds cancelled |date=7 March 2020 |work=iihf.com}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.iihf.com/en/news/18277/iihf-cancels-march-tournaments |title=IIHF cancels March tournaments |date=2 March 2020 |work=iihf.com}}</ref> The federation also cancelled the [[2020 IIHF World U18 Championships|2020 event]] of one of its two official junior world championship tournaments, the [[IIHF World U18 Championship]].<ref>{{cite press release |title=IIHF cancels U18 Worlds |url=https://www.iihf.com/en/events/2020/wm18/news/18313/iihf-cancels-u18-world-chhmpionship |location=[[Plymouth Charter Township, Michigan]] & [[Ann Arbor, Michigan]], [[United States]] |publisher=[[International Ice Hockey Federation]] |first=Adam |last=Steiss |date=13 March 2020}}</ref> On 21 March, IIHF publicly announced that the senior men's world championships had also been cancelled.<ref>{{cite press release |title=2020 IIHF Ice Hockey World Championship cancelled |url=https://www.iihf.com/en/events/2020/wm/news/18344/2020-iihf-ice-hockey-world-championship-cancelled |location=[[Switzerland]] |publisher=[[International Ice Hockey Federation]] |website=iihf.com |first=Adam |last=Steiss |date=21 March 2020 | access-date=21 March 2020}}</ref>

===Europe===
As a result of the German government's ban on large events, the [[Deutsche Eishockey Liga]] announced on 10 March that it would cancel the remainder of its season, marking the first time in the league's history a champion would not be crowned. The top four teams at the time of the cancellation — [[EHC Red Bull München]], [[Adler Mannheim]], [[Straubing Tigers]], and [[Eisbaren Berlin]] — would advance to the [[Champions Hockey League]].<ref>{{cite press release |title=German League cancels season, won't crown champion as a result of coronavirus outbreak |url=https://thehockeynews.com/news/article/german-league-cancels-season-wont-crown-champion-as-a-result-of-coronavirus-outbreak |first=Jared |last=Clinton |publisher=[[The Hockey News]] |website=thehockeynews.com |date=10 March 2020 | access-date=15 March 2020}}</ref>

The [[Swedish Ice Hockey Association]] suspended all remaining hockey, the playoffs and qualification rounds, in the Swedish elite leagues on 15 March; no awarding of the [[Le Mat Trophy]] for the 2019/20 season nor transference of teams from the leagues' qualification plays for the 2020/21 season will happen as a result.<ref>{{cite news |title=Hockeysäsongen 2019/20 ställs in |url=https://www.hockeyallsvenskan.se/artikel/2ittak7t7-1el1/hockeysasongen-2019-20-stalls-in |publisher=[[HockeyAllsvenskan]] |language=Swedish |website=hockeyallsvenskan.se |date=10 March 2020 | access-date=15 March 2020}}</ref>
