===North America===
In early March 2020, the [[National Hockey League]] suspended media access to the locker rooms, saying that only official personnel would be allowed in after the games to limit person-to-person contact. On 12 March, the NHL, [[American Hockey League]], the leagues of the [[Canadian Hockey League]] ([[Ontario Hockey League]], [[Quebec Major Junior Hockey League]], and [[Western Hockey League]]), the [[United States Hockey League|USHL]], and [[ECHL]] announced that their [[2019–20 NHL season|2019–20 seasons]] would be indefinitely suspended.<ref>{{cite web |title=NHL pauses regular season because of coronavirus |url=https://www.nhl.com/news/nhl-coronavirus-status/c-316155530 |website=NHL.com |accessdate=12 March 2020 |date=12 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |last1=Gaydos |first1=Ryan |title=NHL suspends 2019–20 season over coronavirus outbreak |url=https://www.foxnews.com/sports/nhl-suspends-season-over-coronavirus-outbreak |website=Fox News |accessdate=12 March 2020 |date=12 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Kaplan |first1=Emily |title=NHL suspending play immediately due to virus |url=https://www.espn.com/nhl/story/_/id/28891430/sources-nhl-suspending-play-immediately-due-virus |accessdate=12 March 2020 |work=ESPN.com |date=12 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.wearegreenbay.com/community/health/coronavirus/green-bay-gamblers-season-suspended-due-to-covid-19/ |title=Green Bay Gamblers season suspended due to COVID-19 |last=Rose |first=Joshua |date=12 March 202 |work=[[WFRV-TV|WeAreGreenBay.com]] |publisher=[[Nexstar Media Group]] |accessdate=12 March 2020}}</ref>

On 12 March, the [[National Women's Hockey League]] postponed its [[Isobel Cup]] Final game indefinitely.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.sportsnet.ca/olympics/women-hockey/nwhl-postpones-2020-isobel-cup-final-due-covid-19-concerns/ |title=NWHL postpones 2020 Isobel Cup Final due to COVID-19 concerns |date=12 March 2020 |website=www.sportsnet.ca |language=en|access-date=6 April 2020}}</ref>

The ECHL announced on 14 March that the remainder of the season would be cancelled.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.espn.com/nhl/story/_/id/28904194/prudent-decision |title=ECHL cancels season amid concerns over virus |date=15 March 2020 |website=ESPN.com |language=en|access-date=15 March 2020}}</ref> The leagues of the CHL announced on 18 March that they would cancel the remainder of their regular seasons.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://thehockeynews.com/news/article/qmjhl-becomes-first-chl-league-to-cancel-remainder-of-regular-season |title=CHL leagues cancel remainder of regular season campaigns; playoff status still undetermined |last1=EllisMarch 18 |first1=Steven |last2=2020 |date=18 March 2020 |website=The Hockey News |language=en-CA|access-date=23 March 2020}}</ref> On 23 March, the CHL confirmed that all playoffs and the [[2020 Memorial Cup]] were cancelled.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://theprovince.com/sports/hockey/junior-hockey/covid-19-forces-cancellation-of-chl-playoffs-and-2020-memorial-cup |title=COVID-19 forces cancellation of CHL playoffs and 2020 Memorial Cup |date=23 March 2020 |website=The Province |language=en-CA|access-date=23 March 2020}}</ref>

[[Hockey Canada]], the governing body for amateur hockey in the country, cancelled the remainder of its season on 12 March. This included national championships such as the [[Telus Cup]] and [[Esso Cup]], as well as all regional and provincial playoffs, the [[Canadian Junior Hockey League]] playoffs, and the [[2020 Centennial Cup]].<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.hockeycanada.ca/en-ca/news/2020-news-hockey-canada-ends-season |title=Hockey Canada statement in response to coronavirus (COVID-19) |date=12 March 2020 |publisher=Hockey Canada}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://calgary.ctvnews.ca/hockey-canada-ends-season-cancels-championships-1.4851343 |title=Hockey Canada ends season, cancels championships |last=Hunt |first=Stephen |date=12 March 2020 |website=Calgary |language=en|access-date=13 March 2020}}</ref>

On 11 May, the AHL announced the conclusion of the [[2019–20 AHL season]], awarding all regular season trophies.<ref>{{cite web | url = https://www.cbc.ca/sports/hockey/ahl-season-cancelled-dave-andrews-1.5564344| title = American Hockey League pulls plug on rest of season due to COVID-19 pandemic| date = 11 May 2020| access-date = 11 May 2020| language = en| trans-title = }}</ref>
[[File:Edmonton Bubble (50168421076).jpg|thumb|Fencing and security for the [[National Hockey League|National Hockey League]]'s "bubble" in [[Edmonton]]. The [[2020 Stanley Cup playoffs]] were held in two hub city bubbles, Edmonton and [[Toronto]].]] 
On 26 May, the NHL and the [[National Hockey League Players' Association]] agreed on a basic framework to stage the [[Stanley Cup playoffs]] behind closed doors.<ref name=nhlhub>{{cite web|url=https://www.nhl.com/news/nhl-plans-to-return-with-24-team-stanley-cup-playoffs/c-317031010|title=NHL plans to return with 24 teams competing for Stanley Cup|last=Gulitti|first=Tom|website=www.nhl.com|date=13 July 2020|publisher=NHL Enterprises, L.P.}}</ref> The seeds would be based on each club's points percentage when the season paused on 12 March; with the 2019–20 season effectively ended on 11 March. The top four seeds in each conference would receive a bye into the playoffs and play in a round robbin tournament to determine playoff seeding; while the next eight seeds in each conference would play in a best-of-five series for the remaining playoff seeds. The NHL entered its second phase of "returning to play" on 8 June.<ref>{{Cite web|title=NHL to allow teams to reopen training facilities on June 8 - Sportsnet.ca|url=https://www.sportsnet.ca/hockey/nhl/nhl-allow-teams-reopen-training-facilities-june-8/|access-date=10 June 2020|website=[[Sportsnet]]|publisher=[[Rogers Sports & Media]]|date=4 June 2020}}</ref> On 10 July, the NHL announced that the games for the 2020 Stanley Cup playoffs would be hosted in two hub cities, [[Edmonton]], and [[Toronto]]. Toronto's [[Scotiabank Arena]] hosted games for the [[Eastern Conference (NHL)|Eastern Conference]]'s playoff qualifiers, quarterfinals, and semi-finals; while Edmonton's [[Rogers Place]] hosted the same rounds for the [[Western Conference (NHL)|Western Conference]]'s, in addition to both conference's finals, as well as the [[2020 Stanley Cup Final]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.cbssports.com/nhl/news/nhl-will-enter-phase-3-of-return-to-play-plan-on-july-10/#:~:text=The%20NHL%20is%20taking%20another,play%20plan%20on%20July%2010.&text=The%20NHL%20has%20previously%20stated,does%20end%20up%20resuming%20play.|title=NHL will enter Phase 3 of return to play plan on July 10|publisher=CBS Sports Digital|website=www.cbssports.com|last=Bengel|first=Chris|date=11 June 2020|accessdate=13 August 2020}}</ref> Players that entered the hub city "bubbles" were required to agree to protocols governing how camps operate, and the environment around where games are played, separating the hubs into "secure zones".<ref name=nhlsportsnet>{{cite web|url=https://www.sportsnet.ca/hockey/nhl/nhl-nhlpa-vote-accept-cba-return-play-plan-protocols/|title=NHL is back in business with ratification of CBA, return-to-play plan
|last=Johnston|first=Chris|website=www.sportsnet.ca|publisher=Rogers Digital Media|date=10 July 2020|accessdate=13 August 2020}}</ref>

From 28 to 31 July 24 NHL teams each played one exhibition game before the Stanley Cup playoff qualifiers began on 1 August.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.nhl.com/news/nhl-stanley-cup-qualifiers-exhibition-games-schedule/c-317433568|title=Exhibition schedule for Stanley Cup Qualifiers|website=www.nhl.com|publisher=NHL Enterprise, L.P.|date=31 July 2020|accessdate=13 August 2020}}</ref> The league conducted over 7,000 tests for COVID-19 during the first week of return-to-play, with the NHL reporting no positive cases.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.cnn.com/2020/08/03/us/nhl-coronavirus-spt-trnd/index.html|title=NHL announces no Covid-19 cases during first week of return to play|last=Kim|first=Allen|date=3 August 2020|website=www.cnn.com|publisher=Cable News Network}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.espn.com/nhl/story/_/id/29630040/how-nhl-kept-playoff-bubble-coronavirus-free-far|last1=Wyshynski|first1=Greg|last2=Kaplan|first2=Emily|work=ESPN|accessdate=13 August 2020|date=10 August 2020|title=How the NHL has kept its playoff bubble coronavirus-free -- so far|publisher=ESPN, Inc.}}</ref> The playoff qualifiers were concluded on 9 August, with the first round of the Stanley Cup playoffs beginning the day after.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2020/08/10/sports/hockey/nhl-playoffs-round-standings.html|work=The New York Times|title=The First Round of the N.H.L Playoffs Is Set. There Have Already Been Upsets.|publisher=New York Times Company|date=10 August 2020|accessdate=13 August 2020}}</ref> The entire 2020 Stanley Cup playoffs (including the qualifier rounds) were scheduled to last 66 days.<ref name=nhlsportsnet/> Because of the delays to the 2019–20 season, the [[2020–21 NHL season|2020/21 season]] will also be postponed until at least 1 December.<ref name="new schedule">{{cite web|url=https://www.sportsnet.ca/hockey/nhl/nhl-announces-tentative-dates-return-play-compressed-off-season/|title=NHL announces tentative dates for return to play, compressed off-season|first=Chris|last=Johnston|work=Sportsnet|date=10 July 2020|accessdate=21 August 2020}}</ref>

On 22 October, the NHL announced that the [[2022 NHL Winter Classic|2021 NHL Winter Classic]] and [[2021 NHL All-Star Game]] had been postponed. Both events could be held in 2022, possibly in the same respective locations - [[Target Field]] in [[Minneapolis]] and [[BB&T Center (Sunrise)|BB&T Center]] in [[Sunrise, Florida]] - with the All-Star Game depending on if NHL players are released to compete in the [[2022 Winter Olympics]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.nhl.com/news/nhl-postpones-2021-winter-classic-all-star-weekend/c-319501676/|title=NHL postpones Winter Classic, All-Star Weekend for this season|first=|last=|work=NHL Public Relations|date=22 October 2020|accessdate=22 October 2020}}</ref>

==Lacrosse==
The [[National Lacrosse League]] (NLL) temporarily suspended the [[2020 NLL season|2020 season]] on 12 March.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.nll.com/news/nll-statement-on-game-play-march-12-2020/ |title=NLL STATEMENT ON GAME PLAY (MARCH 12, 2020) |publisher=National Lacrosse League |website=nll.com |date=12 March 2020 |accessdate=12 March 2020}}</ref>

The NCAA officially announced the cancelation of the 2020 College Lacrosse Season on 12 March.<ref>{{Cite web|date=12 March 2020|title=NCAA Tournament and NIT canceled due to coronavirus pandemic|url=https://www.syracuse.com/orangesports/2020/03/ncaa-cancels-all-winter-and-spring-championships-including-ncaa-tournament-and-nit.html|access-date=14 July 2020|website=syracuse|language=en}}</ref> Beginning with the [[Ivy League]] canceling its season on 11 March, the NCAA followed canceling all spring season championships. Due to the cancelation of the season, the NCAA voted and approve the allocation of an extra year of eligibility for all of the athletes that missed their spring season.<ref>{{Cite web|last7=Email|last8=URLCopied!|first8=Copy Link|last9=Print|date=30 March 2020|title=NCAA approves extra year of eligibility for spring athletes, with a catch|url=https://www.latimes.com/sports/story/2020-03-30/ncaa-approves-extra-year-of-eligibility-for-spring-athletes-with-a-catch|access-date=14 July 2020|website=Los Angeles Times|language=en-US}}</ref>

[[Major League Lacrosse]] announced the postponement of the start of the 2020 season on 3 April in a statement from commissioner Alexander Brown.  The season was set to begin on 30 May, and then rescheduled to a shortened format from 16 to 26 July with all players and coaches being quarantined. The 6 teams  participated in a two-day training camp on 16–17 July, then a shortened season leading to a playoff crowning the [[Boston Cannons]] champions on 26 July.

The [[Premier Lacrosse League]] announced the postponement of the start of the 2020 season on 10 April.<ref>{{Cite web|title=Premier Lacrosse League Postpones Start of 2020 Season|url=https://www.uslaxmagazine.com/pro/pll/premier-lacrosse-league-postpones-start-of-2020-season#:~:text=The%20PLL's%20second%20season%20was,the%20ongoing%20COVID-19%20pandemic.|access-date=14 July 2020|website=www.uslaxmagazine.com|language=en}}</ref> The League announced the modified season that would take place called the [https://premierlacrosseleague.com/championship-series/ PLL Championship Series] on 6 May.<ref>{{Cite web|last=Slusher|first=Keenan|date=6 May 2020|title=Premier Lacrosse League announces PLL Championship Series|url=https://sports.nbcsports.com/2020/05/06/premier-lacrosse-league-announces-pll-championship-series/|access-date=14 July 2020|website=NBC Sports|language=en-US}}</ref> The series ran from 25 July through 9 August just outside of Salt Lake City, Utah, at [[Zions Bank Stadium]] with the teams being quarantined and playing in absence of fans.<ref>{{Cite web|last=|first=|last2=|date=|title=Premier Lacrosse League announces plan for quarantined tournament, hopes its model can be 'indicator' for others|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/sports/2020/05/06/premier-lacrosse-league-announces-plan-quarantined-tournament-hopes-its-model-can-be-indicator-others/|access-date=29 July 2020|website=Washington Post|language=en}}</ref> The 7 teams competed in a 14-game round-robin format to determine the standings for a single elimination tournament. On 9 August, the [[Whipsnakes Lacrosse Club]] became the champions of the 2020 PLL Season, defeating [[Chaos Lacrosse Club]] with a final score of 12-6 <ref>{{Cite web|title=Championship Series Schedule|url=https://premierlacrosseleague.com/championship-series-schedule/|access-date=20 August 2020|website=Premier Lacrosse League|language=en-US}}</ref>

==Motorsport==

{{main|Impact of the COVID-19 pandemic on motorsport}}

==Poker==
As of 18 March most casinos and other gaming venues worldwide have been closed indefinitely, and many upcoming live [[poker tournament]]s have been either postponed, canceled, or (in jurisdictions where currently permitted) moved to an [[online poker|online platform]]. Tournaments originally scheduled to be played live are now being played online, including the 2020 [[Irish Poker Open]].<ref name="IrishPokerOnline">{{cite web |last1=Pitt |first1=Matthew |title=partypoker To The Rescue! 2020 Irish Open Now Online |url=https://www.pokernews.com/news/2020/03/partypoker-to-the-rescue-2020-irish-open-now-online-36803.htm |website=pokernews.com |accessdate=28 June 2020 |date=17 March 2020}}</ref>

On 20 April, the 2020 [[World Series of Poker]] was postponed.<ref>{{cite web|title=World Series of Poker postponed amid pandemic|url=http://www.espn.com/chalk/story/_/id/29073571/world-series-poker-postponed-amid-coronavirus-pandemic-organizers-target-autumn-dates|first=David|last=Purdum|date=20 April 2020}}</ref>

The pandemic has resulted in a massive increase in online poker traffic.<ref name=PokerCovid>{{cite web |url=https://www.marketwatch.com/story/online-poker-betting-hits-a-record-high-during-the-pandemic-2020-05-29 |title=Online poker betting hits a record high during the pandemic |last=Blasi  |first=Weston |date=29 May 2020 |website=marketwatch.com |access-date=28 June 2020 }}</ref> It is believed to have directed both professional and recreational players who normally prefer live poker to online platforms due to the indefinite closure of most casinos and other live gaming venues worldwide, with even many [[Underground poker|unlicensed venues]] shutting down. In addition, the sudden dearth of live entertainment options due to the widespread disruption of the sports and entertainment schedules around the world is believed to have resulted in more than the usual number of casual players turning to online poker as an alternative. Many operators reported traffic of double or more the previous volume, depending on the time of day. {{Citation needed|date=April 2020}}

==Real Tennis==
The [[2021 Real Tennis World Championship|2020 Real Tennis World Championship]], scheduled to be held at [[Prested Hall, Feering|Prested Hall]] in [[Feering]], [[Essex]], [[United Kingdom]] was postponed on 12 March 2020 to October 2020 due to bans on indoor gatherings and sport and international travel restrictions.<ref>{{cite web |title=WC Challenge Postponed |url=https://www.irtpa.com/news/world-championships-news/wc-challenge-postponed/ |website=IRTPA}}</ref> The championships were further postponed to May 2021.<ref>{{cite web |title=Further WC Postponement |url=https://www.irtpa.com/news/irtpa-news/further-wc-postponement/ |website=IRTPA}}</ref> Additionally, other major tournaments including the 2020 French Open and Champions Trophy were cancelled outright.

==Rodeo==
The 2020 [[Houston Livestock Show and Rodeo]] was canceled on its ninth day after a festival attendee was diagnosed positive with the virus.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.click2houston.com/rodeo/2020/03/11/houston-rodeo-canceled-amid-growing-concerns-over-coronavirus/ |title=Houston Rodeo canceled; coronavirus patient attended Rodeo cookoff in February |last=Barker |first=Daniela Sternitzky-Di Napoli, Aaron |date=12 March 2020 |website=KPRC |language=en|access-date=12 March 2020}}</ref>

The 2020 [[Calgary Stampede]] was canceled.<ref>{{Cite web|last=Gilligan|first=Melissa|date=23 April 2020|title=2020 Calgary Stampede cancelled for first time in over 100 years amid COVID-19|url=https://globalnews.ca/news/6815098/covid-19-2020-calgary-stampede-update/|access-date=23 August 2020|website=Global News}}</ref>

The [[Professional Bull Riders]] organised its Atlanta event March 14-15 behind closed doors, then initially planned to hold events in Colorado.  The organisation shut down and initially planned to hold events in a bubble-type atmosphere at the PBR Performance Center in Pueblo, Colorado, before then planning to resume April 2 at the [[Lazy E Arena]] in Guthrie, Oklahoma.  Those events were subsequently postponed and the first of three Lazy E Arena events was held April 25-26, with a week off before PBR organised two more events at the same venue on consecutive weeks.  PBR eventually held a team event at [[South Point Arena]] in Las Vegas during June, again behind closed doors, before welcoming spectators back in July at the Denny Sanford Premier Center in South Dakota.  PBR subsequently cancelled all majors and moved the World Finals to AT&T Stadium in Arlington, Texas.

==Rowing==
Four [[Rowing at the 2020 Summer Olympics – Qualification|Olympic qualification regattas]] were cancelled, including the final qualification event scheduled to be held in [[Lucerne]], [[Switzerland]], from 17 to 19 May. All three events of the 2020 [[World Rowing Cup]] were also cancelled.<ref>{{cite web |title=Joint Decisions related to the impact of the Novel Coronavirus (COVID-19) on remaining Olympic and Paralympic qualification events |url=http://www.worldrowing.com/news/joint-decisions-related-the-impact-the-novel-coronavirus-covid-remaining-olympic-and-paralympic-qualification-events |website=World Rowing |accessdate=25 March 2020}}</ref>

[[The Boat Race 2020]], due to take place on the [[River Thames]] in [[London]] on 29 March, was cancelled.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.itv.com/news/anglia/2020-03-16/the-boat-race-has-been-cancelled-due-to-coronavirus/ |publisher=ITV |title=The Boat Race has been cancelled due to Coronavirus |date=16 March 2020 |accessdate=17 March 2020}}</ref>

==Rugby league==
The Australian/New Zealand [[National Rugby League]] was scheduled to continue with no spectators permitted in the stadiums; however, the entire season was suspended indefinitely on 23 March 2020.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.nrl.com/news/2020/03/23/nrl-suspends-competition-due-to-coronavirus-pandemic/ |title=NRL suspends competition due to coronavirus pandemic |date=23 March 2020 |work=National Rugby League |first=Dan|last=Walsh}}</ref> In line with an overall easings of restrictions in Australia, plans were announced which would see the season restarted from approximately 28 May.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.abc.net.au/news/2020-04-28/coronavirus-nrl-to-conduct-20-round-season/12194624?section=sport|title=NRL announces 20-round season, grand final to be played on October 25|publisher=ABC News |date=28 April 2020 |accessdate=28 April 2020}}</ref>
The NRL season recommenced on 28 May with a round 3 game played in Brisbane between the Brisbane Broncos and Parramatta Eels.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.nrl.com/news/2020/05/29/1.3-million-reasons-to-smile-nrl-return-most-watched-since-2014/|title=1.3 million reasons to smile: NRL return most-watched since 2014|date=29 May 2020|website=National Rugby League}}</ref> The match was played behind closed doors, and became the most-watched regular season NRL game since 2014.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.smh.com.au/sport/nrl/fake-yeews-the-story-behind-the-nrl-s-new-faux-crowd-noise-20200529-p54xsc.html|title=Fake yeews: The story behind the NRL's new faux crowd noise|first=Sam|last=Phillips|date=29 May 2020|website=The Sydney Morning Herald}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|last=Phillips|first=Sam|date=29 May 2020|title=Broncos-Eels clash most-watched regular-season NRL game since 2014|url=https://www.smh.com.au/sport/nrl/broncos-eels-clash-most-watched-regular-season-nrl-game-since-2014-20200529-p54xlf.html|website=The Sydney Morning Herald}}</ref>

In the northern hemisphere, [[Super League]] and the Rugby Football League's [[RFL Championship|Championship]] and [[RFL League 1|League 1]] suspended their seasons until 3 April as a result of the spread of coronavirus.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/sport/rugby-league/51911290 |title=Coronavirus: Rugby Football League suspends season until 3 April |date=16 March 2020 |work=BBC Sport|access-date=16 March 2020 |language=en-gb}}</ref> This was later revised to 2 August for [[Super League]], whilst the [[RFL Championship|Championship]] and [[RFL League 1|League 1]] were cancelled. The [[2020 Kangaroo tour of England]], which was scheduled to include three test matches between England and Australia in October and November, was cancelled on 1 June.<ref>{{cite web |last1=Woods |first1=Dave |title=England v Australia series in October and November cancelled |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/sport/rugby-league/52876245 |website=BBC Sport |accessdate=1 June 2020 |date=1 June 2020}}</ref>

In June 2020, the NRL received approval to begin admitting small amounts of spectators.<ref>{{Cite web|last=Proszenko|first=Adrian|date=5 June 2020|title=Government gives NRL permission for fans to attend matches from next week|url=https://www.smh.com.au/sport/nrl/government-gives-nrl-permission-for-fans-to-attend-matches-from-next-week-20200605-p55008.html|access-date=20 November 2020|website=The Sydney Morning Herald|language=en}}</ref> The [[2020 State of Origin series]] was delayed to November.<ref>{{Cite web|date=15 May 2020|title=Revealed — State of Origin dates locked in, venues still to be finalised|url=https://coupler.foxsports.com.au/api/v1/article/amp/nrl/nrl-premiership/live-ricky-slams-coaches-with-too-much-selfinterest-as-cartwright-is-overjoyed-to-receive-exemption/news-story/f5a612fbdefec31bbc135a29f6e72639|access-date=15 May 2020|website=Fox Sports|language=en}}</ref> was played with gradually increasing numbers of spectators. The final game was played at Brisbane's [[Suncorp Stadium]] with a near-capacity crowd of 49,155 spectators, making it one of the largest-attended sporting events since the onset of the pandemic. <ref>{{Cite news|last=Kemp|first=Emma|date=18 November 2020|title='The whole city was gridlocked': Brisbane heaves as fans allowed back en masse {{!}} Emma Kemp|language=en-GB|work=The Guardian|url=https://www.theguardian.com/sport/2020/nov/18/the-whole-city-was-gridlocked-brisbane-heaves-as-fans-allowed-back-en-masse|access-date=20 November 2020|issn=0261-3077}}</ref>

==Rugby union==
=== Europe ===
At the end of February and start of March, the [[2020 Six Nations Championship]] saw all games against [[Italy national rugby union team|Italy]] postponed due to the worsening situation in that country,<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/sport/rugby-union/51749254 |title=Coronavirus: England's Six Nations games against Italy postponed |date=5 March 2020 |work=BBC Sport|access-date=13 March 2020 |language=en-gb}}</ref> with games against the [[Scotland women's national rugby union team|Scotland women's team]] also cancelled as one of the players tested positive and the team went into isolation.<ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/sport/rugby-union/51777621 |title=Women's Six Nations: Scotland v France postponed after home player tests positive for coronavirus |date=6 March 2020 |work=BBC Sport|access-date=13 March 2020 |language=en-gb}}</ref> By 13 March, the competition had been suspended <ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/sport/rugby-union/51853907 |title=Six Nations: Wales v Scotland off because of coronavirus |date=13 March 2020 |work=BBC Sport|access-date=13 March 2020 |language=en-gb}}</ref> until late October. On 12 March, the [[Pro14]] European rugby competition was suspended <ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/sport/rugby-union/51858815 |title=Coronavirus: Pro14 suspended indefinitely due to coronavirus |date=12 March 2020 |work=BBC Sport|access-date=13 March 2020 |language=en-gb}}</ref> until 22 August.

=== North America ===
On 12 March, [[Major League Rugby]] suspended its third season for 30 days.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.majorleague.rugby/news/major-league-rugby-suspends-2020-season-for-30-days/ |title=MAJOR LEAGUE RUGBY SUSPENDS 2020 SEASON FOR 30 DAYS |website=Major League Rugby |language=en-US|access-date=19 March 2020}}</ref> The league later announced, on 18 March, that the season had been scrapped.<ref>{{Cite web|title=Major League Rugby cancels 2020 season, creates esports tournament|url=https://www.sportbusiness.com/news/major-league-rugby-cancels-2020-season-launches-esports-tournament/|date=19 March 2020|website=SportBusiness|language=en-US|access-date=4 May 2020}}</ref>

=== Oceania ===
In the [[2020 Super Rugby season]], two fixtures of Japanese team [[Sunwolves]] had been moved to Australia from Japan, while Australia announced on 12 March that beginning in the next round of fixtures, all matches held in Australia would be played with no spectators, but otherwise continue as normal. However, on 14 March, New Zealand (who fields five teams in the competition) announced that it will require 14 days self-isolation for any person that arrives in the country from outside of the Pacific Islands, regardless of origin and including New Zealand citizens. League organizer [[SANZAAR]] stated that it was evaluating the impact of this restriction,<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.foxsports.com.au/rugby/super-rugby/super-rugby-coronavirus-news-2020-new-zealand-government/news-story/794c8a43de0a3806ea699a7503063461 |title=Super Rugby season on verge of shutdown after NZ restrictions |date=14 March 2020 |website=Fox Sports |language=en-AU|access-date=14 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.rugby.com.au:443/news/2020/03/13/corona-virus-international-updates |title=Coronavirus: How rugby has been affected around the world |website=www.rugby.com.au |language=en|access-date=14 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.rugby.com.au:443/news/2020/03/12/super-rugby-waratahs-coronavirus |title=LOCKOUT: Coronavirus forces rugby behind closed doors next week but fans welcome at weekend |website=www.rugby.com.au |language=en|access-date=14 March 2020}}</ref> and ultimately announced later in the day that the season would be suspended following the completion of the weekend's fixtures.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.smh.com.au/sport/rugby-union/all-super-rugby-matches-to-be-cancelled-after-sunday-s-fixtures-20200314-p54a4u.html |title=All Super Rugby matches to be cancelled after Sunday's fixtures |last=Decent |first=Tom |date=14 March 2020 |website=The Sydney Morning Herald |language=en|access-date=14 March 2020}}</ref>

[[Rugby Australia]] and [[New Zealand Rugby]] announced that they would play regional tournaments beginning in July and June respectively  — [[Super Rugby AU]] and [[Super Rugby Aotearoa]] — between local teams who play in Super Rugby, to supplant the suspended season. The Sunwolves were prevented from competing in Super Rugby AU by the government, leading to the team disbanding on 1 June 2020 (the club had already planned to exit Super Rugby and cease operations after the 2020 season).<ref>{{Cite web|last=Grant|first=Joe|date=9 June 2020|title=Up to 35,000 fans expected to attend Super Rugby matches in New Zealand|url=https://www.sunjournal.com/2020/06/09/up-to-35000-fans-expected-to-attend-super-rugby-matches-in-new-zealand/|access-date=10 June 2020|website=Lewiston Sun Journal}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|title=Suncorp Stadium derby to open Super Rugby AU competition|url=https://www.rugby.com.au/news/2020/06/10/super-rugby-au-confirmation|access-date=10 June 2020|website=Rugby.com.au|language=en}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|title=Sunwolves won't compete in Super Rugby AU|url=https://www.rugby.com.au/news/2020/06/01/super-rugby-au-sunwolves|access-date=10 June 2020|website=Rugby.com.au|language=en}}</ref> 

Super Rugby Aotearoa games were initially held with no spectator restrictions, as New Zealand had lifted most restrictions on 8 June due to there having been no active cases and no new cases in the prior 17 days. Entry restrictions to New Zealand have remained in force throughout.<ref>{{Cite web|date=8 June 2020|title=NZ lifts restrictions, crowds free to attend Super Rugby|url=https://www.espn.com/rugby/story/_/id/29280090/new-zealand-lifts-covid-19-restrictions-crowds-free-attend-super-rugby-aotearoa|access-date=10 June 2020|website=ESPN.com|language=en}}</ref> Stadiums remained at full capacity through the first nine weeks of the competition, but a spike in locally transmitted cases led the country to reimpose restrictions on mass gatherings on 11 August,<ref>{{Cite news|last=Cheng|first=Amelia Wade and Derek|date=11 August 2020|title=Covid 19 coronavirus: Auckland in lockdown, rest of country in level 2 - Four cases of community transmission|language=en-NZ|work=NZ Herald|url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&objectid=12355759|access-date=31 August 2020|issn=1170-0777}}</ref> causing one match in the final round to be held behind closed doors and another to be cancelled and scored as a draw.<ref>{{Cite web|date=14 August 2020|title=Super Rugby Aotearoa: Blues-Crusaders game in Auckland is officially cancelled|url=https://www.stuff.co.nz/sport/rugby/super-rugby/300082181/super-rugby-aotearoa-bluescrusaders-game-in-auckland-is-officially-cancelled|access-date=31 August 2020|website=Stuff|language=en}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.espn.com/rugby/story/_/id/29675388/super-rugby-aotearoa-10-week-treat-uncertainty-surrounds-future |title=Super Rugby Aotearoa a 10-week treat, but uncertainty surrounds its future |first=Liam |last=Napier |website=ESPN.com |date=16 August 2020 |accessdate=1 October 2020}}</ref>

The South African clubs also staged their own regional league, [[Super Rugby Unlocked]], between its four teams, joined by the [[Cheetahs (rugby union)|Cheetahs]] from [[Pro14]], and the [[Griquas (rugby)|Griquas]] and [[Pumas (rugby team)|Pumas]] from the [[Currie Cup]].<ref>{{cite news|title=Springbok Showdown to kickstart South Africa's domestic rugby season|publisher=ESPN|url=https://www.espn.com/rugby/story/_/id/29901252/springbok-showdown-kickstart-south-africa-domestic-rugby-season/|accessdate=16 September 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|date=18 September 2020|title=Two trophies up for grabs when local rugby season resumes|work=SA Rugby|url=https://www.sarugby.co.za/news-features/articles/2020/09/18/two-trophies-up-for-grabs-when-season-resumes/|accessdate=19 September 2020}}</ref>

== Sailing ==
Two of the three [[2019–20 America's Cup World Series]] races – scheduled for in Sardinia, Italy in April<ref>{{cite web|title=AMERICA'S CUP WORLD SERIES SARDEGNA – CAGLIARI DUE TO THE COVID-19 PANDEMIC, THIS EVENT HAS BEEN CANCELLED|url=https://www.americascup.com/en/acws/sardegna|access-date=19 December 2020|publisher=Americas Cup}}</ref> and Portsmouth, UK in June<ref>{{cite web|title=UPDATE ON EMIRATES AMERICA’S CUP WORLD SERIES PORTSMOUTH EVENT|url=https://www.americascup.com/en/news/596_UPDATE-ON-EMIRATES-AMERICAS-CUP-WORLD-SERIES-PORTSMOUTH-EVENT|access-date=19 December 2020|publisher=Americas Cup}}</ref> – were cancelled due to the pandemic. The final event in Auckland, New Zealand in December was run as scheduled.

The 2020 [[Sydney to Hobart Yacht Race]] which was to begin on December 26 was cancelled due to a local outbreak of COVID in Sydney the week prior. It would be the first time the annual race had been cancelled since its inception in 1945.<ref>{{Cite web|date=2020-12-19|title=NSW coronavirus outbreak forces first Sydney to Hobart yacht cancellation in 76-year history|url=https://www.abc.net.au/news/2020-12-19/sydney-to-hobart-yacht-race-cancelled-due-to-nsw-coronavirus/13001142|access-date=2020-12-19|website=www.abc.net.au|language=en-AU}}</ref> 100 competitors had originally been expected, later reduced to 75 due to travel and economic restrictions.<ref>{{Cite web|last=|first=|date=2020-12-19|title=Covid-19 outbreak forces cancellation of Sydney to Hobart yacht race|url=http://www.theguardian.com/sport/2020/dec/19/organisers-hustle-to-save-sydney-to-hobart-race-amid-covid-19-fears|url-status=live|archive-url=|archive-date=|access-date=2020-12-19|website=the Guardian|language=en}}</ref>

==Shooting==
The 2020 [[ISSF World Cup]], which was to commence on 15 March in New Delhi, was postponed.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://economictimes.indiatimes.com/news/sports/virus-hits-indian-sports/articleshow/74519560.cms |title=Virus hits Indian sports |work=Economic Times |accessdate=7 March 2020}}</ref> The Olympic Test Event in Tokyo, originally scheduled for April 2020, was also canceled.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.issf-sports.org/news.ashx?newsid |title=Test Event "READY STEADY TOKYO" |publisher=International Shooting Sport Federation |accessdate=23 March 2020}}</ref>

The [[2020 European Shotgun Championships]] was cancelled.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.coni.it/it/news/17132-tiro-a-volo,-nuovi-criteri-di-qualificazione-carte-olimpiche-del-trap-in-palio-agli-europei-di-osijek,-valido-il-ranking-ad-aprile-2021.html|title=Tiro a Volo, le novità: per il Trap carte olimpiche dagli Europei di Osijek o dal ranking ad aprile 2021|publisher=coni.it|quote=Nel dettaglio, per il Tiro a Volo le Carte Olimpiche in palio nell’Europeo 2020 di Chateauroux (FRA) verranno assegnate durante la rassegna continentale 2021 in programma ad Osijek (CRO)|language=italian|date=27 May 2020|accessdate=30 May 2020}}</ref>

==Short track speed skating==
The 2020 [[World Short Track Speed Skating Championships]] in Seoul, South Korea scheduled 13–15 March were canceled.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://speedskating.ca/news-and-info/news/isu-officially-cancels-world-short-track-championships-in-south-korea-due-to-coronavirus |title=ISU Officially Cancels World Short Track Championships in South Korea due to Coronavirus &#124; Speed Skating Canada |website=speedskating.ca |accessdate=27 March 2020}}</ref> The [[International Skating Union]] initially announced they were trying to reschedule the tournament to the beginning of the 2020–21 season<ref>{{cite web|url=https://nos.nl/l/2325012|title=ISU wil afgelast WK shorttrack later dit jaar alsnog op kalender zetten|website=nos.nl|language=nl|access-date=29 March 2020}}</ref> but couldn't find a spot in the calendar.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://nos.nl/l/2330705|title=Nieuwe datum vinden lukt niet, dus definitief streep door WK shorttrack|website=nos.nl|language=nl|access-date=16 April 2020}}</ref>

For the 2020–21 season, the first four world cups, scheduled to be held in November and December in Canada, South Korea and China were cancelled.<ref name=":14">{{Cite web|title=Schaatskalender 2020/2021|url=https://www.schaatsen.nl/contentpagina-s/langebaan/schaatskalender-2020-2021/|access-date=2 October 2020|website=Schaatsen.nl}}</ref><ref name=":19">{{Cite web|title=ISU Announces Cancellation of Additional World Cup Competitions {{!}} Speed Skating Canada|url=https://www.speedskating.ca/news-and-info/news/isu-announces-cancellation-of-additional-world-cup-competitions|access-date=2 October 2020|website=www.speedskating.ca}}</ref>

==Snooker==
The [[2020 Gibraltar Open]] and its qualifying rounds took place from 11 to 15 March. For the first day, there was a limit of 100 spectators per session. On the remaining days, there were no spectators. A significant number of players withdrew, and there was a shortage of referees, with some early matches played without referees.<ref>{{cite news |title=Bizarre times at Gibraltar Open as games played without referees and player brings wrong cue |publisher=[[Metro (British newspaper)|Metro]] |first=Phil |last=Haigh |date=20 March 2020 |accessdate=30 March 2020 |url=https://metro.co.uk/2020/03/15/gibraltar-open-chaos-12400612/}}</ref>

The [[2020 Tour Championship]], originally scheduled for 17 to 22 March, was postponed until 20 to 26 June.

The [[2020 China Open (snooker)|2020 China Open]], originally scheduled for 30 March to 5 April, was indefinitely postponed.<ref>{{cite news |title=Coronavirus: China Open in Beijing postponed |url=https://www.bbc.com/sport/snooker/51325726 |publisher=[[BBC Sport]] |date=31 January 2020 |accessdate=31 March 2020}}</ref>

The [[2020 World Snooker Championship]], originally scheduled 18 April to 4 May, was postponed<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/sport/snooker/51964887 |title=Coronavirus: World Snooker Championship at Crucible postponed |date=20 March 2020 |accessdate=20 March 2020 |publisher=[[BBC Sport]]}}</ref> until 31 July.

The [[2020 World Women's Snooker Championship]], originally scheduled 22 to 27 June, has been postponed.<ref>{{cite web |title=World Women's Championship Postponed |url=https://wst.tv/world-womens-championship-postponed/ |date=31 March 2020 |accessdate=31 March 2020 |publisher=[[World Snooker Tour]]}}</ref>

==Speedcubing==
The [[World Cube Association]] announced on 19 March that all upcoming speedcubing competitions were to be canceled up to 19 April.<ref>{{cite web | title=WCA COVID-19 Situation Update (2020-03-19) |url=https://www.worldcubeassociation.org/posts/covid-19-situation-update-2020-03-19 |date=19 March 2020 |accessdate=12 May 2020 |publisher=[[World Cube Association]]}}</ref> This was later extended until 31 May.<ref>{{cite web | title=WCA COVID-19 Situation Update (2020-03-30) |url=https://www.worldcubeassociation.org/posts/covid-19-situation-update-2020-03-30 |date=30 March 2020 |accessdate=12 May 2020 |publisher=[[World Cube Association]]}}</ref> This included the cancellation of the biennual European and Asian Championships. An estimated 250+ competitions were affected by the pandemic.

== Speed skating ==
For the 2020–21 season, the first four world cups, scheduled to be held in November and December in Poland, Norway, the United States and Canada were cancelled.<ref name=":14" /><ref name=":19" />

==Squash==
The 2020 [[European Squash Individual Championships]], scheduled to take place in [[Eindhoven]], the Netherlands from 29 April to 2 May are canceled.<ref name="nu.nl"/>

==Surfing==
The 2020 [[World Surf League]], which was due to start in Australia on 26 March, was on hold until at least June. The first event of the season, the [[Quiksilver Pro Gold Coast|Corona Open Gold Coast]], was canceled, while the second and third events, the [[Rip Curl Pro|Rip Curl Pro Bells Beach]] and [[Margaret River Pro]], were postponed.<ref>{{cite web |title=WSL Cancels All Events In March |url=https://www.worldsurfleague.com/posts/449880/wsl-cancels-all-events-in-march |website=World Surf League |accessdate=19 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |title=WSL Cancels Or Postpones Events Through May |url=https://www.worldsurfleague.com/posts/450379/wsl-cancels-or-postpones-events-through-may |website=World Surf League |accessdate=19 March 2020}}</ref> On 17 July it was announced that all but the final 2020 season events in Hawaii would become non-championship events known as the WSL Countdown, starting with the Rumble at the Ranch in Lemoore, California.  The December 2020 events in Hawaii, the Maui Pro and Pipe Masters, will start a new wraparound season for 2020-21.

The [[2020 ISA World Surfing Games]], scheduled to be held from 9 to 17 May in [[El Salvador]], were postponed until 8 to 16 May 2021.<ref>{{cite web |title=ISA Announces Postponement of World Surfing Games to May 2021 |url=https://www.isasurf.org/isa-announces-postponement-of-world-surfing-games-to-may-2021/ |website=International Surfing Association |accessdate=1 August 2020}}</ref>

==Swimming==
The [[2020 International Swimming League]] was staged behind closed doors at [[Budapest|Budapest's]] [[Danube Arena]], with all personnel staying within a hotel on nearby [[Margaret Island]].<ref>{{Cite news|last=Higgins|first=Louise Radnofsky and Laine|date=7 November 2020|title=Olympic Sports Are Forming Bubbles to Save Their Seasons—and Tokyo 2021|language=en-US|work=Wall Street Journal|url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/olympic-sports-are-forming-bubbles-to-save-their-seasonsand-tokyo-2021-11604761200|access-date=20 November 2020|issn=0099-9660}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|date=9 September 2020|title=ISL season to be largely held in Budapest "bubble" in bid to combat COVID-19|url=https://www.insidethegames.biz/articles/1098241/isl-swimming-season-two-budapest|access-date=20 November 2020|website=www.insidethegames.biz}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|title=Your guide to season two of the ISL|language=en-GB|work=BBC Sport|url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/sport/swimming/54543738|access-date=20 November 2020}}</ref>

==Table tennis==
The [[2020 World Team Table Tennis Championships]], which was scheduled to be held from 22–29 March in [[Busan]], [[South Korea]], was postponed to 27 September – 4 October.<ref>{{cite web |title=2020 World Table Tennis Championships postponed due to COVID-19 |url=https://www.ittf.com/2020/02/25/2020-world-table-tennis-championships-postponed-due-covid-19/ |website=ITTF |date=25 February 2020 |accessdate=22 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |title=New dates for 2020 World Table Tennis Championships|url=https://www.ittf.com/2020/04/07/new-dates-2020-world-table-tennis-championships/|website=ITTF |date=7 April 2020 |accessdate=7 April 2020}}</ref>

The [[2020 ITTF-ATTU Asian Cup]] was scheduled to be held from 28 February to 1 March in [[Hainan]], [[China]], but was postponed until later in the year.<ref>{{cite web |title=Postponement of 2020 Asian Cup |url=http://www.attu.org/en/news/1057 |website=ATTU |accessdate=22 March 2020}}</ref>

Seven events on the [[2020 ITTF World Tour]] have also been either cancelled or postponed, including the [[China Open (table tennis)|China Open]] and the [[Japan Open (table tennis)|Japan Open]].<ref>{{cite web |title=2020 ITTF World Tour Japan Open postponed due to COVID-19 |url=https://www.ittf.com/2020/03/10/2020-ittf-world-tour-japan-open-postponed-due-covid-19/ |website=ITTF |date=10 March 2020 |accessdate=22 March 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |title=Hong Kong and China Opens postponed due to COVID-19 |url=https://www.ittf.com/2020/03/20/hong-kong-china-opens-postponed-due-covid-19/ |website=ITTF |date=20 March 2020 |accessdate=22 March 2020}}</ref> Four [[Table tennis at the 2020 Summer Olympics – Qualification|Olympic qualifying events]], scheduled to be held in April, were also postponed.<ref>{{cite web |title=ITTF consider Tokyo 2020 Olympic qualification measures after events postponed |url=https://www.insidethegames.biz/articles/1092033/ittf-tokyo-2020-qualification-plans |website=Inside The Games |accessdate=22 March 2020}}</ref>

==Ten-pin bowling==
When the pandemic was declared, the [[PBA World Series of Bowling]] was about to take place at the [[South Point Hotel, Casino & Spa]] in [[Enterprise, Nevada]].  The [[Professional Bowlers Association]] then decided to advance the WSOB World Championship from 18 March 2020 to 15 March 2020, banning spectator admission.  The Animal Pattern Championships were postponed and eventually moved to [[Centreville, Virginia]], to take place in October,<ref>{{cite web |title=World Series of Bowling to resume next week  |url=https://www.flobowling.com/articles/6777618-wsob-to-resume-next-week |website=FloBowling |date=25 September 2020 |accessdate=29 September 2020}}</ref> while the USA vs. The World match was canceled.  The [[USBC Masters]] - scheduled for 29 March in [[Reno, Nevada]] -  and the PBA-PWBA Mixed Doubles competition - scheduled for 5 July in [[Denver]] - were also canceled.

The [[PBA League]] event was postponed from 21–23 July to 27–30 September and relocated from [[Portland, Maine]] to Centreville.

The PBA Playoffs were also postponed.  The 24-player, single-elimination tournament was scheduled to begin on 6 April in [[Norco, California]], then move on to [[Lone Tree, Colorado]] and [[Euless, Texas]] before semifinals and finals on 17 May in [[North Brunswick, New Jersey]].  The playoffs were rescheduled for 10 and 11 October, with one live telecast followed by a series of [[broadcast delay|delayed broadcasts]] until 8 November.  All rounds were held in Centreville.

The PBA added three exhibition events to its schedule: PBA Strike Derby on 7 June, PBA Summer Clash on 13 June, and King of the Lanes<ref>{{cite web |title=New PBA King of the Lanes series will be live on FS1 in July  |url=https://www.pba.com/articles/New-PBA-King-of-the-Lanes-series-will-be-live-on-FS1-in-July |website=Professional Bowlers Association |date=18 June 2020 |accessdate=29 September 2020}}</ref> from 20 to 22 July.  All competitions occurred in [[Jupiter, Florida]].

==Tennis==
In one of the first major U.S. sport cancellations of the pandemic, the [[2020 BNP Paribas Open]] [[tennis]] tournament in [[Indian Wells, California]] was postponed on 8 March 2020 as a precautionary measure due to the [[COVID-19 pandemic in California|rising cases in California]] (the state where it was held), with organizers stating they planned to seek a new date. This would leave out itself to effectively cancel the tournament.<ref>{{Cite news|last1=Rothenberg|first1=Ben|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2020/03/08/sports/coronavirus-indian-wells-canceled.html|title=Indian Wells Tennis Tournament Canceled Because of Coronavirus Outbreak|date=8 March 2020|work=The New York Times|access-date=7 April 2020|last2=Clarey|first2=Christopher|language=en-US|issn=0362-4331}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.usatoday.com/story/sports/columnist/dan-wolken/2020/03/08/coronavirus-indian-wells-cancellation-potential-sports-turning-point/4997987002/|title=Opinion: Indian Wells cancellation could be turning point for sports and coronavirus|last=Wolken|first=Dan|website=USA Today|language=en-US|access-date=7 April 2020}}</ref> On 12 March, [[List of mayors of Miami|Mayor of Miami]] [[Carlos A. Giménez]] ordered the cancellation of the [[Miami Open (tennis)|Miami Open]] pursuant to the state of emergency in [[Miami-Dade County]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.espn.com/tennis/story/_/id/28891183/miami-open-canceled-coronavirus-outbreak|title=Miami Open becomes latest top tourney canceled|date=12 March 2020|website=ESPN.com|language=en|access-date=13 April 2020}}</ref>

On 12 March, the [[Association of Tennis Professionals|ATP]] announced that in response to the aforementioned cancellations among others, they would suspend events for at least six weeks. The [[International Tennis Federation]] also suspended play through at least 20 April, and the [[Women's Tennis Association|WTA]] canceled [[WTA Tour]] events through 12 April.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.espn.com/tennis/story/_/id/28891268/atp-suspends-men-tennis-tournaments-six-weeks|title=ATP, ITF announce six-week shutdown over virus|date=12 March 2020|website=ESPN.com|language=en|access-date=13 April 2020}}</ref> On 16 March, the WTA suspended play through 2 May.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.espn.com/tennis/story/_/id/28910506/wta-suspends-tour-2-due-coronavirus|title=WTA suspends tour until May 2 due to virus|date=16 March 2020|website=ESPN.com|language=en|access-date=13 April 2020}}</ref>

On 16 March, the start of the [[2020 French Open]] was postponed from 24 May to 20 September and then to 27 September on 16 June, and the ATP and WTA jointly announced that their suspension of play had been extended through 7 June.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.espn.com/tennis/story/_/id/28922126/tennis-tours-suspend-play-june-7-eliminating-clay-court-circuit|title=ATP, WTA suspend tour play until June 7|date=18 March 2020|website=ESPN.com|language=en|access-date=13 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2020/03/17/sports/tennis/french-open-postponed.html |title=The French Open Is Postponed, to the Surprise of the Tours |last=Clarey |first=Christopher |newspaper=The New York Times |date=17 March 2020}}</ref> On 1 April, [[The Championships, Wimbledon|Wimbledon]] was canceled for the first time since [[World War II]], while the ATP and WTA announced that their suspension will be extended through 13 July.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.atptour.com/en/news/atp-wta-tours-announce-further-suspension-wimbledon|title=ATP & WTA Announce Further Suspension Of Tours|website=ATP Tour|access-date=13 April 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/sport/tennis/52104196 |title=Wimbledon cancelled due to coronavirus – where does that leave tennis in 2020? |date=1 April 2020 |work=BBC Sport|access-date=4 April 2020 |language=en-gb}}</ref> On 15 May, the suspension was extended through 3 August.<ref>{{Cite news|date=15 May 2020|title=Tennis extends coronavirus suspension: ATP and WTA Tours on further hold|language=en-GB|work=BBC Sport|url=https://www.bbc.com/sport/tennis/52676023|access-date=10 June 2020}}</ref>

Several exhibition tennis competitions with modified rules emerged in the wake of the pandemic, including the [[Ultimate Tennis Showdown]] in [[Nice]], France,<ref>{{Cite web|date=11 June 2020|title=No. 3 Thiem to play in Ultimate Tennis Showdown|url=https://www.espn.com/tennis/story/_/id/29298027/dominic-thiem-gives-ultimate-tennis-showdown-fourth-top-10|access-date=26 July 2020|website=ESPN.com|language=en}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|date=20 July 2020|title=What we learned from tennis' COVID-19 shutdown|url=https://www.espn.com/tennis/story/_/id/29481273/what-learned-tennis-covid-19-shutdown|access-date=26 July 2020|website=ESPN.com|language=en}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|last=Wolken|first=Dan|title=New brand of tennis: Serena Williams' coach pushes for faster pace and a more dynamic show|url=https://www.usatoday.com/story/sports/columnist/dan-wolken/2020/06/11/serena-williams-coach-pushes-faster-pace-dynamic-show-uts/5337646002/|access-date=26 July 2020|website=USA TODAY|language=en-US}}</ref> and the [[Adria Tour]] — an attempted series of tennis events in [[Southeast Europe]] organized by [[List of ATP number 1 ranked singles tennis players|world No. 1]] [[Novak Djokovic]]. The latter received notability for not restricting attendance, and was ultimately halted before the finals of its second leg in [[Croatia]]<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.croatiaweek.com/croatias-health-minister-coronavirus-at-zadar-tennis-tournament-is-a-big-warning/ |website=CroatiaWeek |date=22 June 2020 |title=Croatia's health minister: Coronavirus at Zadar tennis tournament is a big warning}}</ref> after [[Grigor Dimitrov]] tested positive for COVID-19. Multiple players involved — involving Djokovic himself — also contracted the virus.<ref>{{Cite web|date=23 June 2020|title=Djokovic has tested positive for coronavirus|url=https://www.espn.com/tennis/story/_/id/29351887/novak-djokovic-tested-positive-coronavirus|access-date=23 June 2020|website=ESPN.com|language=en}}</ref><ref name=":03">{{Cite web|date=22 June 2020|title=Viktor Troicki becomes fifth Adria Tour participant to test positive for coronavirus - report|url=https://www.eurosport.com/tennis/adria-tour/2020/viktor-troicki-becomes-fifth-adria-tour-participant-to-test-positive-for-coronavirus-report_sto7784154/story.shtml|access-date=23 June 2020|website=Eurosport}}</ref>

On 16 April, the [[United States Tennis Association]] announced the formation of an advisory group to evaluate whether the [[2020 US Open (tennis)|US Open]] would be played, with plans expected to be announced by June. USTA chief Mike Dowse stated that it was "highly unlikely" the tournament would be played behind closed doors, since it was "not really in the spirit of the celebration of tennis, and it also goes back to the health and wellbeing of our players and support staff that help run the tournament". He added that "on one sense we're very fortunate that we are the fourth Grand Slam to go, so time is on our side at this point." The [[COVID-19 pandemic in New York (state)|state of New York]] (which at one point, had more cases than any foreign country worldwide),<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.businessinsider.com/new-york-state-more-coronavirus-cases-than-any-country-worldwide-2020-4|title=New York state now has more confirmed coronavirus cases than any country in the world|first=John|last=Haltiwanger|website=Business Insider}}</ref> and especially the tournament's host, [[COVID-19 pandemic in New York City|New York City]], saw the largest initial impact of the pandemic in the United States.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.bbc.com/sport/football/52316965|title=US Open: 'Unlikely' tournament will be played behind closed doors|date=16 April 2020|work=BBC Sport|access-date=17 April 2020|language=en-GB}}</ref>

On 16 June 2020 Governor [[Andrew Cuomo]] announced that it had authorised the U.S. Open to be played in New York on its original dates, subject to safety protocols developed by the USTA and being closed to spectators. It was also announced that to reduce travel, the preceding [[Cincinnati Masters]] (Western & Southern Open) would be re-located to the same venue as the US Open, with both tournaments held over consecutive weeks.<ref>{{Cite web|date=16 June 2020|title=N.Y. Gov. Cuomo gives go-ahead for US Open|url=https://www.espn.com/tennis/story/_/id/29318557/ny-gov-cuomo-gives-ok-us-open-held-august|access-date=26 July 2020|website=ESPN.com|language=en}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|last=Baum|first=Dave Clark and Adam|title=The 2020 Western & Southern Open will be played in New York this summer|url=https://www.cincinnati.com/story/sports/tennis/2020/06/16/cuomo-allows-nyc-tennis-w-s-open-may-replace-u-s-open-qualifying/3198764001/|access-date=26 July 2020|website=The Enquirer|language=en-US}}</ref> The next day, the 2020 Canadian Open (originally scheduled for early-August as one of the first events to be held) was cancelled in full (the women's WTA Premier half of the tournament in Montreal had already been cancelled in April, while the ATP Masters 1000 men's tournament was still tentative), tentatively leaving the WTA International [[Palermo Ladies Open]], and the ATP 500/WTA International [[Washington Open (tennis)|Washington Open]] as the first two post-resumption events.<ref>{{Cite web|date=17 June 2020|title=Toronto loses Rogers Cup men's event for 2020 because of COVID-19|url=https://toronto.ctvnews.ca/toronto-loses-rogers-cup-men-s-event-for-2020-because-of-covid-19-1.4987910|access-date=4 July 2020|website=CTV News Toronto|language=en}}</ref> On 21 July, it was announced that the Washington Open had been cancelled.<ref>{{Cite news|last=Clarey|first=Christopher|date=21 July 2020|title=Men's Tennis Event in Washington Is Canceled|language=en-US|work=The New York Times|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2020/07/21/sports/citi-open-washington-canceled.html|access-date=26 July 2020|issn=0362-4331}}</ref> Two days later, the ATP and WTA cancelled all upcoming tournaments in China (including the [[WTA Finals]]), in respect of a moratorium by the [[General Administration of Sport of China|General Administration of Sport]] on most international events in the country through the end of 2020.<ref>{{Cite web|date=24 July 2020|title=WTA Finals, 10 other tourneys in China canceled|url=https://www.espn.com/tennis/story/_/id/29526842/wta-finals-10-other-tennis-tournaments-china-canceled|access-date=26 July 2020|publisher=Associated Press|language=en}}</ref> On 4 August, the annual [[Madrid Open (tennis)|Madrid Open]], to be held in [[Madrid]], Spain, was first postponed from the regular May schedule, then initially rescheduled to September, but it was given a complete cancellation due to the [[COVID-19 pandemic in Spain|resurgence of coronavirus cases in the country]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.madrid-open.com/en/mutua-news/official-statement-from-the-mutua-madrid-open-2/|title=Official Statement from the Mutua Madrid Open|publisher=Mutua Madrid Open|date=4 August 2020}}</ref>

From mid-August 2020, one case apiece was recorded in connection with tournaments in [[2020 Advantage Cars Prague Open|Prague]],<ref>{{cite web|url=https://twitter.com/ATPMediaInfo/status/1294660928458432512?s=20 |title=Tweet |website=twitter.com |accessdate=2020-12-13}}</ref> [[2020 Internazionali di Tennis Città di Todi|Todi]],<ref>{{cite web|url=https://twitter.com/ATPMediaInfo/status/1295439327657418755?s=20|title=Tweet |website=twitter.com |accessdate=2020-12-13}}</ref> and [[2020 US Open (tennis)|New York]].<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.straitstimes.com/sport/tennis/tennis-coronavirus-case-found-in-us-open-bubble|title=Tennis: Coronavirus case found in US Open 'bubble'|date=19 August 2020|website=The Straits Times}}</ref> [[Benoît Paire]] tested positive just prior to the [[2020 US Open (tennis)|US Open]] and was withdrawn from the tournament.<ref>{{Cite web|url=http://www.theguardian.com/sport/2020/aug/30/benoit-paire-tests-positive-for-covid-19-on-eve-of-us-open|title=Benoît Paire 'tests positive for Covid-19' on eve of US Open|date=30 August 2020|website=the Guardian}}</ref>

===Affected players and personnel===
A number of notable professional tennis players, coaches, or commentators have contracted [[Coronavirus disease 2019|COVID-19]] in 2020. Affected players include [[Borna Ćorić|Ćorić]], [[Grigor Dimitrov|Dimitrov]], [[Novak Djokovic|Djokovic]], [[Fiona Ferro|Ferro]], [[Fabio Fognini|Fognini]], [[David Goffin|Goffin]], [[Simona Halep|Halep]], [[Rosalie van der Hoek|van der Hoek]], [[Anna Kalinskaya|Kalinskaya]], 
[[Karen Khachanov|Khachanov]], [[Corentin Moutet|Moutet]], [[Kei Nishikori|Nishikori]], [[Benoît Paire|Paire]], [[Sam Querrey|Querrey]], [[Thiago Seyboth Wild|Seyboth Wild]], [[Frances Tiafoe|Tiafoe]], [[Viktoriya Tomova|Tomova]], [[Viktor Troicki|Troicki]], [[Fernando Verdasco|Verdasco]] and [[Markéta Vondroušová|Vondroušová]]. Also affected were coaches [[Franco Davín]], [[Groh|Christian Groh]], and [[Goran Ivanišević]], in addition to commentator [[Patrick McEnroe]]. (Certain other coaches or spouses of the above returned a positive test for the disease.)

Earlier in the year, controversial tennis star [[Bernard Tomic]] generated media interest after conflicting claims of exposure to the virus.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.theguardian.com/sport/blog/2020/mar/17/bernard-tomic-australian-tennis-self-isolating-coronavirus|title=Bernard Tomic endures blizzard of uncharitable scorn in self-isolation|first=Kevin|last=Mitchell|date=17 March 2020|via=www.theguardian.com}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.tennisworldusa.org/tennis/news/Tennis_Interviews/85690/bernard-tomic-reportedly-admitted-to-andrea-petkovic-he-lied-about-coronavirus-/|title=Bernard Tomic reportedly admitted to Andrea Petkovic he lied about coronavirus|website=Tennis World USA}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Y7k2pejwwzI |title=Video |website=www.youtube.com |accessdate=2020-12-13}}</ref>

==Triathlon==
The World Triathlon Executive Board, met via teleconference this Friday morning, has decided to extend the suspension of all activities of the International Federation until 30 June, due to the current situation worldwide with the COVID-19 outbreak. This suspension includes WTS Yokohama, three African (ATU) cups, three American (PATCO) events, four Asian (ASTC) cups, one event in Oceania (OTU) and eight in Europe, (ETU) plus the Yokohama Paratriathlon Series and Paratriathlon World Cup.

==Ultimate==
On 24 March, the World Flying Disc Federation announced to cancel or postpone all world championships over the next six months. This included the World Ultimate and Guts Championships (WUGC), World Junior Ultimate Championships (WJUC) and the World Masters Ultimate Championships (WMUC) due to the rapid spread of coronavirus.North America's national body for ultimate, USA Ultimate, also canceled all scheduled club and college tournaments as well as the suspension of the semi-professional league, the AUDL, from commencing the 2020 season.{{citation needed|date=May 2020}}

==Volleyball==
On 12 March, The [[National Collegiate Athletic Association]] (NCAA) cancelled the Spring 2020 men's volleyball championships due to concern over the coronavirus.<ref>{{Cite web|title=NCAA cancels remaining 2020 winter and spring championships {{!}} NCAA.com|url=https://www.ncaa.com/news/basketball-men/article/2020-03-12/ncaa-cancels-remaining-2020-winter-and-spring-championships|website=www.ncaa.com|language=en|access-date=29 May 2020}}</ref>

On 13 March, the [[Fédération Internationale de Volleyball|International Volleyball Federation]] (FIVB) decided to postpone the Nations League for [[2020 FIVB Volleyball Men's Nations League|men]] (finals scheduled for [[Turin]], Italy) and [[2020 FIVB Volleyball Women's Nations League|women]] until after the [[2020 Summer Olympics]] caused by the outbreak of coronavirus.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.fivb.com/en/about/news/fivb-announces-changes-to-events-calendar?id=90648 |title=FIVB announces changes to events calendar |date=13 March 2020 |website=FIVB|access-date=14 March 2020}}</ref>  On 8 May, the FIVB announced that the Nations League competitions were cancelled.

==Water polo==

===International===
The [[2020 Women's Water Polo Olympic Qualification Tournament]] was scheduled to take place in [[Trieste]], [[Italy]], 8–15 March 2020. On 28 February 2020, [[FINA|International Swimming Federation]] (FINA) announced that the tournament would be postponed to 17–24 May due to the coronavirus outbreak, then it was moved again to 17–24 January 2021 due to the [[COVID-19 pandemic in Italy|outbreak in the country]].<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.fina.org/news/fina-announcement-fina-womens-water-polo-olympic-games-qualification-tournament |date=28 February 2020 |title=FINA ANNOUNCEMENT: FINA Women's Water Polo Olympic Games Qualification Tournament |publisher=[[FINA]] |website=fina.org |access-date=12 March 2020}}</ref>

On 12 March, FINA announced that several international water polo tournaments would be postponed due to the coronavirus pandemic. The [[2020 Men's Water Polo Olympic Qualification Tournament]] due to take place in [[Rotterdam]], [[Netherlands]], 22–29 March, would be postponed to 31 May – 7 June, then it was postponed again to 21–28 February 2021. The [[2020 FINA Men's Water Polo World League]] and [[2020 FINA Women's Water Polo World League]] would be postponed to September–October 2020.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.fina.org/news/pr-16-first-meeting-fina-covid-19-taskforce |date=12 March 2020 |title=PR 16 – First meeting of FINA COVID-19 taskforce |publisher=[[FINA]] |website=fina.org |access-date=12 March 2020}}</ref>

===Asia===
[[2020 Asian Water Polo Championship]], the Asian continental qualification for the [[Water polo at the 2020 Summer Olympics|2020 Olympic water polo tournament]], was scheduled to take place in [[Nur-Sultan]], [[Kazakhstan]], 12–16 February 2020.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://astanatimes.com/2020/01/kazakh-capital-to-host-olympics-water-polo-asian-pre-qualification-tournament/ |first=Nurdana |last=Adylkhanova |date=31 January 2020 |title=Kazakh capital to host Olympics water polo Asian pre-qualification tournament |publisher=Astana Times |website=astanatimes.com |access-date=12 March 2020}}</ref> In late January the event was canceled as the Kazakh Government suspended all flights and visas from [[China]] due to concerns about the coronavirus outbreak in the country.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.swimmingworldmagazine.com/news/coronavirus-claims-first-tokyo-olympic-victim-2020-asian-water-polo-championships/ |first=Michael |last=Randazzo |date=13 February 2020 |title=Coronavirus Claims First Tokyo Olympic Victim: 2020 Asian Water Polo Championships |publisher=[[Swimming World]] |website=swimmingworldmagazine.com |access-date=12 March 2020}}</ref> In mid-February [[Asia Swimming Federation]] decided to use the final ranking of the [[Water polo at the 2018 Asian Games|2018 Asian Games]] to allocate its continental quotas.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://total-waterpolo.com/asian-federation-decides-kazakhstan-and-china-goes-to-tokyo/ |first=Ivan |last=Curcic |date=14 February 2020 |title=Asian Federation decides: Kazakhstan and China go to Tokyo |publisher=Total Waterpolo |website=total-waterpolo.com |access-date=12 March 2020}}</ref>

===Europe===
On 28 February 2020, [[LEN|European Swimming League]] (LEN) announced that the match of [[2019–20 LEN Champions League]] Day 10 between [[Ferencvárosi TC (men's water polo)|Ferencváros]] (Hungary) and [[Pro Recco]] (Italy), and the match of [[2019–20 LEN Euro Cup]] semifinal between [[Egri VK]] (Hungary) and [[AN Brescia]] (Italy) would be postponed due to the coronavirus outbreak.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www2.len.eu/?p=16594 |date=28 February 2020 |title=Two matches postponed – Euro Cup & Champions League |publisher=[[LEN]] |website=len.eu |access-date=12 March 2020}}</ref>

On 11 March 2020, LEN announced that all eight matches of 2019–20 LEN Champions League Day 11, the second leg of the [[2019–20 LEN Euro League Women]] quarter-finals, and the 2020 men's U19 European Championships qualification tournaments would be postponed to later dates due to the coronavirus pandemic.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://swimswam.com/len-postpones-upcoming-water-polo-competitions/ |date=11 March 2020 |title=LEN POSTPONES UPCOMING WATER POLO COMPETITIONS |publisher=[[LEN]] |website=Swim Swam |access-date=5 September 2020 }}</ref>

===North America===
On 11 March 2020, the [[USA Water Polo]] (USAWP) announced that the 2020 ODP Girls National Water Polo Championship would be postponed, and the exhibition matches scheduled to be played on 19–21 March 2020 in [[California]] between [[United States men's national water polo team|United States]] and [[Spain men's national water polo team|Spain]] men's national water polo teams would be canceled.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://usawaterpolo.org/news/2020/3/11/general-2020-odp-girls-national-championship-postponed-usa-mens-national-team-series-with-spain-canceled.aspx |date=11 March 2020 |title=2020 ODP Girls National Championship Postponed; USA Men's National Team Series With Spain Canceled |publisher=[[USA Water Polo]] |website=usawaterpolo.org |access-date=22 March 2020}}</ref>

On 16 March 2020, USAWP announced that the inaugural USA Water Polo Division III Women's National Championship scheduled for 8–10 May 2020 in [[Southern California]] would be rescheduled for May 2021; and week three of the 2020 National Water Polo League and the 2020 National League Championship/Fisher Cup would be canceled.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://usawaterpolo.org/news/2020/3/16/general-usa-water-polo-announces-the-cancellation-of-multiple-upcoming-events.aspx |date=16 March 2020 |title=USA Water Polo Announces The Cancellation Of Multiple Upcoming Events |publisher=[[USA Water Polo]] |website=usawaterpolo.org |access-date=22 March 2020}}</ref>

===Oceania===
On 16 March 2020, the [[Water Polo Australia]] (WPA) announced that the 2020 [[Australian National Water Polo League]] would be terminated, the 2020 WPA National Championships scheduled to take place in [[Adelaide]], [[South Australia]] in May would be canceled, and the 2020 Open Championships (Country and Masters) scheduled to take place in the [[Gold Coast, Queensland|Gold Coast]], [[Queensland]] in May would be postponed.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.waterpoloaustralia.com.au/news/covid-19-virus-i-changes-to-national-calendar-/ |date=16 March 2020 |title=COVID-19 virus I Changes to National Calendar |publisher=[[Water Polo Australia]] |website=waterpoloaustralia.com.au |access-date=24 March 2020}}</ref>

==Impact on sports venue workers==
The novel coronavirus pandemic has resulted in economic losses for workers who struggled to make a living during these times.  Throughout the COVID-19 pandemic, teams were eager to start playing again, but they needed the support of the workers who provide a comfortable and adequate place for them to play.<ref name=":20">{{Cite web|last=Yousefi|first=Ryan|date=18 March 2020|title=Miami Heat and Marlins Pledge to Take Care of Employees Amid Work Outages|url=https://www.miaminewtimes.com/arts/miami-heat-and-miami-marlins-pledge-to-pay-workers-amid-coronavirus-11600601|access-date=7 December 2020|website=Miami New Times}}</ref> Globally, since the new norm in 2020 is social distancing, the most important step was to figure out how to survive financially, especially for the stadium workers who couldn’t afford the time it takes to stimulate a new bill to address these and provide for these personal issues.<ref name=":20" />

The Miami Heat basketball team has announced that they will be committed to help their stadium workers survive financially by paying them immediately instead of waiting for a check to come in, because the wait would have had a severe financial detrimental effect to each individual worker.<ref name=":20" /> Heat owner Micky Arison has announced that he pledged to donate $1 million to provide for the Miami community because of the immense impact that COVID-19 has had on the financial-compromised community. <ref name=":20" />
